1 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Pace v. State


S99P0647.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 829; 524 S.E.2d 490; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 1030; 2000 Fulton County D. Rep. 601



December 3, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 2, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5369. Reconsideration Denied December 20, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Long.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Fulton Superior Court, Georgia, which convicted him of murder, rape and sodomy.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of four counts of malice murder, four counts of felony murder, four counts of rape, and two counts of aggravated sodomy. The jury recommended a death sentence for each malice murder conviction after finding beyond a reasonable doubt the existence of 19 statutory aggravating circumstances. Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-30 (b) (2), (7). On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that a consent form signed by defendant when he was 28 years old permitted the State to use his blood and hair samples against him in a court of law. The court also held that evidence of all four murders was admissible against him to show identity. Finally, the court held that trial court did not err by failing to disqualify prospective jurors who were allegedly predisposed to a death sentence because a prospective juror could have an opinion leaning for or against a death sentence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; defendant's grounds for appeal were denied. State was permitted to use prior blood and hair samples to convict him, jurors were properly selected notwithstanding claims that jurors were predisposed to the death penalty, and evidence of other charged murders was admissible to show identity.

 

2 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Redfearn v. Huntcliff Homes Ass'n


S99A1121, S99X1124.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 745; 524 S.E.2d 464; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 1002; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 4097



November 23, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Equity. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Bonner.



DISPOSITION: Transferred to the Court of Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant homeowners appealed the judgment of the Fulton Superior Court, Georgia, granting summary judgment awarding plaintiff homeowner's association injunctive relief to remedy the violation of its restrictive covenants.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed that the written agreement regarding construction of a house between the parties permitted construction of a retaining wall, and also claimed the trial court erred in rejecting their defense of laches. The court found that the primary issue was whether the trial court properly construed the contracts at issue, which was an issue of law. Because the primary issue to be resolved was legal and the viability of any equitable claim was ancillary, the appeal was outside the realm of the court's jurisdiction. Any equitable defense asserted in a response seeking equitable relief did not invoke the court's jurisdiction to hear an appeal.


OUTCOME: The appeal was transferred to the Georgia Court of Appeals. The primary issue in the case was legal and because the viability of any equitable claim was ancillary, the appeal was outside the court's jurisdiction.

 

3 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Rouse v. Dep't of Natural Res.


S99A1148.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 726; 524 S.E.2d 455; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 1029; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 4106



November 22, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Protections of Tidewaters Act; constitutional question. Ware Superior Court. Before Judge Altman.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from a ruling of the Ware Superior Court (Georgia), which affirmed administrative law judge's decision against appellant. Appellant then moved for a discretionary review of the constitutionality of the Protections of Tidewaters Act, Ga. Code Ann. §§ 52-1-1 to 52-1-10.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had a houseboat and river house located on the tidal portion of a river, both of which pre-dated the Protection of Tidewaters Act (Act), Ga. Code Ann. §§ 52-1-1 to 52-1-10. Appellee, the Department of Natural Resources, granted a permit for the houseboat to remain on the river until June 30, 1997. However, it did not grant a permit for the river house. Eventually, appellant was ordered to remove both structures. Appellant's attacks on the constitutionality of the Act were without merit. The terms "structure" and "tidewaters" were not unconstitutionally vague. The Act did not impinge on any fundamental right, and it was rationally related to the governmental interest in protecting the tidewaters of the state for the use and enjoyment of the state's citizens. Nor was there an equal protection violation nor an unconstitutional taking of appellant's property.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, since the Protection of Tidewaters Act was constitutional.

 

4 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Krieger v. Walton County Bd. of Comm'Rs


S99A0689.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 791; 524 S.E.2d 461; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 993; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 4109



November 22, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 20, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Walton County local acts; constitutional question. Walton Superior Court. Before Judge Pickett from Augusta Circuit.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, chairperson of county board of commissioners, challenged an order of the Superior Court of Walton County (Georgia) denying a request for declaratory and injunctive relief and upholding certain ordinances enacted by the board in the exercise of county's home rule authority.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sued to have certain county ordinances declared invalid and to enjoin their enforcement. The trial court denied his petition, ruling instead that each of the ordinances constituted a valid exercise of the county's home rule authority under the Georgia Constitution. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the county's ordinance, which tracked the language of Ga. Code Ann. § 36-5-22, vested in the office of county manager certain administrative functions, and did not attempt to confer on that office the executive powers reserved for the chairman, was consistent with the county's home rule authority, and did not violate the Georgia Constitution.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. County ordinance which vested in the office of county manager certain administrative functions, did not attempt to confer on that office the executive powers reserved for the chairman, was consistent with the county's home rule authority, and did not violate the Georgia Constitution.

 

5 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Kolokouris v. State


S99A0725.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 597; 523 S.E.2d 311; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 920; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 3972



November 1, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Reckless conduct; constitutional question. Hall Superior Court. Before Judge Fuller.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a jury verdict of guilty of reckless conduct in the Hall Superior Court (Georgia), challenging the constitutionality of the reckless conduct statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-60 (b), arguing that the inconsistent verdict rule should apply, and that evidence of a victim's gang membership should have been admitted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction of reckless conduct for shooting at two African-American minors at a convenience store. Because defendant did not question the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-60 (b) at the close of the state's evidence, or at the close of all evidence he could not on appeal. The jury's acquittal on aggravated assault charges did not establish that his justification defense was accepted, and that he was acting with intent. Defendant could not argue inconsistency between the aggravated assault and reckless conduct verdicts. The evidence was sufficient to sustain a conviction for reckless conduct. Although the evidence objected to concerned defendant's expression of racial bias some time before the shooting, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the testimony of his former girlfriend in rebuttal to his direct testimony. Evidence of the victim's gang membership was not admissible, and was not relevant.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because defendant's constitutional attack on the statute was not timely, the inconsistent verdict rule did not apply in Georgia, the evidence was sufficient to sustain a conviction for reckless conduct, evidence of the victim's gang membership was not relevant, and evidence of defendant's racial bias showed motive.

 

6 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Wilson v. State


S99P0651.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 811; 525 S.E.2d 339; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 1035; 2000 Fulton County D. Rep. 501



November 1, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 2, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5355. Reconsideration Denied December 20, 1999.
Reconsideration denied by, 12/20/1999
Writ of certiorari denied Wilson v. Georgia, 531 U.S. 838, 121 S. Ct. 99, 148 L. Ed. 2d 58, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5355 (2000)
Companion case at Butts v. State, 273 Ga. 760, 546 S.E.2d 472, 2001 Ga. LEXIS 323 (2001)
Related proceeding at Wilson v. Terry, 131 S. Ct. 799, 178 L. Ed. 2d 534, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 9493 (U.S., 2010)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by Wilson v. Upton, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 2889 (M.D. Ga., Jan. 12, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Baldwin Superior Court. Before Judge Prior.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his jury convictions of malice murder, felony murder, armed robbery, hijacking motor vehicle, possession of firearm during commission of crime, and possession of sawed-off shotgun, and death sentence from Baldwin Superior Court (Georgia).


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the jury's convictions of malice murder and felony murder and other offenses and death sentence finding, inter alia, as follows: that the evidence was sufficient to convict and to deny a directed verdict; that defendant's right of free association was not violated by introducing evidence of his gang participation; that self-exculpatory statements of co-defendant were inadmissible and defendant failed to make proffer of evidence; that juror selection was proper; that it was error for judge not to attend viewing of crime scene but defendant failed to object and there was no harm shown; that jury was properly charged; that a mistrial was properly denied and curative instructions were sufficient respecting inadmissible hearsay suggesting defendant shot someone else; victim's photo in life and crime scene photos were properly admitted; defendant failed to object to prosecutor's statements which would not have changed outcome of case; and sentence was imposed without passion or prejudice.


OUTCOME: Convictions for malice murder and felony murder and other offenses and imposition of death sentence affirmed because evidence was sufficient to convict, evidence was properly admitted, jury was properly charged, and sentence was imposed without passion or prejudice.

 

7 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Brown v. Liberty County


S99A1451.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 634; 522 S.E.2d 466; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 947; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 4117



October 18, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied November 10, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Tax commissioner's compensation; constitutional question. Liberty Superior Court. Before Judge Fryer, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, county tax commissioner sought review of the judgment of the Liberty Superior Court (Georgia), granting partial summary judgment in favor of appellee county in a declaratory judgment action to determine the method and amount of compensation from 1993 to 1998.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-183 was unconstitutionally vague. The court found that, when reasonably construed, Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-183(a) was not vague, as it gave sufficient notice of its coverage to counties and their tax commissioners, and its provisions were not meaningless or contradictory. Subsection (f) contemplated application of the statute to tax commissioners whose compensation included both salary and fees. The statute controlled over the local act upon which appellant relied. Appellant was authorized to be paid not less than the minimum salary mandated by Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-183(b)(1), but she was not entitled to any additional fees under Ga. Code Ann. § 40-2-33 or 48-5-180 as compensation for her service.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed; the statute was not constitutionally vague as it gave sufficient notice of its coverage to counties and tax commissioners; appellant was authorized to be paid not less than the minimum salary mandated but was not entitled to additional fees.

 

8 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Wrzesinski v. State


S99A1159.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 659; 522 S.E.2d 461; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 792; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 3821



October 18, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied November 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. §§ 43-11-17 (a) (6), 43-11-50; constitutional question. Bibb Superior Court. Before Judge Johnson.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Bibb Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of practicing dentistry without a license in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 43-11-50.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was not licensed to practice dentistry. Defendant took impressions of teeth for the purpose of making appliances usable as teeth, which appliances were not ordered by and returned to a licensed dentist. Defendant filed various pre-trial motions that attacked the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. §§ 43-11-17 (a) (6), 43-11-50 which were denied and defendant was convicted of practicing dentistry without a license in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 43-11-50. On appeal defendant contended that Ga. Code Ann. § 43-11-17 (a) (6) violated state constitutional due process, equal protection and anti-monopoly provisions and that Ga. Code Ann. § 43-11-50 was unconstitutional because the legislation which enacted it referred to more than one subject matter. Judgment affirmed because the statute was not an unconstitutional special law and the legislation which enacted Ga. Code Ann. § 43-11-50 was simply comprehensive in the area of regulation of health professions and, therefore, was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed because the statute was not an unconstitutional special law and the legislation which enacted the statute was simply comprehensive in the area of regulation of health professions and, therefore, was not unconstitutional.

 

9 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Johnson v. Griffin


S99A1358.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 663; 522 S.E.2d 657; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 968; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 3805



October 18, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied November 15, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Habeas corpus. Baldwin Superior Court. Before Judge Cline.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state appealed the judgment of the Baldwin Superior Court (Georgia) granting appellee's petition for habeas corpus to set aside his guilty pleas on alleged ineffective assistance of counsel, involuntariness of guilty pleas, and unconstitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. §§ 42-9-40 and 42-9-45.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state contended the trial court erred in granting appellee's petition for writ of habeas corpus. The court found that Ga. Code Ann. § 9-14-42(a) limited the scope of habeas proceedings to claims by state prisoners where there was substantial denial of his rights under the Georgia or United States constitutions. Appellee's claim was not cognizable in habeas corpus proceedings. Appellee's claim arose from the Parole Board's determination that he was no longer eligible for parole. The proper remedy was in a mandamus action against the Board.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed; appellee's claim was not cognizable in a habeas corpus proceeding as his claims arose from the Parole Board's determination that he was no longer eligible for parole.

 

10 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Nash v. State


S98G1663.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 281; 519 S.E.2d 893; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 612; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 2518



July 6, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia - 233 Ga. App. 75, 503 S.E.2d 23.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part, remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a writ of certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia, which had affirmed his conviction for aggravated assault and his sentence as a recidivist based on the entry of a guilty plea in a prior proceeding. Defendant challenged his sentence, claiming that the prior guilty plea used to enhance his sentence was not knowingly and voluntarily entered.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated assault and sentenced as a recidivist. At his sentencing hearing, the state had introduced evidence that defendant had previously pled guilty to a felony. This prior conviction was used to enhance defendant's sentence on the assault conviction. Defendant argued that the state had not met its burden of proving that the guilty plea was knowingly and voluntarily entered because it could not produce a transcript of the prior hearing to demonstrate that the judge conducted a colloquy to determine that the guilty plea was knowing and voluntary. The lower court affirmed the conviction and sentence, and defendant appealed. Although the state had not produced a transcript, it did produce evidence of the trial court's custom and practice of determining that a guilty plea was knowing and voluntary before accepting the plea. The court affirmed, holding that in non-death penalty cases, the burden was on defendant to prove that a prior guilty plea was not knowingly and voluntarily entered. The court expressly overruled its opinion in Pope v. State, 345 S.E.2d 831 (1986), which had required the state to show the prerequisites of a valid waiver.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling below that defendant's prior conviction by a guilty plea was presumed valid, because in non-death penalty cases the prior conviction was entitled to a presumption of regularity subject to defendant's proof to the contrary. However, the court remanded the case for a hearing to give defendant an opportunity to prove that his prior guilty plea was not knowingly and voluntarily entered.

 

11 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Etkind v. Suarez


S98G1978.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 352; 519 S.E.2d 210; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 627; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 2512



July 6, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia - 234 Ga. App. 108, 505 S.E.2d 831. Fulton County State. Trial Judge: Hon. M. Yvette Miller. Date of Judgment Appealed: 09-02-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 09-30-97. Lower Ct # : A98A1318 97VS0126229C.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents challenged an order of the Court of Appeals of Georgia that affirmed a trial court order granting defendant doctors' motion for summary judgment on the pleadings in a wrongful birth case.


OVERVIEW: After their child was born with Down's Syndrome, plaintiff parents brought a wrongful birth suit against defendant doctors claiming that, but for the treatment or advice provided by defendants, plaintiffs would have aborted the fetus and prevented the birth of their child. The trial court granted defendants' motion for judgment on the pleadings. The intermediate court affirmed and held that, unless and until it was authorized by the General Assembly, there was no cause of action for wrongful birth in Georgia. The appellate court also affirmed and held that wrongful birth actions were not recognized in Georgia. The court said that because the General Assembly had not enacted any legislation authorizing a recovery for wrongful birth, plaintiffs had no viable claim. The court said that the principle of stare decisis compelled it to follow and apply judicial precedent despite any disagreement it had with the reasoning behind the precedent.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed an intermediate court order that granted defendant doctors' motion for summary judgment in a wrongful birth action. The court held that absent a clear legislative mandate, it could not recognize a cause of action for wrongful birth.

 

12 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Baker v. City of Marietta


S99A0311. S99X0314.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 210; 518 S.E.2d 879; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 589; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 2226



June 14, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Annexation; constitutional question. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Matthews, from Rome Circuit.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated in part and case remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney general challenged a decision of the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia) that denied injunctive relief sought by county. Appellant contended that the lower court resolved the controversy between the county and appellee city by holding that the county had not properly invoked the statute and thereby lost jurisdiction to enter declaratory judgment that statutes were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee city notified the county that appellee had accepted an application for annexation certain real property. The county commission chairman objected to the proposed annexation but appellee annexed and re-zoned the property without resolving the land use dispute with the county. The county filed a petition seeking declaratory and injunctive relief and the lower court denied the request, instead ruling that portions of Ga. Code Ann. §§ 36-36-11 and 36-70-24(4)(C) were unconstitutional. Appellant attorney general sought to intervene in the declaratory judgment action because appellee had alleged in its defense that the statutes were unconstitutional. Appellant contended that the lower court resolved the actual controversy between the county and appellee by holding the county had not properly invoked the statute and thereby lost jurisdiction to enter the declaratory judgment. The supreme court agreed and held that the lower court should not have ruled on the petition for declaratory judgment after resolving the dispute between appellee and the county. The court remanded the case with direction that the lower court's rulings on the constitutionality of the statutes be vacated.


OUTCOME: The supreme court ordered that the lower court's judgment be vacated in part and case remanded with direction when the court found that the lower court should not have ruled on the petition for declaratory judgment after resolving the dispute between appellee city and the county. The court ordered a remand to the lower court with direction that its rulings on the constitutionality of the statutes be vacated.

 

13 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Smith v. Langford


S99A0438.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 221; 518 S.E.2d 884; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 582; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 2231



June 14, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Senior judges; constitutional question. Stephens Superior Court. Before Judge Woods.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the Stephens Superior Court (Georgia), which appointed appellee judge to preside over appellant's criminal trial after the chief superior court judge recused himself from the case. Appellant asserted it was unconstitutional for a non-elected senior judge to discharge the duties of the elective office of a judge of the superior court.


OVERVIEW: Appellee judge was appointed to preside over appellant's criminal trial after the chief superior court judge recused himself from the case. Appellant filed an information in the nature of quo warranto seeking to prevent appellee from sitting in the case. Appellant argued it was unconstitutional for a non-elected senior judge to discharge the duties of the elective office of a judge of the superior court. The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which refused to restrain appellee from serving and denied appellant's request to find Ga. Code Ann. §§ 15-1-9.2 and 47-8-61 unconstitutional. The court held that Ga. Const. art. VI, § I, para. III clearly contemplated and authorized the service of senior judges in general, and in particular, in the stead of a judge of the superior court. Sections 15-1-9.2 and 47-8-61 were the statutory enactments pursuant to the constitution. Further, the creation of the position of senior judge did not establish a separate judicial forum.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that refused to restrain appellee judge from presiding over appellant's criminal trial after the chief superior court judge recused himself. The judgment also denied appellant's request to find the state statutes, which authorized such appointment, unconstitutional. The court held that the state constitution clearly contemplated and authorized the service of senior judges.

 

14 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Lucious


S99A0099.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 361; 518 S.E.2d 677; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 587; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 2237



June 14, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder, etc. Clayton County Superior. Before Judge Simmons.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 08-26-98. Lower CT # : 96CR001168.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the Clayton County Superior (Georgia), which denied defendant's omnibus motion seeking a declaration that the Criminal Procedure Discovery Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 17-16-1 et seq., was unconstitutional, but granted defendant the unilateral right to discover specific material in preparation for his trial on murder charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted on murder charges. During pretrial proceedings, the state refused to open its file except to the extent mandated by the state and federal constitutions because defendant elected not to participate in the Criminal Procedure Discovery Act (the act), Ga. Code Ann. § 17-16-1 et seq. Although the trial court denied defendant's omnibus motion seeking a declaration that the act was unconstitutional, it granted defendant the unilateral right to discover specific material. The state appealed, and the appellate court affirmed the judgment in part and reversed in part. The court affirmed the constitutionality of the act, finding that the act furthered legitimate state interests by establishing a closely symmetrical discovery scheme. The court reversed the discovery order, holding that because of defendant's election not to participate in the act, he was not entitled to discovery rights which were not guaranteed under state or federal constitutions or otherwise provided for by statute or court rule. The court overruled the unilateral discovery permitted by Eason v. State and it declared Ga. Unif. Super. Ct. R. 30.3 unenforceable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment in part and reversed in part. The court affirmed the denial of defendant's omnibus motion seeking a declaration that the Criminal Procedure Discovery Act was unconstitutional where the act furthered legitimate state interests. The court reversed the order granting defendant unilateral discovery rights where defendant's discovery rights were limited because of his election not to participate in the act.

 

15 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Ashkouti v. City of Suwanee


S99A0334.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 154; 516 S.E.2d 785; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 506; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 2075



June 1, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended July 30, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Zoning; constitutional question. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Winegarden.

Gwinnett County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Richard T. Winegarden. Date of Judgment Appealed: 08-25-98. Notice of Appeal Date: 10-26-98. Lower Ct # : 98A44795.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff land developers sought review of denial of their application for rezoning by defendant zoning commission, from the Gwinnett Superior Court (Georgia), contending that the zoning classification in question was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs land developers sought review of denial of their application for rezoning by defendant zoning commission, contending that the zoning classification in question was unconstitutional. On appeal, judgment was reversed. In support of its ruling, the court held that notice to a zoning authority concerning the constitutionality of an existing zoning classification did not have to meet a high standard of particularity; all that was required was that the zoning authority be given fair notice that a constitutional challenge was being raised. The court further held that plaintiffs' attack on the constitutionality of the zoning classification was sufficient in that it put defendant on notice that plaintiffs were challenging the constitutionality of the existing zoning classification, and it focused defendant's attention upon the factors which might have rendered the classification unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying plaintiffs' zoning application was reversed, as plaintiffs' attack on the constitutionality of the zoning classification was deemed to have been sufficient.

 

16 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Love v. State


S99A0509.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 398; 517 S.E.2d 53; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 514; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 2084



June 1, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 30, 1999. O.C.G.A. § 40-6-391 - (a) (6); constitutional question.


PRIOR HISTORY: Gwinnett State Court. Before Judge Greene.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 09-29-98. Notice of Appeal Date: 10-20-98. Lower Ct # :96D50161.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction of driving with unlawful drugs present in his blood or urine pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(6) (the statute) by the Gwinnett State Court (Georgia) and asserted that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped for a speeding violation. The arresting officer smelled marijuana in appellant's car and obtained tests that revealed the presence of marijuana metabolites in appellant's blood and urine. After being convicted of driving with marijuana in his blood or urine pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(6) (the statute), appellant sought review and asserted the statute was unconstitutional. The court noted the statute did not operate to classify a driver as unlawfully impaired, but criminalized the specific act of driving while there was any amount of marijuana in the driver's blood or urine. In addition, the statute did not apply to drivers who lawfully used marijuana for medical purposes. The court acknowledged the statute bore a rational relationship to the legitimate state purpose of protecting the public, but held that the distinction between legal and illegal users was arbitrarily drawn and the statute was therefore an unconstitutional denial of equal protection. The court reversed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment convicting appellant of driving with unlawful drugs present in his blood or urine after holding that the statutory distinction between legal and illegal users of marijuana was arbitrarily drawn and the statute was therefore an unconstitutional denial of equal protection.

 

17 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Fullwood v. Sivley


S99H0240.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 248; 517 S.E.2d 511; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 516; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 2077



June 1, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 6, 1999.
Reconsideration denied by, 07/06/1999
Writ of habeas corpus granted Fullwood v. State, 2012 Ga. LEXIS 21 (Ga., Jan. 9, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Habeas corpus. Crisp Superior Court. Before Judge Faircloth.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from the Crisp Superior Court (Georgia), which accepted petitioner's guilty plea to a charge of possessing cocaine with intent to distribute and imposed a 10-year first offender probated sentence.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner entered a guilty plea to a charge of possessing cocaine with intent to distribute. The trial court accepted the plea and imposed a 10-year probated sentence. Petitioner attempted to file a pro se habeas corpus petition, challenging his conviction. The habeas court denied filing of the petition on the ground that venue was not proper. The court held that the merits of the habeas court's order denying filing of a petition could not be reached by an appellate court unless it was established that the court had jurisdiction. The habeas court informed petitioner that his right to appeal was governed by Ga. Code Ann. § 9-14-52. The statute provided that as to final orders of the court which were adverse to petitioner, no appeal shall be allowed unless the supreme court of the state issued a certificate of probable cause. The court determined that an order denying filing of a habeas petition pursuant to the statute was a final order which was adverse to petitioner because it had the effect of denying any of the relief sought. The habeas court correctly informed petitioner of the proper procedure for obtaining appellate review. The court dismissed the petition.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed petitioner's appeal of his conviction and sentence following his guilty plea to a charge of possessing cocaine with intent to distribute because the appeal was not authorized as required by the statute.

 

18 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Statesboro Publ'g Co. v. City of Sylvania


S99A0474.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 92; 516 S.E.2d 296; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 421; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 1907; 27 Media L. Rep. 1892



May 17, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Freedom of speech; constitutional question. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Karpf.

Chatham County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Michael L. Karpf. Date of Judgment Appealed: 10-07-98. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-02-98. Lower Ct # : CV961434KA.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Chatham County Superior Court (Georgia) that held appellee's ordinance limiting the way appellant delivered its newspapers was valid and constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant delivered a weekly shopper newspaper without charge to appellee city's residents by throwing the paper in yards or driveways. To deal with the litter caused by unclaimed papers, appellee enacted an ordinance that prohibited distribution of free printed material in yards, driveways, or porches. Appellee city then sought a declaratory judgment and the trial court upheld the ordinance as constitutional. On appeal, the court held that because the ordinance was not narrowly tailored to meet the appellee's interest in preventing litter and failed to provide for meaningful alternatives of communication, the ordinance violated the freedom of speech and press under the United States and Georgia Constitutions. Therefore, the lower court judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court struck down appellee city's ordinance limiting the way appellant delivered its newspapers because the ordinance was too narrowly construed to meet the compelling interest standard as set forth in the U.S. Constitution, therefore, it was declared unconstitutional.

 

19 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Bryant v. State


S99A0482.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 99; 515 S.E.2d 836; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 436; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 1938



May 17, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Daniel, Senior Judge.

Fulton County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. William W. Daniel. Date of Judgment Appealed: 09-24-98. Notice of Appeal Date: 10-15-98. Lower Ct # : Z70576.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of conviction and life sentence imposed by the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) after a jury found defendant guilty of felony murder while in the commission of aggravated assault and theft by taking.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stole a gun and jewelry from a relative, then drove to a friend's home and shot him with a shotgun and stole his car. Although the gun was never recovered, circumstantial evidence admitted at trial indicated that the relative's gun and the gun used to shoot the victim were the same caliber. Defendant maintained that he accidentally shot the victim after both had been drinking, but forensic testimony indicated that the shooting was not accidental. Defendant requested, and received, a jury instruction on voluntary manslaughter. A jury convicted defendant of felony murder while in the commission of both aggravated assault and theft by taking. Defendant appealed claiming evidence of the theft from his relative was inadmissible and that the voluntary manslaughter instruction unconstitutionally shifted the burden of proof to defendant. The court affirmed the conviction because defendant did not object to the admission of the evidence at trial and that it was relevant because it indicated where the murder weapon came from. The court also ruled that the jury instruction mirrored Ga. Code Ann. Ann. § 16-5-2(a) and defendant was estopped from arguing about a requested charge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for and sentence for felony murder because evidence of a prior criminal act was admissible to show how defendant obtained his murder weapon, and because defendant was estopped from arguing that a jury instruction he requested was given in error, especially when it mirrored a statute on that subject.

 

20 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Cobb County Sch. Dist. v. Barker


S99A0248.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 35; 518 S.E.2d 126; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 370; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 1774



May 3, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Former O.C.G.A. § 34-9-200.1 (g) (6); constitutional question. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Kreeger.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part, and case remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district's discretionary application was granted in order to review a decision of the Superior Court of Cobb County (Georgia), which upheld the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 34-9-200.1(g)(6) (amended 1992). The trial court also affirmed the decision of a workers' compensation administrative law judge, which reinstated appellee's temporary total disability benefits after finding her work-related injury was catastrophic.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the part of a trial court's judgment that found Ga. Code Ann. § 34-9-200.1(g)(6) constitutional; but vacated the part of the judgment that affirmed an administrative decision that appellee, a claimant of temporary total disability benefits, suffered a catastrophic injury. The court held that, contrary to appellant school district's contention, § 34-9-200.1(g)(6)'s language did not require a worker's compensation administrative law judge (ALJ) to conclusively presume a finding of catastrophic injury because the claimant had been awarded Social Security disability or SSI benefits. The statute did not, therefore, deprive appellant of its constitutional right to due process, nor did the statute violate appellant's right to equal protection of the laws. However, because the court was unable to state with certainty that the ALJ did not employ a conclusive presumption based on an award of Social Security benefits, it vacated the trial court's affirmance of the ALJ's decision and remanded the case for a clarification of findings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of a judgment finding the relevant subsection of a workers' compensation statute was constitutional because the subsection at most provided a rebuttable presumption that a claimant had suffered a compensable catastrophic injury. The court vacated that part of the judgment affirming an administrative decision that appellee had suffered a catastrophic injury and remanded for clarification of the findings.

 

21 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Jackson


S99A0451.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


271 Ga. 5; 515 S.E.2d 386; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 322; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 1448



April 12, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 16-13-30 (j) (2); constitutional question. Dougherty Superior Court. Before Judge Gray.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state challenged the order of the Dougherty Superior Court (Georgia), which dismissed defendant's indictment for violating Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(j)(1), on the grounds that the statute violated defendant's equal protection rights under the U.S. Constitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with purchasing marijuana in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(j)(1). Under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(j)(2), conviction of this crime would result in felony sentencing even though the amount of marijuana that defendant allegedly purchased was less than one ounce. Under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-2 (b), a conviction of possession, rather than purchase, of this small amount of marijuana would mandate only misdemeanor punishment. Based upon the disparity between the prescribed punishments for possession and purchase of the same amount of marijuana, defendant filed a demurrer asserting the unconstitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(j)(2). The trial court sustained the demurrer and dismissed the indictment. The court reversed and held that defendant was not treated any differently than others charged with the purchase of marijuana. The court ruled that a purchase of drugs involved more than simply possessing the contraband. The court found that the purchase of drugs posed a greater threat to the public health, safety and welfare than merely the private possession of the same controlled substance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the indictment and held that defendant was treated no differently than all other purchasers of marijuana. Moreover, the court found that the crime of purchasing marijuana was different than the possession of the same drug because the purchase of marijuana posed a greater threat to the public health, safety and welfare than merely the private possession of the same controlled substance.

Pruitt v. State


S98P1962.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 745; 514 S.E.2d 639; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 311; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 1136



March 19, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 1, 1999. Certiorari Denied November 15, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7568.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Lumpkin County Superior Court. Trial Judge: Hon. Hugh W. Stone. Date of Judgment Appealed: 02-11-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 04-07-97. Lower Ct # : 95CR181HS.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Lumpkin County Superior Court (Georgia) after it convicted him of malice murder, felony murder, kidnapping with bodily injury, rape, aggravated sodomy, aggravated child molestation, aggravated assault, aggravated battery, child molestation, and cruelty to children. The defendant was sentenced to death after the jury found aggravating circumstances.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of malice murder, felony murder, kidnapping with bodily injury, rape, aggravated sodomy, aggravated child molestation, aggravated assault, aggravated battery, child molestation, and cruelty to children. The lower court found aggravating circumstances and sentenced defendant to death. The lower court judgment was affirmed. The evidence was sufficient to enable a rational trier of fact to find defendant guilty of the crimes charged beyond a reasonable doubt. The evidence was also sufficient to enable the jury to find the existence of aggravating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court also rejected defendant's other claimed errors. Because the death sentence was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or other arbitrary factor and was not disproportionate to the penalty imposed in similar cases, the sentence was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court that sentenced defendant to death and convicted defendant of malice murder, felony murder, kidnapping with bodily injury, rape, aggravated sodomy, aggravated child molestation, aggravated assault, aggravated battery, child molestation, and cruelty to children was affirmed. The court was not persuaded by defendant's numerous assignments of error and found that the lower court did not err.

 

23 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Jackson County Bd. of Health v. Fugett Constr.


S98A1837., S98X1838.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 667; 514 S.E.2d 28; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 304; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 1043



March 15, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 31-2-7; constitutional question. Jackson Superior Court. Before Judge McWhorter.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Cross-appeals were taken from a decision of the Jackson Superior Court (Georgia), finding petitioner septic tank manufacturer failed to establish that it had statewide approval for all but one of petitioner's systems. The court then found Ga. Code Ann. § 31-2-7 unconstitutional in that it deprived petitioner of continuing statewide approval for its one system.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed an action in mandamus seeking approval to install one of petitioner's septic tank systems. The trial court entered judgment finding that petitioner failed to prove that it had gotten statewide approval for several of its systems. The trial court did find that petitioner had received prior approval for one of its system and that the amendments to Ga. Code Ann. § 31-2-7 unconstitutionally deprived petitioner of ongoing approval. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. In affirming the judgment for respondent, the court held that petitioner failed to prove that it had received approval for its systems and that the trial court did not err by sustaining the best evidence rule objection. The best evidence rule was properly invoked because the witness referred to a document and petitioner sought production of the contents of the document. In reversing the ruling of unconstitutionality, the court held that petitioner did not have a vested right to approval because county regulations could be enacted that would prevent petitioner from installing its systems.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying petitioner the right to install its systems without the requirements ordered by respondent because petitioner failed to show that it had statewide approval for its systems. The court reversed the finding of unconstitutionality because petitioner did not have a vested right to approval and because subsequent amendment of the statute regarding statewide approval was constitutional.

 

24 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Luke v. Ga. Dep't of Natural Res.


S98A1447.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 647; 513 S.E.2d 728; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 300; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 1042



March 15, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Underground Storage Tank Trust Fund; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Shoob.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, owner of an underground storage tank, challenged a decision from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) dismissing his action that questioned the constitutionality of a fee imposed under Ga. Code Ann. § 12-13-10 for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted.


OVERVIEW: Appellant owned an underground storage tank. Appellant contended that a fund participation fee paid by owners of such tanks under the Underground Storage Tank Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 12-13-1 et seq., violated the requirement of Ga. Const. art. III, § 9, par. 6(b) that motor fuel tax revenues be used for activities relating to public roads. The court found that the participation fee did not violate § 9 because it did not constitute a tax. The fee was voluntary and was assessed only when owners opted to participate in the underground storage tank trust fund. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. Appellant had the option of paying the fee and participating in the fund or fulfilling his statutory obligation of showing financial responsibility in other ways. Because appellant was not obligated to pay the fee, the fee was not a motor fuel tax subject to § 9.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision dismissing appellant's constitutional challenge to the participation fee because the fee was not a motor fuel tax subject to state constitutional restrictions. Payment of the participation fee was voluntary and owners of underground storage tanks, like appellant, could opt out of participation in the fund.

Nat'l Health Network, Inc. v. Fulton County


S98G0155., S98G0408.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 724; 514 S.E.2d 422; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 305; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 1051



March 15, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied April 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Fulton County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Joel J. Fryer. Date of Judgment Appealed: 11-13-96. Notice of Appeal Date: 12-09-96. Lower Ct # : A97A1163 E43295.

DeKalb County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Daniel M. Coursey, Jr. Date of Judgment Appealed: 12-30-96. Notice of Appeal Date: 01-27-97. Lower Ct # : A97A1330 9544057.

Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia - 228 Ga. App. 584.

Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia - 229 Ga. App. 185.
Brian Realty Corp. v. DeKalb County, 229 Ga. App. 185, 493 S.E.2d 595, 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 1382 (1997)
National Health Network, Inc. v. Fulton County, 228 Ga. App. 584, 492 S.E.2d 333, 1997 Ga. App. LEXIS 1207 (1997)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. S98G0155 and reversed in Case No. S98G0408.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant and appellee property owners in consolidated cases both filed an action seeking a property tax refund under Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-380. The court granted certiorari to the Court of Appeals (Georgia), which affirmed the grant of summary judgment to appellee county in one case and reversed as to appellant county in the other, to determine whether the tax refund statute was properly construed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and appellee property owners in consolidated cases both filed an action seeking a property tax refund under Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-380. In one case appellee challenged the tax assessor's failure to consider conditions attached to the property's zoning in assessing value and in the other case appellant challenged the county's failure to consider the property's existing use. The issue on appeal was whether either property owner had raised a claim of an erroneous or illegal assessment under the tax refund statute. Because appellant and appellee property owners had not established that the counties assessed or collected an erroneous or illegal tax, the court concluded that they were not entitled to a refund under Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-380. Because the Court of Appeals correctly held that appellant did not meet the criteria for bringing a refund action, the judgment was affirmed. The judgment in the second case was reversed because appellee did not present a claim for an erroneous or illegal assessment under the state refund statute.


OUTCOME: The court found that, because appellant property owner in one case did not meet the criteria for bringing a refund action, the judgment for appellee county was affirmed. The judgment in the second case was reversed because appellee property owner also did not present a claim for an erroneous assessment under the state refund statute.

Miller v. Walker


S98A1664.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 811; 514 S.E.2d 22; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 261; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 933



March 8, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied April 2, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: Trust. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Bonner. Date of Judgment Appealed: 05-07-98. Notice of Appeal Date: 05-28-98. Lower Ct # : E53909.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A guardian ad litem for potential beneficiaries of a trust appealed the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) finding that certain adopted children no longer held interests in the trust.


OVERVIEW: The case involved the question of whether certain minor children remained beneficiaries of a trust created by their natural grandfather despite the children's adoptions by unrelated persons. The superior court granted the guardian ad litem's motion for summary judgment, citing Ga. Code Ann. § 19-8-19. The court noted that in construing the settlor's intent with regard to the rights of an adopted child to take under the trust instrument, it was not a question of the right or equity of the adopted child to a share but simply a question of the settlor's intent with respect to those who were to benefit. The ruling that the children were no longer beneficiaries of the trust was affirmed because the settlor chose not to name his then living grandchildren as beneficiaries but instead to benefit a class designated as descendants. Thus, it could be concluded that the settlor did not intend the descendants, as beneficiaries of both the present and remainder interests in the trust, to include children adopted out of the settlor's family.


OUTCOME: The court's finding that the children were no longer beneficiaries of the trust was affirmed because the settlor did not intend to include children adopted out of the settlor's family.

Speed v. State


S98P1359.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 688; 512 S.E.2d 896; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 173; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 863



March 1, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reconsideration Denied March 19, 1999. Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5563.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Fulton Superior Court. Before Trial Judge Hon. Isaac Jenrette. Date of Judgment Appealed: 03-24-98. Notice of Appeal Date: 04-20-98. Lower Ct # : Z41174.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), entering his conviction for malice murder and a sentence of death. Defendant claimed the trial court erred in holding an in-camera conversation with a prospective juror and in limiting defense psychologist's testimony. Where defendant killed a police officer during a frisk, defendant claimed the trial court erred in failing to give an instruction regarding warrantless arrests.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's murder conviction and death sentence were affirmed where defendant waived the issue of the trial court's questioning of a prospective juror and jury instructions, and the defense psychologist's testimony was not improperly limited. Defendant, a known drug dealer, approached an officer who was frisking individuals. Defendant killed the officer point-blank in the head. Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed, claiming, inter alia, that the trial court improperly questioned a prospective juror during voir dire in-camera, his psychologist's testimony was improperly limited, and he was denied an instruction listing the circumstances under which an officer may make a warrantless arrest. The reviewing court affirmed, holding where defendant agreed to the juror's questioning, no error occurred. The defense psychologist's testimony was not improperly limited where he was allowed to give the basis of his opinion, but restrained from testifying to hearsay. Where the trial court gave the recommended charge in the pattern jury instructions, and defendant failed to reargue his request to give an additional charge, the issue was waived.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court affirmed the trial court's judgment entering defendant's murder conviction and death sentence. Where defendant agreed to the trial court's juror questioning, no error occurred. Where defendant failed to reargue a juror instruction, the issue was waived. Where the defense psychologist was allowed to give the basis of his opinion, and merely restrained from giving hearsay testimony, the testimony was properly limited.

Dekalb County v. State


S98A1338.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 776; 512 S.E.2d 284; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 161; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 741



February 22, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reconsideration Denied April 2, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 48-8-67; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Wendy Lee Shoob.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 05-13-98. Notice of Appeal Date: 05-14-98. Lower Ct # : E67520.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant counties sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which granted appellee State's motion to dismiss appellants' injunctive, mandamus, and accounting claims and held that Ga. Code Ann. § 48-8-67 was constitutional because it did not breach an implied contract between the parties and lacked a retroactive application that altered appellants' vested rights under Ga. Code Ann. § 48-8-100 et. seq.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that Ga. Code Ann. § 48-6-67 was constitutional, finding that the statute was neither an retrospective application law or a breach of an implied contract between appellant counties and appellee State. The court found that the statute did not take away or impair any existing rights to receive proceeds; rather, the court found that Ga. Code Ann. § 48-8-67 removed the Commissioner of Revenue's discretion in dealing with unidentifiable tax proceeds by providing a disbursement scheme to distribute those amounts. The court noted that the statute was procedural in nature and did not impair appellants' substantive rights. However, the court then found that summary dismissal of appellant county's claim remaining claims for injunction, mandamus, and accounting was inappropriate and remanded for further consideration. The court noted that dismissal for failure to state a cause of action was improper where appellant county had raised material allegations on the issue of accounting which called into question whether the Commissioner of Revenue made "reasonable efforts" to identify the proceeds and fulfilled his obligation under the law.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the constitutionality of the challenged statute that provided a disbursement scheme for unidentifiable tax proceeds because the procedural statute did not impair appellant counties' substantial rights; dismissal of accounting claim reversed and remanded where material allegations questioned whether the revenue commissioner fulfilled his obligation under the law and made "reasonable efforts" to identify the proceeds.

 

29 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Boyer


S98A1851.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 701; 512 S.E.2d 605; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 171; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 757



February 22, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reconsideration Denied March 19, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 16-5-60 (b); constitutional question. Lowndes County State Court. Before Judge Kelly D. Turner.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 05-11-98. Notice of Appeal Date: 06-05-98. Lower Ct # : 98SC11030, 98SC11031.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order from the trial court (Georgia), which sustained defendant's demurrer, finding the reckless conduct statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-60(b) unconstitutional in an action charging defendant with one count of reckless conduct and one count of simple battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was an employee of a child day care center. While supervising a room of 12-month old children, defendant roughly handled a child, including forcefully pushing the child down on a mat by the back of the child's head. Defendant was charged with one count of reckless conduct and one count of simple battery. Defendant filed a demurrer, which the trial court sustained, finding the reckless conduct statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-60(b), unconstitutional. The trial court also found that the simple battery charge was duplicitous of the reckless conduct charge. The state appealed the demurrer. The court found that § 16-5-60(b) was not unconstitutionally vague because defendant had ample notice that the conduct of which she was accused was prohibited. In addition, the court found that duplicity had not occurred because Ga. Code Ann. § 16-1-17(a)(2) specifically allowed defendant to be prosecuted on two separate counts for the same transaction. Defendant's alleged conduct fit the definition of more than one crime, and the state could have charged her with any and all crimes that arose from that behavior and did not have to choose to charge defendant with only a single crime.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order sustaining defendant's demurrer because statutory law was not unconstitutional and because statutory law allowed defendant to be prosecuted on two separate counts for the same transaction and the state could have charged her with any and all crimes that arose from her alleged conduct.

 

30 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Jackson v. State


S98A1930.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 494; 512 S.E.2d 241; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 108; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 556



February 8, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Glynn Superior Court. Before Judge Taylor.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 06-15-98. Notice of Appeal Date: 06-16-98. Lower Ct # :9400088.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Glynn Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of two counts of malice murder, two counts of burglary, one count of terroristic threats, and imposed a life sentence without parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant threatened to kill his wife and her lover after finding out about their extramarital affair. On one morning, defendant entered the house of his wife's lover and stabbed both his wife and her lover to death with a knife that defendant had taken from the kitchen of the house. Defendant was convicted of two counts of malice murder and burglary and one count of terroristic threats and was sentenced to life without parole. On appeal, the court affirmed his convictions and sentence. The appellate court concluded that it was irrelevant that defendant had not carried a weapon to the house because malice aforethought could be formed instantly and did not require premeditation. Moreover, the facts authorized the jury to conclude that defendant had intended to commit an aggravated assault when he entered the house, so the burglary convictions were valid even though the potential victim or victims of the aggravated assault had not been determined. Furthermore, defendant failed to present evidence that young adults had been consistently underrepresented in the jury pools, so whether or not they were a cognizable group for purposes of challenging the venire was irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions on two counts of malice murder and burglary and on one count of terroristic threats and his life sentence without parole. The appellate court concluded that defendant's lack of a weapon when he entered the victim's house did not prevent defendant from having the malice necessary to commit murder or the intent to commit an aggravated assault necessary to his burglary conviction.

D'Auria v. State


S98A2002.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 499; 512 S.E.2d 266; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 103; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 565



February 8, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 16-6-22.1; constitutional question. DeKalb State Court. Before Judge Smith.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 06-20-95. Notice of Appeal Date: 12-24-97. Lower Ct # :93C105641.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the denial by the DeKalb State Court (Georgia) of his plea in bar based on the statute of limitation and his demurrer based on the alleged unconstitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-22.1.


OVERVIEW: Appellant physician treated the alleged victim for injuries she received in an automobile accident. In the course of his treatment, the victim voluntarily submitted herself to at least minimal physical contact by appellant. Appellant was later charged with sexual battery pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-22.1, the accusation against him alleging only that he committed that offense on a certain date by making contact with the intimate body parts of the victim in violation of the statute. The trial court denied his plea in bar based on the statute of limitation and his demurrer based on the alleged unconstitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-22.1. The reviewing court reversed, holding the accusation in the indictment invalid because it did not apprise him of what he allegedly did to violate the law. Specifically, the indictment did not identify which body parts he allegedly touched without the victim's consent, did not identify the manner in which the touching allegedly occurred, and did not recite all the elements of the crime. Because no other indictment was filed within the limitations period, appellant's plea in bar based on the statute of limitations was wrongfully denied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of appellant's plea in bar based on the statute of limitation, holding that the accusation of sexual battery against him in the indictment was invalid because it failed to identify which body parts were allegedly touched without the victim's consent, to identify the manner in which the illegal touching allegedly occurred, or to delineate all of the elements of the crime with which he was charged.
