Marion v. Floyd County Bd. of Equalization


S98A1349.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 475; 511 S.E.2d 512; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 97; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 542



February 8, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 48-5-11; constitutional question. Floyd Superior Court. Before Judge Salmon.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 04-13-98. Notice of Appeal Date: 05-06-98. Lower Ct # :95CV38241.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Floyd Superior Court (Georgia) that granted appellee, the Floyd County Board of Equalization, summary judgment in appellant's suit challenging appellee Floyd County Board of Tax Assessors' tax assessment against appellant's boat, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. §§ 48-5-11 and 48-5-16.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a judgment that granted appellee summary judgment in appellant's suit challenging a tax assessment against appellant's boat made pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. §§ 48-5-11 and 48-5-16. The court reversed the judgment that granted appellee summary judgment and thereby sustained the tax assessment. The court ruled that § 48-5-16, which provided a means of determining in which of two Georgia counties a boat was taxable, did not apply as there was no contention that the boat was located in a Georgia county other than the county of appellant's residence. The court then considered appellant's claim that § 48-5-11 was unconstitutional as applied to him because the sovereign power of a state did not extend beyond its borders to permit taxation of his boat, which was located in Alabama for certain period of the taxable year. After ruling that § 48-5-11 did not, on its face, violate due process guarantees, the court ruled that appellee was improperly granted summary judgment because the record was insufficient to make a determination of whether appellant's boat acquired a tax situs in Alabama, thereby rendering that statute unconstitutional as applied to appellant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment that granted appellee summary judgment in appellant's suit challenging a tax assessment against appellant's boat because the statute relied upon in assessing the tax was inapplicable as appellant's boat was not in a Georgia county other than appellant's county of residence. Because the record was insufficient to determine whether an Alabama tax situs had been established by appellant, summary judgment was improper.

 

33 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Rainey v. Chever


S98A1518.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 519; 510 S.E.2d 823; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 58; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 366



January 19, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration Denied February 19, 1999. Certiorari Denied June 24, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 4558.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 53-2-4 (b) (2); constitutional question. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Jackson.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 05-08-98. Notice of Appeal Date: 05-14-98. Lower Ct # :97A80283.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from the order of the Gwinnett County (Georgia) Superior Court, which granted summary judgment to defendant father in plaintiff mother's action seeking to sever defendant's inheritance rights for his out-of-wedlock child under Ga. Code Ann. § 53-2-4(b)(2) after he found that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After her son died, plaintiff mother sued defendant father, who had fathered the child out of wedlock, seeking to sever defendant's inheritance rights pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 53-2-4(b)(2), which precluded the father of an out-of-wedlock child from inheriting from the child if he failed to treat the child as his own or failed to support the child. Plaintiff and defendant both filed summary judgment motions. The trial court granted defendant's summary judgment motion, finding that Ga. Code Ann. § 53-2-4(b)(2) was unconstitutional. The court affirmed. Under Ga. Code Ann. § 53-2-4(a), the mother of an out-of-wedlock child was permitted to inherit from the child without any preconditions. Therefore, by its plain language, Ga. Code Ann. § 53-2-4(b)(2) created a gender-based classification in that only fathers were required to meet certain requirements in order to inherit from a child born out of wedlock. The court rejected the argument that the statute advanced the state's interest in encouraging fathers to take responsibility for their out-of-wedlock children. The state had an equally important interest in encouraging the identical behavior in mothers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment for defendant on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional. The statute created a gender-based classification because only fathers were required to meet certain requirements in order to inherit from an out-of-wedlock child, and the classification was not justified by any legitimate state interest.

 

34 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Barnett v. State


S98A1768.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 472; 510 S.E.2d 527; 1999 Ga. LEXIS 1; 99 Fulton County D. Rep. 250



January 11, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied February 8, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 40-6-391 (k); constitutional question. Cherokee State Court. Before Judge Gober. Date of Judgment Appealed: 04-20-98. Notice of Appeal Date: 04-20-98. Lower Ct # :97T8580 97M2052.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Cherokee State Court (Georgia), which convicted him of driving under the influence of alcohol with a blood alcohol concentration of 0.02 grams in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(k) and denied his motion to declare section 40-6-391(k) unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 17 years old when he was arrested, charged, and convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol with a blood alcohol concentration of 0.02 grams pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(k). Defendant filed a motion declaring that section 40-6-391(k) was unconstitutional, but the trial court denied said motion. Defendant then appealed claiming that section 40-6-391(k) violated his equal protection rights under the state and federal constitutions by setting forth a blood alcohol concentration standard different for persons under age 21 than for persons above age 21 where there exists a statutory presumption that persons with a blood alcohol concentration of 0.05 grams or less are deemed not to be under the influence of alcohol. The court held that section 40-6-391(k) did not violate defendant's equal protection rights under the state or federal constitutions because the general assembly had a rational basis for enacting said statute. In addition, the court found that section 40-6-391(k) bore a reasonable relationship to both legitimate state purposes of protecting the public safety and safeguarding the physical well being of children.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying defendant's motion to declare statute unconstitutional because the general assembly had a rational basis for enacting the statute and the statute did not violate defendant's equal protection rights under the state or federal constitutions.

 

35 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Powell v. State


S98A0755.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 327; 510 S.E.2d 18; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 1148; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 4177



November 23, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied December 17, 1998. As Amended December 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 16-6-2 (a); constitutional question. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Bishop. Date of Judgment Appealed: 10-10-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-06-97. Lower Ct #: 96B34486.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for the crime of sodomy, which was entered by the Gwinnett County Superior Court (Georgia), on the basis of an unconstitutional intrusion on the right of privacy guaranteed him by the Georgia Constitution and on the sua sponte jury instruction allowing consideration of a lesser included offense.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was tried for the crimes of rape and aggravated sodomy after having sexual relations with his wife's 17 year old niece. The niece testified at trial that the two had engaged in sexual intercourse and oral sex against her will. The defendant testified that such acts did happen, but they were consensual. The jury believed the acts were consensual and acquitted him of the rape and aggravated sodomy. The trial court gave sua sponte jury instruction allowing the jury to consider a lesser included offense of sodomy, which did not hinge upon consent for a finding of guilty. The jury then convicted him of sodomy and he appealed. He claimed that the trial court erred in the sua sponte instruction and that the sodomy statute was unconstitutional. The court determined that the trial court could properly give the lesser included offense instruction. The court reversed his conviction, however, after finding the statute unconstitutional as violating his right to privacy. The court held that the Georgia Constitution provided protection for sexual acts that occurred without force in a private home between persons legally capable of consenting to the acts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction after determining that the Georgia Constitution protected unforced, private, adult sexual activity from governmental interference, and that, therefore, the statute was unconstitutional. The court did find the trial court's sua sponte jury instruction to be proper.

 

36 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Brent v. State


S98A1306.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 160; 510 S.E.2d 14; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 1137; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 3865



November 16, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Roadblock stops; constitutional question. Rockdale Superior Court. Before Judge Todd.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 04-17-98. Notice of Appeal Date: 04-17-98. Lower Ct # :97SR3058.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court for Rockdale County (Georgia), which convicted defendant of driving while intoxicated, less safe to drive, Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested at a roadblock traffic stop when a police officer detected the odor of alcohol while checking defendant's driver's license and proof of insurance. The officer had defendant pull over and requested consent to field sobriety tests. Defendant tested positive for alcohol on an alco-sensor and failed all six parts of a horizontal gaze nystagmus test. Defendant was convicted after a bench trial. On appeal, defendant contended that the use of the roadblock that led to his arrest violated Ga. Const. art. I § I para. XIII. The court held that: (1) the evidence was sufficient to enable a rational trier of fact to find defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt; (2) it was not incumbent upon the state to prove that defendant committed an unsafe act while he was behind the wheel; (3) the detention and subsequent arrest of defendant was constitutional because it satisfied constitutional criteria that balanced citizens' rights to be free from governmental interference and the countervailing right to effective law enforcement; and (4) the admission of the police officer's opinion testimony was a proper exercise of the trial court's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction against defendant for driving while intoxicated.

 

37 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Collins v. Lombard Corp.


S98G0548. S98G0553.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 120; 508 S.E.2d 653; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 1059; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 3780



November 9, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied March 29, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2214.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia - 229 Ga. App. 654.

DeKalb County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Gail C. Flake. Date of Judgment Appealed: 05-20-96. Notice of Appeal Date: 06-05-96. Lower Ct # :A97A0150, 95101144.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state and county tax commissioners, sought review of a decision by the Court of Appeals of Georgia, which reversed, as moot, the trial court's dismissal of an action by plaintiff company to declare that the intangible property tax statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 48-6-20 et seq., unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The company was assessed a tax under the intangible property tax statute, § 48-6-20 et seq. The company brought an action to declare the statute unconstitutional. While the action was pending, the legislature repealed the statute, and a third party paid the tax. The trial court dismissed the action as moot. The appellate court reversed, creating a public policy exception to the mootness doctrine. Upon appeal, the court reversed, holding that the creation of ad hoc exceptions for individual cases was unnecessary and undesirable in that they fostered uncertainty in the law and inappropriately served to expand the jurisdiction of a court applying such exceptions. The court found that the appellate court erred in creating the public policy exception to the mootness doctrine on which it based its decision. The court found that the company's liability for a specific tax assessment ceased to be a live controversy when the tax was paid. The court held that the underlying issue of the constitutionality of the statute could be raised in an action for a refund, an action not susceptible of the third-party involvement in this case. Therefore, the court found that the matter was moot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the holding that the matter was not moot.

Smith v. State


S98P0790.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 240; 510 S.E.2d 1; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 1057; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 3788



November 9, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended December 9, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Benefield.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 12-22-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 01-20-98. Lower Ct # :95CR013696.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Clayton County (Georgia), which convicted defendant of malice murder, theft by receiving stolen property, and possession of a firearm during the commission of a felony, and imposed a death sentence, a concurrent 10-year sentence, and a consecutive 5-year sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant purchased a stolen sawed-off shotgun from an acquaintance. He owned a second shotgun. Defendant got into an argument with the victim; that night the victim was killed after defendant and the victim went into a wooded area. Defendant was indicted for malice murder, theft by receiving, possession of a firearm, and other counts. The court held that: (1) evidence of two incidents that involved defendant and the victim were relevant and should have been admitted because notice under Ga. Unif. Super. Ct. R. 31.6 was not required; (2) the trial court was erroneous in its ruling that defendant could not impeach a witness with that witness' written police statements until the statements had been admitted into evidence; (3) the trial court abused its discretion because it did not permit defendant to ask a witness whether the witness was a racist; (4) defendant was entitled to rebut an allegation that defendant had used a racial slur by showing that he was not a racist; and (5) the prosecutor argued improperly in the sentencing phase closing argument because the prosecutor sought to diminish the jury's sense of responsibility in a misleading fashion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions for murder and for possession of a firearm, and affirmed the conviction for theft by receiving stolen property.

State v. Cafe Erotica


S98A1218.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 97; 507 S.E.2d 732; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 1043; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 3675; 27 Media L. Rep. 1221



November 2, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 32-6-75 (b) ; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Bonner.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 01-23-98. Notice of Appeal Date: 02-20-98. Lower Ct # :E49696.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged a decision of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which struck down as violative of the right to free speech under the federal and state constitutions an amendment to the Outdoor Advertising Control Act of 1971, Ga. Code Ann. § 32-6-70 et seq., which prohibited any off-premises outdoor advertising of commercial establishments where nudity was exhibited.


OVERVIEW: Appellee business was an establishment that provided food services and offered adult entertainment. It brought an action to enjoin enforcement of Ga. Code Ann. § 32-6-75(b), which prohibited any off-premises outdoor advertising of commercial establishments where nudity was exhibited. The business also sought a declaration that the legislation unconstitutionally limited free speech in violation of the First Amendment and Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. V. The trial court entered a temporary restraining order enjoining enforcement of the legislation for a period of 30 days to maintain the status quo. The business sought a permanent injunction, and the trial court permanently enjoined the statute's enforcement because it impermissibly infringed upon the right of free speech. The state appealed, and the court affirmed, concluding that § 32-6-75(b) was not narrowly tailored to achieve its purpose in that it banned even a worded sign advertising the location of a business when it said "any outdoor advertising of a commercial establishment where nudity is exhibited." The court held that traffic safety could have been served as well by a more limited restriction on commercial speech.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment striking down a statute that prohibited any off-premises outdoor advertising of commercial establishments where nudity was exhibited as being violative of the right to free speech under the federal and state constitutions.

Cotton, Inc. v. Phil-Dan Trucking


S98A1084.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 95; 507 S.E.2d 730; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 1042; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 3679



November 2, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Equity. Henry Superior Court. Before Judge Smith.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 10-10-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 10-13-97. Lower Ct # :97CV2067S.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporations appealed a decision of the Henry Superior Court (Georgia) that entered a preliminary injunction prohibiting defendants from transferring their real and personal property, in connection with plaintiff trucking company's suit against defendants alleging violations of the state and federal civil Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act.


OVERVIEW: The lower court entered a preliminary injunction prohibiting defendant corporations from transferring their real and personal property unless a transfer was necessary for ordinary personal and business expenses, in connection with plaintiff trucking company's suit against defendants alleging violations of the state and federal civil Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act (RICO). Defendants appealed, arguing the lower court abused its discretion in granting equitable relief in the form of a preliminary injunction because plaintiff had an adequate remedy at law in the form of money damages for breach of contract. Upon review, the court affirmed. It noted that the trial court did not issue the preliminary injunction pursuant to its inherent equitable power; rather, the preliminary injunction was issued in accordance with the statutory authorization set forth in Ga. Code Ann. § 16-14-6. Accordingly, the injunction was properly issued.


OUTCOME: The order granting plaintiff trucking company a preliminary injunction prohibiting defendant corporations from transferring real and personal property was affirmed because the lower court was authorized to do so under the statute applicable to claims brought under the Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act.

 

41 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Johnson


S98A0595.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 111; 507 S.E.2d 443; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 991; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 3479



October 19, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration Denied November 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 40-6-275; constitutional question. Coweta State Court. Before Judge Thornton.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 11-19-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 12-11-97. Lower Ct # :97TR916 97TR9168 97TR9169 97TR9170.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged a judgment of the Coweta State Court (Georgia), which quashed the accusation charging defendant with three counts of vehicular homicide in the second degree under Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-393(b) after holding that Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-275, pertaining to removal of cars involved in traffic accidents from the road, was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant collided with another vehicle, stopped his tractor-trailer in the middle of the highway lane, and placed warning devices behind his vehicle. A truck ran into the back of the tractor-trailer, killing all three occupants, and defendant was charged with three counts of vehicular homicide in the second degree pursuant to § 40-6-393, predicated on an alleged violation of § 40-6-275. The trial court found § 40-6-275 unconstitutionally vague and granted appellee's motion to quash the accusation. The court held that the statute was unconstitutionally vague because the term "extensive property damage" was so indefinite that a person of reasonable understanding could not know whether the law was violated. The statute required a driver involved in a traffic accident on a multilane highway to move his vehicle out of harm's way unless the accident included personal injury, death, or extensive property damage. If no vehicle incurred extensive property damage the driver must remove his vehicle from the roadway to minimize the chance of further accidents. This created a dilemma because the term "extensive property damage" could mean different things to different people.


OUTCOME: The judgment which quashed the accusation against defendant was affirmed.

OVERVIEW: After appellee city council denied appellant retailer's application for a permit to build a new store in the city, appellant brought suit, seeking writs of certiorari and mandamus. Womack v. State


S98A0810.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


270 Ga. 56; 507 S.E.2d 425; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 801; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 3565



September 14, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration denied October 26, 1998. As Amended October 26, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Equity. Tift Superior Court. Before Judge Crosby.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 11-25-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-26-97. Lower Ct # :97CV438.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State filed an action against defendants, corporation and president, to prohibit them from selling unregistered securities and for the appointment of a receiver for the corporation. The Tift Superior Court (Georgia) permanently enjoined the corporation and president from selling promissory notes of the corporation and appointed a receiver to liquidate its assets. The corporation and president challenged the decision.


OVERVIEW: The corporation and president maintained that they were exempt from registering the promissory notes as securities under Ga. Code Ann. § 10-5-8(9) and that Ga. Code Ann. § 10-5-21, which conferred immunity on the Commissioner of Securities, was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the decision and held that the promissory notes represented investments in a common scheme, not commercial transactions, and therefore were not entitled to exemption. Although most of the notes matured in less than nine months as required by the statute for exemption, the court strictly construed the statute in favor of investors and determined that the character of the indebtedness disqualified the notes from exemption. Section 10-5-21 was found to be constitutional because it was the prerogative of the legislature to confer immunity from suit on the state. Thus, the statute did not unconstitutionally deny equal access to the courts through counterclaim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of a permanent injunction against the corporation and president and the appointment of a receiver.

 

45 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Harry v. Glynn County


S98A0374.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 503; 501 S.E.2d 196; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 569; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 1852



June 1, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Sovereign immunity; constitutional question. Glynn Superior Court. Before Judge Scoggin, Senior Judge.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 08-22-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 09-15-97. Lower Ct # :9600830.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action of plaintiff husband against defendants, Glynn County (County) and its employee, for damages arising from the death of the husband's wife, the Glynn Superior Court (Georgia) entered a judgment granting the County and its employee's motion for summary judgment on their immunity defenses.


OVERVIEW: When the wife collapsed, the employee (a paramedic) unsuccessfully treated her and transported her to a hospital. After her death, the husband contended that the employee had failed to provide the proper treatment to his wife, causing her death, and that the County was liable as his employer. The supreme court concluded that the County was afforded immunity from the action because Ga. Const. art. I, § II, par. IX was not ineffectual or invalid merely because it conflicted with an earlier constitutional provision. Also, its immunity was not waived by the purchase of insurance covering the negligence of employees arising from the use of a motor vehicle because the alleged negligence was the employee's misdiagnosis and choice of treatment, and the ambulance and its use did not play any part in his diagnosis or choice of treatment. The employee was protected by official immunity because he was in the conduct of his official duties and was engaged in discretionary actions, and there was no allegation of malice or intent to injure the wife. His actions were clearly discretionary because he exercised personal deliberation and judgment and acted on them in a way not specifically directed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Cafe Erotica


S98A0396.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant club challenged the judgment from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which granted a permanent injunction against the enforcement of Ga. N. Fulton Med. Ctr. v. Stephenson


S98A0484. S98X0486.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 540; 501 S.E.2d 798; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 562; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 1772



May 26, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsiderations Denied June 26, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mandamus. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Wright.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 07-31-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 09-24-97. Lower Ct # :E16116.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. S98X0486 and reversed in Case No. S98A0484.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital sought review of a judgment from the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which affirmed the validity of a rule promulgated by appellee State Health Planning Agency (SHPA). Cross-appellant outpatient facility sought review of the trial court's judgment, arguing that the trial court should not have considered the hospital's mandamus request.


OVERVIEW: The SHPA promulgated rules exempting certain facilities from the certificate of need requirements of the State Health Planning Act, in an attempt to satisfy the Act in connection with the relocation of the outpatient center. The outpatient center had moved and been in operation for two years when it applied for and received a certificate of need. The hospital filed an administrative appeal of the decision granting the certificate of need, which was affirmed. On appeal, the trial court refused to hear the hospital's constitutional challenge to the rules. On further review, the court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court found that the SHPA was authorized only to take action that carried into effect those laws already passed by the general assembly. The SHPA had no constitutional authority to legislate, and it was not authorized to establish rules that conflicted with legislation. The court affirmed the trial court's decision to hear the hospital's petition for a writ of mandamus, rather than grant the stay requested by the outpatient center, holding that mandamus relief was proper where the alternative legal remedy was not equally convenient, complete, or beneficial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in the hospital's direct appeal and found that the SHPA exceeded its authority by promulgating a rule in direct conflict with an express legislative requirement. The court affirmed the judgment in the outpatient center's cross-appeal.

 

48 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Moore v. Ray


S98A0345.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 457; 499 S.E.2d 636; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 510; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 1705



May 18, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 17-10-7 (c); constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Wyatt Cummings Moore.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 05-30-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 07-31-97. Lower Ct # :E58960.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of an order of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which denied the inmate's application for a writ of mandamus to compel respondent Chairman of the State Board of Pardons to consider the inmate eligible for parole, following the inmate's sentence as a recidivist, under Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-7(c).


OVERVIEW: The inmate was sentenced, under § 17-10-7(c), to two consecutive terms of probation. When his probation was revoked, the chairman determined that the inmate's sentence, under § 17-10-7(c), rendered him ineligible for parole. In determining that the inmate was, indeed, ineligible for parole, the court relied on a prior ruling, which held that Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-16, which provided for a sentence of life without parole, did not violate the doctrine of separations of powers. Like § 17-10-16, Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-7 did not impinge upon the parole board's authority to grant parole, it simply rendered certain defendants ineligible for parole. The legislature's power to prescribe punishment for crime included the power to make ineligibility for parole part of that punishment. The court also rejected the inmate's argument that the application of § 17-10-7 to him violated the prohibition against ex post facto laws. The court found that the inclusion of an effective date provision in the Sentence Reform Act of 1994 did not affect the applicability of § 17-10-7. The only effect the Sentence Reform Act of 1994 had on § 17-10-7 was to change the numbering and add a few words.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's order denying the inmate's application for a writ of mandamus.

 

49 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Adams v. State


S98A0341.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 405; 498 S.E.2d 268; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 442; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 1423



May 4, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 17-10-15 (b); constitutional question. Ware Superior Court. Before Judge Blount.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 10-29-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 10-29-97. Lower Ct # :97W2226 97W2227 97W2229 97W2233.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Ware Superior Court, which granted the State's motion to compel him to submit to an HIV test, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-15 (b), following a struggle with police officers who arrested him. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statute on Fourth Amendment, right of privacy, and equal protection grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant fought with police who came to interrogate and arrest him. In the course of the struggle, defendant began to bleed and one of the officers sustained a cut. Fearing that defendant's blood contaminated his cut, the officer requested a blood test from defendant pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-15 (b). The trial court ordered defendant to submit to the test and defendant appealed. The court affirmed, finding that the blood test was a search under the Fourth Amendment, but that the intrusion occasioned by the search was minimal and the blood tests were safe and were not brutal, offensive, or shocking to the conscience. Balancing the government's need to search against the intrusion occasioned by the search, the court concluded that the government's interest outweighed the individual's interest and that, therefore, the search was reasonable. The testing procedure was civil, not criminal, in nature. The results could not be used against the defendant in any criminal proceeding arising out of the alleged offense and disclosure of the results was limited to the victim and public health authorities. Thus, the statute accomplished its objective through the least intrusive means.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the statute allowing a court to compel blood tests for HIV did not violate the Fourth Amendment, the right of privacy under the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, or the equal protection clauses of the State and Federal Constitutions.

 

50 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Grantham v. Grantham


S98A0348.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 413; 499 S.E.2d 67; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 443; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 1421



May 4, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Child custody. Coffee Superior Court. Before Judge Newton.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 07-16-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 09-23-97. Lower Ct # :1295S1312.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and case remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a decision from the Coffee Superior Court (Georgia) that awarded appellee grandmother custody of the mother's five-year-old child. The mother had asked the trial court to supplement its custody order so as to find the facts specially and state separately the trial court's conclusions of law pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-52.


OVERVIEW: The grandmother filed a seeking custody of the child, alleging that her daughter, the child's mother, was not a fit and proper person to have custody of the child and that the best interest and welfare of the child required that legal custody of the child be given the grandmother. The trial court's initial order awarding the grandmother custody was vacated and remanded because no sworn testimony had been given. The trial court subsequently issued another order awarding the grandmother custody of the child. Although the mother had requested the trial court to supplement its order, the appellate record did not reflect that the trial court amended its order. The court granted discretionary review, and vacated and remanded the trial court's custody order. The trial court's order contained potentially conflicting conclusions of law and no findings of fact to substantiate either one, thereby precluding an intelligent review of the merits of the appeal. The court refrained from addressing the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 19-7-1(b.1).


OUTCOME: The court vacated and remanded the trial court's order that awarded the grandmother custody of the five-year-old child.

Mitchell v. State

SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 378; 497 S.E.2d 566; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 431; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 1270

Date of Judgment Appealed: 03-12-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 03-27-97. Lower Ct # :97C60914.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appeals his conviction from the DeKalb State Court (Georgia) of violating Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(5), which made it a crime to have a blood-alcohol concentration of 0.10 grams within three hours after driving.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(5), which made it a crime to have a blood-alcohol concentration of 0.10 grams within three hours after driving. On appeal, defendant raised several issues. The court affirmed defendant's conviction because 1) Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(5) was unconstitutional because it did not deny due process of law; 2) evidence of defendant's blood-alcohol concentration was properly admitted into evidence; and 3) the evidence was sufficient to establish the alcohol concentration element of the offense, and along with evidence establishing the other elements, was sufficient to authorize a rational trier of fact to find defendant guilty of violating Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(5).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of having a blood-alcohol concentration of 0.10 grams within three hours after driving.

Harrison v. Wigington


S98A0508.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 388; 497 S.E.2d 568; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 425; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 1260



April 13, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 17-6-50 (b) (3); constitutional question. Rockdale Superior Court. Before Judge Nation.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 11-05-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-12-97. Lower Ct # 97CV1967N.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, employee and employer, challenged an order from the Rockdale Superior Court (Georgia), granting a motion for summary judgement filed by defendants, sheriff and county, in plaintiffs' action challenging the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 17-6-50(b)(3). Plaintiffs' cross-motion for summary judgment was denied. The sheriff had determined that the employee did not meet the qualifications of § 17-6-50(b)(3) to become a bondsperson.


OVERVIEW: The employee was convicted of two counts of criminal attempt to hinder the apprehension of a criminal and one count of criminal attempt to commit bail jumping. The appellate court affirmed the felony convictions. The Board of Pardons and Paroles (board) later issued an "Order of Restoration of Civil and Political Rights." The employee applied with the employer to become a professional bondsperson. The sheriff denied her request, finding she did not meet the qualifications set forth in § 17-6-50(b)(3), which provided that a professional bondsperson had to be of "good moral character" and have no convictions for a felony. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the board had not pardoned the employee; the convictions were never removed. Plaintiffs lacked standing to assert that the sheriff's refusal to allow the employee to become a bondsperson by virtue of her prior convictions pursuant to § 17-6-50(b)(3) conflicted with the board's constitutional authority to grant pardons, and to remove disabilities imposed by law. The statute was only subject to a constitutional attack on that ground by one whom could demonstrate that her felony convictions had been removed by the board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granting defendants' motion for summary judgment and denying plaintiffs' cross-motion for summary judgment in plaintiffs' constitutional challenge of the statute which set forth the requirements for professional bondspersons.

 

53 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Jackson


S97A1791.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 308; 496 S.E.2d 912; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 382; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 901



March 20, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 49-5-180 et seq.; constitutional question. Decatur Superior Court. Before Judge Cato.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision by the Decatur Superior Court, Georgia, which granted an injunction against the portion of Ga. Code Ann. § 49-5-180 et seq. (statute), which contained the mechanism by which an alleged child abuser was listed in a database, after it found that it violated respondent acquitted child abuser's due process rights because the statute prohibited in all cases the confrontation of witnesses under the age of 14.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state enacted Ga. Code Ann. § 49-5-180 et seq. (statute), and established the Child Protective Services Information System as a central registry of confirmed, and unconfirmed, reports of child abuse. Department of Family and Children Services expressed its intention to continue its efforts to have respondent acquitted child abuser listed as a confirmed child abuser. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment and held that the entire statute was unconstitutional. The court held that normally stigmatization of reputation did not implicate a liberty interest, but more than respondent's reputation was involved. Appellant was attempting to take further official action against him. This implicated his status as an exonerated criminal defendant. The court held that substantive due process required that state infringement on fundamental rights be narrowly tailored to serve a compelling state interest. The statute was not narrowly focused to serve that interest, the welfare of children, but prohibited, in all cases, the alleged child abuser from compelling the testimony of a child under the age of 14. Thus, the statute was not properly focused, but was impermissibly broad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and held that the entire statute was unconstitutional because the statute as a whole established and maintained the Child Protective Services Information System, and did so for the protection of children, and barring respondent acquitted child abuser from compelling the testimony of a child was apparently in furtherance of that goal. Appellant state's laudable purpose could not override fundamental constitutional protections.

 

54 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Turpin v. Christenson


S97A1435, S97X1438.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 226; 497 S.E.2d 216; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 377; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 906



March 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Habeas corpus. Butts Superior Court. Before Judge Foster from Tallapoosa Circuit.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 04-14-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 05-13-97. Lower Ct # 95V562.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee prisoner brought a habeas corpus action raising numerous claims including ineffective assistance of counsel. The Butts Superior Court (Georgia) affirmed the prisoner's conviction for murder and robbery but vacated the prisoner's death sentence. The state and the prisoner both challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner based his habeas corpus action on many claims; however, several of the claims were barred because they had been raised and decided on direct appeal and several claims were procedurally defaulted. The prisoner argued that he had received ineffective assistance of counsel. The state argued that both the conviction and the sentence should stand. The court concluded that: (1) the prisoner failed to show that there was a reasonable probability that, but for trial counsel's errors, he would not have been convicted; (2) in the penalty phase, the prisoner's counsel possessed a wealth of information regarding the prisoner's psychiatric problems and drug abuse, which counsel ignored; (3) counsel failed to adequately investigate all the prisoner' s possible defenses to the death penalty; (4) the decision not to investigate the prisoner's mental health was not reasonable or strategic; (5) counsel committed a number of serious errors that hurt the case for a sentence less than death; and (6) but for counsel's deficient representation at trial, there was a reasonable probability that the jury would have recommended life in prison.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which affirmed the prisoner's conviction but vacated his death sentence.

Lafontaine v. State


S97A1814.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 251; 497 S.E.2d 367; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 376; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 897



March 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 40-6-391 (a) (5); constitutional question. Forsyth Superior Court. Before Judge Bagley, pro hac vice.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 03-26-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 03-26-97. Lower Ct # 96101900.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Forsyth Superior Court (Georgia) convicted the defendant for violating Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(5), the per se offense of operating a moving vehicle while having an unlawful blood alcohol level.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was convicted for driving while intoxicated after being arrested at a roadblock. On appeal, the defendant claimed the roadblock that led to his arrest violated the Fourth Amendment, that Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(5) was unconstitutional, and that his challenge to the admission of blood alcohol evidence should have been sustained. The court held that the constitutional challenge to § 40-6-391(a)(5) and the challenge to the admissibility of the blood alcohol evidence had been rejected by recent decisions. On the roadblock challenge, the court found nothing inherently unconstitutional about roadblocks. The roadblock set up primarily as a means to perform routine traffic checks was valid. The roadblock was established and implemented by supervisory personnel and, although field troopers were given limited decision making authority where to place the roadblock, their discretion was clearly minimal. The roadblock was not arbitrary or oppressive to motorists. The stop was made within constitutional confines. And, the ensuing arrest was the result of the defendant's personal decision to operate a motor vehicle while in an intoxicated state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction for driving while intoxicated.

 

56 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Lowry v. McDuffie


S97A2089. S97X2092.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 202; 496 S.E.2d 727; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 379; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 893



March 16, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended March 18, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 48-5-472 (b); constitutional question. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Staley.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 07-17-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 07-21-97. Lower Ct # 971167928.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed in Case Nos. S97A2089 and S97X2092.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff car dealer appealed an order of the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia), which upheld Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-472 (b) against the dealer's constitutional challenge. The dealer had filed the action against defendants, state and county tax commissioners. He contended that § 48-5-472 (b) was not authorized by Ga. Const. art. VII, § I, para. III (b)(3) and was specifically precluded by Ga. Const. art. VII, § II, paras. I and II.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the dealer as a taxpayer had standing to challenge the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-472 (b). The court also held that the trial court properly ruled that § 48-5-472 (b) exempted dealer-owned motor vehicles held for sale or resale from ad valorem taxation. The statute plainly, not impliedly, granted an exemption from ad valorem taxation for such dealer-owned vehicles. For a tax exemption to be constitutional, it must have been authorized by the Georgia Constitution or it must have been approved by two-thirds of the state legislature. The plain language of Ga. Const. art. VII, § I, para. III (b)(3) was broad enough to authorize the state legislature to grant an exemption to dealer-owned motor vehicles and it did not conflict with Ga. Const. art. VII, § II, paras. I and II. The plain language of the constitution empowered the state legislature to create subclasses of motor vehicles and to provide that those subclasses would have no tax liability. Thus, the power to exempt a subclass of motor vehicles from taxation was not granted by implication but by the plain language of Ga. Const. art. VII, § I, para. III (b)(3).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and upheld the constitutionality of the statute.

 

57 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Syntec Indus. v. Godfrey


S97A1511.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 170; 496 S.E.2d 905; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 342; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 815



March 9, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 34-9-103; constitutional question. Floyd Superior Court. Before Judge Matthews.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged the judgment from the Floyd Superior Court (Georgia), on the basis that Ga. Code Ann. § 34-9-103(a) (1994) was unconstitutional because it impermissibly shifted the burden of proof on appeal to the prevailing party who did not have a burden of proof before the administrative law judge in an action for workers' compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: The court granted a discretionary appeal and considered whether Ga. Code Ann. § 34-9-103(a) (1994) violated due process by impermissibly shifting the burden of proof on appeal to a prevailing party who did not have the burden of proof before the administrative law judge. The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court and held that the statute did not violate due process and did not impermissibly shift any burden of proof. The language that required the appellate division to accept the administrative law judge's findings if supported by competent and credible evidence merely provided the standard of review for the appellate division. The standard of review did not relieve appellee employee of the burden to prove that he suffered a compensable injury and did not shift the burden to the employer to prove that the employee was not entitled to recover. The court refused to consider the question of whether the statute impermissibly permitted the appellate division to weigh the evidence and assess the credibility of witnesses because the employer did not raise the issue before the lower court or the appellate division.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Randolph v. State


S97A1517.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 147; 496 S.E.2d 258; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 286; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 741



March 2, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 16-6-5.1 (b); constitutional question. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Castellani.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged by interlocutory appeal the denial of his motion to dismiss two counts for sexual assault against a person in custody by the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia). The trial court certified for immediate review defendant's claim that Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-5.1(b) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-5.1(b) was unconstitutional because of a violation of the one-subject rule of the Georgia Constitution and because of vagueness. The court granted defendant's interlocutory appeal application, posing two questions: 1) whether § 16-6-5.1 violated Ga. Const. art. III, § V, par. III (1983), or art. III, § V, par. IV (1983); and 2) whether Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-5.1 was unconstitutionally vague as applied to this case. The court affirmed, holding that the body of the act that followed the caption definitely related to it, had a natural connection to it, and was not in conflict with it. Accordingly, there was no violation of the constitutional requirement. The court also held that the statute gave one in defendant's position sufficient warning regarding those persons with whom it was forbidden for him to engage in sexual conduct, and thus was sufficient to convey sufficiently definite warning as to the proscribed conduct. Thus, the trial court was correct in rejecting defendant's vagueness attack on § 16-6-5.1(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court to deny defendant's motion to dismiss a two-count indictment against him.

Woodard v. State


S97A1867.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 317; 496 S.E.2d 896; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 289; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 743; 71 A.L.R.5th 787



March 2, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended On Reconsideration April 2, 1998. Reconsideration Dismissed April 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 24-3-16; constitutional question. Carroll Superior Court. Before Judge Duffey.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment from the Carroll Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of child molestation. Defendant argued that the trial court erred by admitting hearsay statements that were made by a six-year-old witness to the crime, thus calling into question the validity of Ga. Code Ann. § 24-3-16.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of child molestation. He argued that the trial court erred by admitting into evidence certain hearsay statements that were made out-of-court by a six-year-old witness to the crime. The issue involved the validity of the 1995 amendment to the Child Hearsay Statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 24-3-16. The amendment allows hearsay declarations made by a child under the age of 14 who witnessed an act of sexual or physical abuse inflicted on another to be introduced as substantive evidence in a criminal trial, so long as the child declarant is available to testify. The court struck down the statute because it violated well established principles of equal protection by creating disparate classifications among similarly situated individuals, all of whom have been charged under the same criminal code section with the same crime, with no rational basis for doing so.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

61 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Santana v. Ga. Power Co.


S97A2055.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 127; 498 S.E.2d 521; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 259; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 648



February 23, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] High-voltage Safety Act; constitutional question. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Benefield.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Clayton Superior Court (Georgia) granted summary judgment to appellee alleged tortfeasor in appellant victims' action for damages suffered when they came into contact with appellee's high voltage power line. The victims challenged the dismissal of their action.


OVERVIEW: The victims were injured when a metal ladder that they were using while painting a building came into contact with the alleged tortfeasor's power lines. The lower court granted summary judgment to the alleged tortfeasor on the ground that the High-voltage Safety Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 46-3-30 et seq. relieved the alleged tortfeasor from any liability because of the victims' failure to give statutorily required notice of their work. The court affirmed the summary judgment. Ga. Code Ann. § 46-3-39(a) absolved any owner of high-voltage lines from liability for damage resulting from work in the vicinity of the line unless the utilities protection center, an organization formed by utilities, was notified before the work began. That statute was not so vague that it denied the victims due process because the language was clear and unambiguous in its requirement that notice be given before work began. The victims' due process rights were not violated by depriving them of a common law claim because the state was free to eliminate any cause of action before it had accrued.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the victims' action for damages from their contact with the alleged tortfeasor's power lines was affirmed.

 

62 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Bohannon v. State


S97A2082.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 130; 497 S.E.2d 552; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 276; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 666



February 23, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 4-6-391 (a) (5); constitutional question. Stephens Superior Court. Before Judge Smith, pro hac vice.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned for an interlocutory appeal of a judgment of the Stephens Superior Court (Georgia), which entered a judgment on charges of drunk driving against defendant. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(5), on the basis that § 40-6-391 was overbroad, vague, and was not reasonably related to a legitimate state interest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with a violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(5). The court granted defendant's petition for an interlocutory appeal, in which defendant contended that § 40-6-391(a)(5) violated due process because it was not reasonably related to a legitimate state interest, because it was too vague to apprise people of the prohibited conduct, and because it was overbroad in that it criminalized constitutionally-protected activity. The court held that the statute was constitutional, and affirmed the trial court judgment. The court held that § 40-6-391(a)(5) was reasonably related to a legitimate state interest of public safety in that the statute curtailed alcohol-related accidents. The court held that the statute was not impermissibly vague because the statute sufficiently informed people of the conduct that was prohibited. The court rejected defendant's overbreadth claim, holding that defendant failed to demonstrate that § 40-6-391(a)(5) impinged on a substantial amount of constitutionally protected activity. The court found that defendant's actions in drinking and driving were not constitutionally protected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court against defendant on charges of drunk driving, and found that the statute regarding drunk driving was constitutional.

 

63 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Jenkins v. State


S97P1474.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 282; 498 S.E.2d 502; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 277; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 655



February 23, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsiderations Denied April 2, 1998. Certiorari Denied November 2, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 6954.
Reconsideration denied by, 04/02/1998
Writ of certiorari denied Jenkins v. Georgia, 525 U.S. 968, 119 S. Ct. 416, 142 L. Ed. 2d 338, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 6954 (1998)
Writ of habeas corpus granted Terry v. Jenkins, 280 Ga. 341, 627 S.E.2d 7, 2006 Ga. LEXIS 158 (2006)
Subsequent appeal at Jenkins v. State, 2014 Ga. LEXIS 114 (Ga., Feb. 24, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Wayne Superior Court. Before Judge Taylor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Wayne Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of malice murders, kidnapping with bodily injury, armed robbery, and theft. The superior court sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant received two death sentences, and the court affirmed the judgment. Venue was properly changed because there was no proof of prejudice or biased jurors. Credibility of witnesses was for the jury to decide. A separate trial on the issue of mental retardation was properly denied because Ga. Code Ann. § 17-7-131(3) required the jury in a capital trial to determine defendant's mental retardation during the guilt/innocence phase. The court gave deference to the trial court's decision on disqualification of jurors due to views on capital punishment. The state's peremptory strikes were properly based on its race and gender neutral reasons for the strikes. A directed verdict was not warranted under Ga. Code Ann. § 17-9-1(a) because the evidence regarding defendant's mental ability was disputed and conflicting. The court set aside a mutually supporting aggravating circumstance, but held it did not require reversal. Each death sentence remained, based on other valid statutory aggravating circumstances. The court held that the death sentence was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor and was not excessive or disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted and sentenced defendant to death. The court held that the death penalty was authorized for defendant's crimes, venue was properly changed, the jurors were not biased, and set aside the use of one murder to support the death penalty for another, but held that it did not require reversal.

 

64 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Turpin v. Hill


S97A1496.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 302; 498 S.E.2d 52; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 265; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 652



February 23, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 2, 1998. Certiorari Denied November 2, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 6968.
Reconsideration denied by, 04/02/1998
Writ of certiorari denied Hill v. Turpin, 525 U.S. 969, 119 S. Ct. 418, 142 L. Ed. 2d 340, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 6968 (1998)


PRIOR HISTORY: Habeas corpus. Butts Superior Court. Before Judge Allen from Chattahoochee Circuit.
Hill v. State, 263 Ga. 37, 427 S.E.2d 770, 1993 Ga. LEXIS 315 (1993)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a judgment of the Butts Superior Court (Georgia), which granted a limited writ of habeas corpus to appellee inmate for the purpose of conducting a jury trial on the issue of his mental retardation.


OVERVIEW: Appellee inmate was sentenced to death for the murder of a fellow prison inmate. The habeas court granted appellee a limited writ of habeas corpus for the purpose of conducting a jury trial on the issue of his mental retardation. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the trial court properly considered affidavits submitted by appellee because appellee satisfied the requirements of Ga. Code Ann. § 9-14-48(c) for the admissibility of the affidavits. The court held that appellee's mental retardation claim was not subject to procedural default. The court reversed the habeas court's ruling because the old standards set forth for such claims were not applicable to mental retardation claims raised in cases tried after the effective date of Ga. Code Ann. § 17-7-131(c)(3) and (j). The court remanded the case to the habeas court to determine whether appellee could establish under the applicable standard set forth in Ga. Code. Ann. § 17-7-131(c)(3) that he was mentally retarded so as to invoke Ga. Code Ann. § 17-7-131(j)'s bar against execution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the habeas court and remanded for a determination as to whether appellee was mentally retarded because the habeas court applied the wrong standard to determine whether appellee had presented sufficient credible evidence of mentally retardation.

 

65 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Rogers v. Dekalb County Bd. of Tax Assessors


S97A1812.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


269 Ga. 31; 495 S.E.2d 33; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 50; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 386



February 2, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 48-5-116 (e); constitutional question. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Hancock.

Date of Judgment Appealed: 06-10-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 07-07-97. Lower Ct # :9717202.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged an order of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), in favor of appellee Dekalb County Board of Tax Assessors, and determined that the taxpayer's aircraft was appropriately value and taxed pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-16(e), which was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The county assessor notified the taxpayer that ad valorem property taxes were due on his aircraft. The taxpayer's plane, which was used for business, was hangared in the county and its flights usually originated there. The taxpayer resided in the county but was a practicing accountant in another county. The taxpayer challenged the tax based on valuation and on the ground that Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-16(e) was unconstitutional. The lower court found in favor of the county assessor, concluding that § 48-5-16(e) did not create a separate class of property and that the taxpayer's plane was properly valued. The taxpayer appealed. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, concluding that aircraft were uniformly taxed within the county and the state. Thus, § 48-5-16(e) did not create a prohibited separate class of tangible property by requiring the return of aircraft for taxation in the county in which it had its primary home base. The statute merely fixed the situs for taxation purposes. That was not prohibited by principles of uniformity or of equal protection. Thus, the taxpayer's aircraft was properly subjected to ad valorem taxation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, which found in favor of the county assessor and determined that the taxpayer's aircraft was properly valued and subject to taxation without violating the state or federal constitutions.

 

66 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Hussey v. Chatham County


S97A2004.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 871; 494 S.E.2d 510; 1998 Ga. LEXIS 2; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 236



January 12, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Ga. L. 1994, p. 3940 et seq.; constitutional question. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Bass.

Chatham County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. James F. Bass, Jr. Date of Judgment Appealed: 06-10-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 07-08-97 Lower Ct #: CV960161BA.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, members of city and county board of tax assessors, sought review of a decision of the Chatham County Superior Court (Georgia), which, on remand, found that 1994 Ga. Laws 3940 et seq., authorizing appellee county to appoint a board of tax assessors, was constitutional and denied the members' action for a permanent injunction to enjoin the county from removing the members from office.


OVERVIEW: The legislature passed 1994 Ga. Laws 3940 et seq. authorizing the creation of a county board of tax assessors. The members of the joint city and county board brought an action against the county to declare the act unconstitutional and to issue a permanent injunction to enjoin the county from removing the members from office. The trial court held the act unconstitutional because it related back to a 1965 act repealed by implication. On appeal by the county, the court reversed on the implied repeal rationale and remanded the case to the trial court to consider the constitutional issue. On remand, the trial court found the 1994 act constitutional and denied the injunction. On the members' appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court determined that Ga. Const. art. III, § V, para. III provided that an act could not contain matters different than indicated by the caption, that the 1994 act to repeal the legislation implied that with repeal of its legislative authorization the board ceased to exist, that the power to create the office implied the power to abolish the office, and that the members' request for attorney fees was not asserted in a timely manner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which found that the 1994 act was constitutional and denied the members' action for a permanent injunction to enjoin the county from removing the members from office.

Turpin v. Todd


S97A1354, S97X1396.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 820; 493 S.E.2d 900; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 757; 98 Fulton County D. Rep. 152



December 5, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 19, 1997. As Amended December 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Habeas corpus. Butts Superior Court. Before Judge Howell from Cherokee Circuit.

Butts County Superior Court. Trial Judge: Hon. Shepherd Lee Howell. Date of Judgment Appealed: 04-23-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 05-20-97. Lower Ct # : 95V652.



DISPOSITION: Case remanded in Case No. S97A1354. Judgment affirmed in part; reversed in part; and remanded in part in Case No. S97X1396.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the judgment of the Butts Superior Court (Georgia), which after hearing petitioner prisoner's habeas corpus action, reversed his death sentence imposed after his conviction for murder and armed robbery. The prisoner cross-appealed the denial of relief on guilt-innocence and sentencing issues raised by him.


OVERVIEW: In challenging the judgment, the state claimed that the issue of improper contact between the jury and the bailiff, during which the bailiff was asked about possible sentencing ramifications, was procedurally barred because it was not raised in prisoner's direct appeal and that the prisoner had not shown the cause and prejudice necessary for its review. Though it recognized that an improper communication between the bailiff and jury might have denied defendant a fair trial, the court noted that the habeas court's decision was conflicting on whether there was actual extra-judicial communication as alleged. Thus, the court found that it was premature to decide that the verdict could be impeached. The court found that cause existed for failing to raise the issue on his direct appeal, but concluded that the prejudice" standard used by the habeas court was incorrect. In doing so, it adopted the federal standard of prejudice. It found no basis for the claim of ineffective assistance of trial counsel but that the habeas court erred in ruling that the ineffective assistance claim with respect to the new trial motion and appeal was decided on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in part, affirmed it in part, and remanded it to the habeas court for determination of several issues consistent with the opinion.

 

68 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Bridges v. State


S97A0890.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 700; 492 S.E.2d 877; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 744; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 4255



November 24, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied April 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 2385.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Bonner.

Fulton County Superior Court. Trial Judge: Hon. Alice Bonner. Date of Judgment Appealed: 01-28-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 02-26-97. Lower Ct #: Z60666.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his convictions for murder, armed robbery and aggravated assault in the Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder, armed robbery and aggravated assault in connection with a shooting death. After a jury trial, defendant was convicted, and the trial court denied defendant's motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court noted that, along with several proper jury instructions, the trial court delivered several improper jury charges that shifted the burden of proof to defendant. The trial court improperly instructed the jury that, in order to acquit, the jury had to find beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant did not commit the offenses. The trial court also improperly delivered a Sandstrom instruction, which charged the jury that intent to kill was presumed if defendant used a deadly weapon in a manner likely to result in death. However, the court ruled that the jury instructions as a whole satisfied due process where there was no reasonable likelihood that defendant was convicted based upon an unconstitutional burden of proof. Also, the court ruled that the improper instructions did not prejudice defendant because the evidence of his guilt was overwhelming. Thus, the improper instructions constituted harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of murder, armed robbery and aggravated assault.

Deyoung v. State


S97P0875.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 780; 493 S.E.2d 157; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 748; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 4248



November 24, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 19, 1997. Certiorari Denied May 26, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 3505.
Reconsideration denied by, 12/19/1997
Writ of certiorari denied, Motion denied by DeYoung v. Georgia, 523 U.S. 1141, 118 S. Ct. 1848, 140 L. Ed. 2d 1097, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 3505 (1998)
Related proceeding at DeYoung v. Schofield, 543 U.S. 892, 125 S. Ct. 168, 160 L. Ed. 2d 155, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 5219 (2004)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Injunction denied by, Motion denied by, Dismissed by DeYoung v. Owens, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 101221 (N.D. Ga., July 20, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Robinson.

Cobb County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Dorothy A. Robinson. Date of Judgment Appealed: 01-27-97. Notice of Appeal Date: 02-26-97. Lower Ct #: 939276705.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of the malice murders of his parents and sister and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the malice murders of his parents and sister, and the trial court sentenced him to death. Defendant sought review, and the court affirmed. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in ruling that a venireperson should be disqualified where it was for the trial court to resolve the equivocations and conflicts in the venireperson's responses to questions about the death penalty. The court held that defendant did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel. Requesting disqualification of a venireperson would not have been successful where no bias was shown, and other claimed errors were a matter of trial strategy. Sufficient probable cause existed to authorize the issuance of both search warrants. It was clear, based on the information contained within one affidavit, that there was a fair probability that evidence of the murders would be found in the house and vehicles parked in the driveway. Another warrant was not invalidated by an error in the affidavit regarding the date on which defendant had last visited a storage facility. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress his custodial statements.


OUTCOME: Defendant's murder conviction and death sentence were affirmed where the trial court did not abuse its discretion in disqualifying jurors, probable cause existed to support the issuance of search warrants, and defendant received effective assistance of counsel.

Black v. Fayette County


S97A0632, S97A1056.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 570; 492 S.E.2d 517; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 704; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 4011



November 3, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Condemnation. Fayette Superior Court. Before Judge Miller.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. S97A0632 and reversed in Case No. S97A1056.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged a judgment of the Fayette Superior Court (Georgia), which allowed a condemnation proceeding to go forward before a special master while a related inverse condemnation proceeding regarding the same property was pending. Appellant county contested the trial court's order in a related condemnation proceeding changing the size, location, and duration of easements granted to the county by a special master.


OVERVIEW: The county brought a condemnation proceeding to take an easement on thee property owners' land for the purpose of installing a water line. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court and ruled the condemnation ineffective. The county installed the water line during the appeal. After the easement was declared invalid, the property owners brought an inverse condemnation proceeding against the county. While the inverse proceeding was pending, the county brought another condemnation proceeding for installation of a finished water line. In the second condemnation proceeding, the trial court reduced the size, location, and duration of easements granted by the special master, and the county appealed. The property owners objected to the second proceeding going forward while the inverse proceeding was pending. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision that the second condemnation proceeding could go forward. The court reversed the trial court's modification of the easements and held that in the absence of bad faith the right of eminent domain was within the discretion of the county.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order changing the size, location, and duration of easements on the property owners' property granted to the county by a special master in a condemnation proceeding. The court held that the right of eminent domain rested in the discretion of the county. The court affirmed a judgment allowing the condemnation proceeding to go forward while a related inverse condemnation proceeding brought by the property owners was pending.

City of Atlanta v. Morgan


S97A1068.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 586; 492 S.E.2d 193; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 708; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 4007



November 3, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: Domestic partnership benefits ordinance; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Jenrette.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged an order from the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which entered a judgment that declared appellant's 1996 Domestic Partnership Benefits Ordinance unconstitutional under Ga. Const. art. III, § VI(IV)(a), (c), and the Municipal Home Rule Act of 1965, Ga. Code Ann. § 36-35-1 et seq. Appellant argued that the ordinance passed constitutional muster.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the 1996 Domestic Partnership Benefits Ordinance, Atlanta, Ga., Ordinance § 2-858, was unconstitutional under Ga. Const. art. III, § VI(IV)(a), (c), and the Municipal Home Rule Act of 1965, Ga. Code Ann. § 36-35-1 et seq. The court reversed this decision. It held that appellant city acted within its authority when it chose to provide insurance benefits to the dependents of a city employee. The court reasoned that it was within appellant's discretion as a governing authority to determine whether to provide such benefits to all, some, or none of its employees' dependents. The court concluded that appellant was authorized to provide benefits to those dependents that were financially reliant upon a city employee.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's finding that appellant city's Domestic Partnership Benefits Ordinance was unconstitutional. The court held that appellant was authorized to provide insurance benefits to its employees and their dependents, and that appellant acted within its discretion to allow such benefits to certain family members of its employees.
