Moran v. State


S97A1307, S97A1337.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 816; 493 S.E.2d 126; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 721; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 4015



November 3, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 17-6-1 (g); constitutional question. Henry Superior Court. Before Judge Craig.

Henry County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. William H. Craig. Date of Judgment Appealed: 12-20-96. Notice of Appeal Date: 01-13-97. Lower Ct #: 94CR0566. Henry County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. William H. Craig. Date of Judgment Appealed: 08-29-96. Notice of Appeal Date: 09-19-96. Lower Ct #: 94CR0566.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed in Case Nos. S97A1307 and S97A1337.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Henry Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted defendant of trafficking in cocaine. Defendant also challenged the denial of his appellate bond, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 17-6-1(g).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in a car that was stopped by police. Because defendant was acting suspiciously, the police officer asked for permission to search the car. The driver indicated that the car belonged to defendant, who gave consent to search. A canine officer indicated that drugs were in the trunk of the car. Defendant admitted that the drugs in the trunk were the only drugs in the car. Defendant was convicted of trafficking in cocaine. His motion for appellate bond was denied. On review, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and the denial of his appellate bond. The court determined that the failure to instruct the jury on both actual and constructive possession was harmless error because the jury was instructed that it had to find beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant possessed the drugs. A further instruction would not have benefitted defendant. The court held that § 17-6-1(g) did not violate equal protection. The classification under § 17-6-1-(g) was rationally related to two state interests. Therefore, the trial court did not err in finding that § 17-6-1(g) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for trafficking in cocaine and the denial of his appellate bond.

Chambers v. Peach County


S97A0648.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 672; 492 S.E.2d 191; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 654; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 3757



October 14, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Adult entertainment ordinance. Peach Superior Court. Before Judge Brown.

Peach County Superior Court. Trial Judge: Hon. S. Phillip Brown. Date of Judgment Appealed: 10-21-96. Notice of Appeal Date: 12-13-96. Lower Ct # : 96V444.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner of a lounge which provided adult entertainment sought review of the judgment of the Peach County Superior Court (Georgia), which denied the owner's motion for an interlocutory injunction against appellee county's enforcement of its new ordinance prohibiting alcoholic beverages being served in adult entertainment establishments.


OVERVIEW: The owner filed a complaint for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief against the county's enforcement of the new ordinance and sought a writ of mandamus ordering the county to issue her a permanent adult entertainment license. The county delayed enforcement of the ordinance for 45 days, in which time the trial court, after a hearing, denied the owner's request for an interlocutory injunction, concluding that the new ordinance was constitutional and that the owner had not shown a likelihood of success on the merits. The court agreed with the trial court. The ordinance met the test for content-neutral legislation because it furthered important governmental interests (the reduction of crime and the protection of property values), which were unrelated to the suppression of speech, and the incidental restriction of speech was no greater than necessary to further the governmental interests. The owner's argument that the new ordinance could not be applied constitutionally because she provided adult entertainment and alcoholic beverages prior to passage of the ordinance failed because she had no protectable property interest in the renewal of her license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the interlocutory injunction to the owner.

Gee v. Prof'l Practices Comm'n


S97A1075.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teacher appealed the judgment from the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which denied his request that defendant Georgia Professional Practices Commission (Practices Commission) be enjoined from taking any action against his teaching certificate without first conducting a hearing, and denied his request for declaratory judgment that the Practices Commission violated his procedural due process rights by not conducting such a hearing.


OVERVIEW: Students accused the teacher of making sexual advances toward them. After an investigation, the county school superintendent reported the matter to the Practices Commission. The teacher filed an action for injunctive relief preventing the Practices Commission from taking any action against his teaching certificate without first conducting a hearing. The teacher also sought a declaratory judgment that the Practices Commission had violated his procedural due process rights by not conducting such a hearing, and a declaratory judgment that Ga. Code Ann. §§ 20-2-796, 20-2-797, which authorized the Practices Commission's investigative actions, were unconstitutional. The superior court granted the Practices Commission's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court found that both the state's statutory scheme and its actions against the teacher's license to teach under that scheme satisfied the requirements of procedural due process and affirmed the summary judgment. The system required a hearing to be conducted in contested cases even before a formal recommendation was made concerning the revocation or suspension of a teaching license. The teacher was provided a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that the state's statutory scheme and its actions against the teacher's license to teach under that scheme satisfied the requirements of procedural due process.

City of Cumming v. Realty Dev. Corp.


S97A1285.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 461; 491 S.E.2d 60; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 632; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 3685



October 6, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Zoning. Forsyth Superior Court. Before Judge Gault.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged the order of the Forsyth Superior Court (Georgia), which found city in willful contempt of an order remanding a zoning matter, which was brought by appellee developers.


OVERVIEW: Developers sought rezoning for a project and annexed the tract into city. City denied the zoning application. The trial court found the existing zoning unconstitutional and directed city to reconsider developers' application. That order was not appealed. City gave developers notice of a vote, but stated that no hearing would be conducted. City voted to rezone the property for other than the sought use. The trial court found the rezoning to be unconstitutional and found that city had willfully violated its previous order. The trial court remanded again, and city appealed. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part and held that city willfully violated the trial court's order by making no effort to reconsider the rezoning application or to consider the findings and conclusions made in the first order. The sanction, requiring payment until compliance, was proper, but the award of attorney fees was not because it did nothing to encourage compliance and, therefore, was punitive. A hearing was necessary because the statute required one hearing in the process and the trial court's order remanding the matter had the effect of starting the process again.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment that held city in contempt for willfully violating the trial court's previous order.

 

76 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



City of Lilburn v. Sanchez


S97A0678, S97A0870.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 520; 491 S.E.2d 353; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 622; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 3681



October 6, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Ordinance; pot-bellied pig; constitutional question. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Davis, pro hac vice.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an order of the Gwinnett Superior Court, Georgia, which, in an action brought by appellee resident, declared unconstitutional the city's municipal ordinance requiring land lots at least one acre in size for the keeping of a Vietnamese pot-bellied pig as a domestic pet.


OVERVIEW: A resident challenged the constitutionality of a city ordinance which required land lots at least one acre in size for the keeping of a Vietnamese pot-bellied pig as a domestic pet. The lower court issued an order which declared the ordinance unconstitutional, and the city appealed. The court reversed and held that a rational relationship existed between the ordinance and the legitimate governmental goal of reducing the substantial negative impacts the animals might have upon residential communities. The court found that because ownership of a Vietnamese pot-bellied pig was not a fundamental right, and because pot-bellied pig owners were not a suspect class, the city's ordinance had to be examined under the rational basis test. The court found that the rational relation between the ordinance and its goals was clear. The court held that because no claim was made that the ordinance was arbitrary on its face or as applied, the constitutionality of the ordinance was conclusively established.


OUTCOME: The lower court's order declaring the city's ordinance unconstitutional was reversed.

Campbell v. Dep't of Corr.


S97A0767.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff challenged decisions from the Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia), which transferred her tort action against defendant corrections department pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 50-21-28 and ordered her to pay the corrections department's attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff contended that § 50-21-28 was unconstitutional, as well as arguing that the trial court erred in awarding attorney fees to the corrections department pursuant to Ga. Also, the award of attorney fees as sanctions under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-15-14 was erroneous because plaintiff's constitutional argument was arguably supported by the text of the Georgia Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision transferring the action and reversed the trial court's decision ordering plaintiff to pay the corrections department's attorney fees.

 

78 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Dee v. Sweet


S97A0563.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 346; 489 S.E.2d 823; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 509; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 3398



September 15, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 16-14-6 (c); constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Bonner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which awarded attorney fees under the Georgia Racketeer Influenced & Corrupt Organizations (RICO) Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-14-6(c), to appellees, in a RICO action where appellants were found in violation of RICO and appellees were awarded damages. Appellants challenged the constitutionality of § 16-14-6(c).


OVERVIEW: Appellees filed a civil action against appellants, asserting claims that arose out of the dissolution of an executive search business and seeking damages for Georgia Racketeer Influenced & Corrupt Organizations Act (RICO), Ga. Code. Ann. § 16-14-1 et seq., violations. A jury found that appellants violated RICO and awarded damages to appellees. Appellees filed a motion for attorney fees under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-14-6(c). The trial court granted the motion. Appellants challenged the constitutionality of the statute. The court affirmed, holding that § 16-14-6(c) did not violate the constitutional guarantees of due process and equal protection or deny access to the courts. The court found that it was neither unreasonable nor arbitrary for the state legislature to distinguish between RICO defendants and non-RICO defendants in making the decision to treat the former differently by requiring only RICO defendants to bear the financial responsibility of attorney fees and costs reasonably incurred by RICO plaintiffs in response to appellate litigation a RICO defendant elected to pursue upon judgment being entered in favor of the RICO plaintiff.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's award of attorney fees to appellees who were awarded damages in a Georgia Racketeer Influenced & Corrupt Organizations (RICO) Act action against appellants, who were found to be in violation of RICO. The court held that the attorney fee statute under RICO was not unconstitutional and did not violate due process or equal protection.

 

79 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Copeland v. State


S97A1013.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 375; 490 S.E.2d 68; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 516; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 3410



September 15, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Local amendment; water and sewer tax; Constitutional question. Henry Superior Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, intervening taxpayers, sought review of a judgment from the trial court (Georgia) concluding a proposal to issue water and sewage revenue bonds was valid, and ruling a local amendment to the state constitution was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Water and sewage bonds in the aggregate amount of $ 45,830,000 were issued and appellants, intervening taxpayers, contested the validity and legality of the bonds. The trial court found the proposal to issue the bonds was sound, reasonable, and feasible. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that a local amendment to Ga. Const. art. VII, § IV, para. II, enacted by 1968 Ga. Laws, p. 1739, authorizing issuance of the bonds, was not repealed by implication or otherwise unconstitutional. The court also rejected appellants' contention that the tax was violative of due process rights and equal protection rights under the state and federal constitutions. The court ruled that under common law appellants did not have standing because they did not receive benefits of tax monies other taxpayers received. The court further ruled that the amendment was valid despite a debt limitation clause, there was evidence to support the trial court's determinations of facts, and an engineers' report did not lack certainty and definiteness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court on the grounds that the local amendment to the state constitution authorizing issuance of the bonds was valid and constitutional, and other claims by appellants, intervening taxpayers, were not meritorious.

 

80 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Fantasia v. State


S97A0611.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 512; 491 S.E.2d 318; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 517; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 3426



September 15, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 40-6-392 (d), (f); constitutional question. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Smith.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted defendant of driving under the influence with an unlawful blood alcohol level. Specifically, defendant appealed the admission into evidence of the certificates of inspection for the breath-testing machine as well as the results of defendant's breath test. Defendant raised constitutional challenges to the validity of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-392(f), 40-6-392(d).


OVERVIEW: Under Georgia law, a person suspected of driving under the influence who was asked to submit to a breath test had the right to refuse the test. But, if the person refused, then the refusal to submit to the test was admissible at trial under Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-392(d). On defendant's appeal of his conviction and of the admission of certain evidence, the court affirmed. The court first noted that Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-392(f) had no constitutional infirmity, as decided in a recent decision by the court. Further, Georgia's statutory scheme, which meant that defendant had to choose between either submitting to the breath test or refusing to do so but having the refusal admitted into evidence, was not the equivalent of compelling defendant to perform an act to incriminate himself. Moreover, because defendant was not compelled by the state to submit to the breath test, the admission of the test results was not error. Finally, it was not error under the best evidence rule to admit photocopies of the certificates of inspection of the breath-testing machine because the originals were accounted for, and there was no evidence that the photocopies were not exact duplicates of the original.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for driving under the influence with an unlawful blood alcohol level and affirmed the admission into evidence of the breath test results as well as the certificate of inspection for the breath-testing machine.

Glean v. State, 268 Ga. 260, 486 S.E.2d 172, 1997 Ga. LEXIS 346 (1997)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Ware County Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of murder.

OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder.

Thomason v. State


S97P0285.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 298; 486 S.E.2d 861; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 432; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 2595



July 16, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 30, 1997.
Reconsideration denied by, 07/30/1997
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Thomason v. Georgia, 522 U.S. 1129, 140 L. Ed. 2d 137, 118 S. Ct. 1080, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 1159 (1998)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part Head v. Thomason, 2003 Ga. LEXIS 278 (Ga., Mar. 24, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Floyd Superior Court. Before Judge Salmon.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a three-day bench trial, defendant was convicted of malice murder, burglary, and possession of a firearm by a felon during the commission of a burglary. The Floyd Superior Court (Georgia) sentenced defendant to death for the murder conviction, finding statutory aggravating circumstances under Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-30(b)(2) and (4). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The murder victim was a homeowner who discovered and reported a robbery in progress when he returned home during the middle of the day. The court held that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence gathered as a result of the State's warrantless seizures and searches of defendant and his car. The court found that the officer's initial stop of defendant was based upon reasonable suspicion and that defendant consented to the subsequent warrantless search of his car. The court found that the seizure of defendant was also permissible because the degree of the officer's knowledge, considered in its entirety, would justify a person of reasonable caution to believe it probable that an offense had been committed. The court also found that the trial court properly admitted into evidence two eyewitness identifications of defendant, made as he fled the murder scene, because no substantial likelihood of misidentification existed. To the extent that the trial court failed to follow the procedures delineated in the Unified Appeal Procedure, the court held that no reversible error occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Bishop v. State


S97P0205.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 286; 486 S.E.2d 887; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 431; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 2605



July 16, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 30, 1997.
Writ of certiorari denied Bishop v. Georgia, 522 U.S. 1119, 118 S. Ct. 1059, 140 L. Ed. 2d 121, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 1024 (1998)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by Bishop v. Hall, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 26523 (M.D. Ga., Apr. 2, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Baldwin Superior Court. Before Judge George.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of murder and armed robbery and imposed the death sentence. The Baldwin Superior Court (Georgia) denied defendant's motion for a new trial and entered judgments in accordance with the jury's verdicts. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed a man in the course of stealing his car. A grand jury indicted defendant for murder and armed robbery. The jury found defendant guilty as charged and imposed the death penalty based on the aggravating circumstance that he committed the murder in the course of committing an additional capital felony. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder and armed robbery, and affirmed his death sentence.

Phagan v. State


S97A0161.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 272; 486 S.E.2d 876; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 429; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 2622



July 16, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 30, 1997.
Reconsideration denied by, 07/30/1997
Writ of certiorari denied Phagan v. Georgia, 522 U.S. 1128, 118 S. Ct. 1079, 140 L. Ed. 2d 136, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 1151 (1998)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Remanded by Phagan v. State, 2010 Ga. LEXIS 645 (Ga., Oct. 4, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. 16-6-3 (a) and 16-6-4; constitutional question. Hall Superior Court. Before Judge Fuller.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Hall County (Georgia), which convicted defendant of aggravated child molestation, sexual exploitation of a child, and two counts of statutory rape. The judgment imposed sentence of 20 years (15 to serve, 5 on probation) on the statutory rape and sexual exploitation counts, and a sentence of 30 years (15 to serve, 15 on probation) for aggravated child molestation.


OVERVIEW: Included in defendant's indictment were two counts of statutory rape, which alleged defendant engaged in sexual intercourse with a 15-year-old girl during the summer months of 1995. Effective July 1, 1995, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-3(a) made it illegal to have sex with a person to whom an accused was not married, who was under the age of 16, and a similar change was made in Ga. Code Ann. § 16-3-4, which prohibited aggravated child molestation. The prior age limit had been 14 years. The victim turned 16 on September 29, 1995. The court held that the trial court did not err when it found that Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-3(b) was constitutional because there was a rational basis for the enactment of disparate sentencing for the crime of statutory rape based on the age of the perpetrator. The court held that the playing of the videotapes found during a search of defendant's home for the jury was erroneous because (1) the videotapes were not properly authenticated and (2) the court could not say it was highly probable that the erroneous admission of the videotapes did not infect the jury's determination that the defendant knew that the victim was under age 18.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, in part, defendant's convictions for statutory rape, and reversed, in part, the convictions for aggravated child molestation and sexual exploitation.

Dep't of Human Res. v. Phillips


S97A0468.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 316; 486 S.E.2d 851; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 430; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 2581



July 16, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsiderations Denied July 30, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Tort Claims Act; constitutional question. Baldwin Superior Court. Before Judge George.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Georgia Department of Human Resources sought review of a judgment entered by the Baldwin Superior Court (Georgia), in favor of plaintiff parent of deceased minor in her wrongful death action under the Georgia Tort Claims Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 50-21-20 et seq. (1994).


OVERVIEW: While in the care of defendant Georgia Department of Human Resources, plaintiff parent of deceased minor's daughter died as a result of an adverse reaction to two incompatible prescription drugs. The trial court entered judgment in the amount of $ 3.5 million in favor of plaintiff, and defendant sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that because the parties stipulated in a pre-trial order that the damage cap in the Georgia Tort Claims Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 50-21-20 et seq. (1994) was applicable, plaintiff was only entitled to judgment in the amount of $ 2 million. The court held that the pre-trial order was not modified by plaintiff counsel's remarks to the jury, and that plaintiff did not request modification of the pre-trial order until after the jury returned its verdict. The court held that the stipulation was binding on the parties because plaintiff's request to modify it was not timely made, and the trial court abused its discretion in awarding a judgment in excess of the applicable damage cap.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part judgment in favor of plaintiff parent of deceased minor in her wrongful death suit against defendant Georgia Department of Human Resources. Because the parties stipulated in a pre-trial order that the damage cap contained in the Georgia Tort Claims Act was applicable, the trial court abused its discretion in entering a judgment in excess of the cap.

In re T.B.


S97A0167.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 149; 486 S.E.2d 177; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 361; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 2342



June 30, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Former O.C.G.A. § 15-11-41 (g). Gordon Juvenile Court. Before Judge Bearden.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed from an order of the Gordon Juvenile Court (Georgia), which extended the juvenile's custody for an additional period of two years from the date of the original commitment pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-41(g).


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was adjudicated delinquent for acts of child molestation on his siblings. He was committed jointly to the Department of Children & Youth Services (DCYS) and the Gordon County Department of Family & Children Services. The commitment to the DCYS was for a period of two years. Near the end of the two years, DCYS moved for an extension of custody pursuant to former Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-41(g). The juvenile court granted a two-year extension and the court affirmed. Contrary to the juvenile's assertions, § 15-11-41(g) was not unconstitutional as a violation of double jeopardy protection. The juvenile code was concerned with the care, guidance, and well-being of children and was distinct from the criminal code. Because the extension acted to further accomplish the juvenile's treatment and rehabilitation, it did not violate the constitutional prohibitions against double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order extending the juvenile's custody for an additional period of two years from the date of the original commitment.

Campbell v. State


S97A0556. S97A0557.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 44; 485 S.E.2d 185; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 184; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 1641



May 12, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 17-10-6.1 (b); constitutional question. Lowndes Superior Court. Before Judge Cowart.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the mandatory minimum sentences they received after their conviction in the Lowndes Superior Court (Georgia) following their guilty pleas to one count of armed robbery. They contended that the superior court erred by denying their motions challenging the constitutionality of § 17-10-6.1(b) of the Georgia Sentence Reform Act of 1994, Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-6.1(b) (1994), under which they were sentenced.


OVERVIEW: Defendants pled guilty to armed robbery, their motions challenging the constitutionality of § 17-10-6.1(b) of the Georgia Sentence Reform Act of 1994 (act), Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-6.1(b) (1994), were denied, and they were given the mandatory minimum sentence under the act. The court affirmed their sentences and the denial of their motion and found that the statute did not violate the proscription against cruel and unusual punishment under the Eighth Amendment and Ga. Const. art. I, § I, para. XVII, the separation of powers doctrine under Ga. Const. art. I, § II, para. III, or the Equal Protection Clauses of the United States and Georgia constitutions. The statute did not impose unconstitutionally excessive punishment, and the fact that defendants were 18 years old at the time of sentencing and may have been first offenders did not render the statute unconstitutional as applied to them. The court ruled that the legislature acted within constitutional bounds in establishing maximum and minimum punishment in sentencing certain serious violent offenders and that the act bore a reasonable relationship to the legitimate concern of deterring crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' mandatory minimum sentences for armed robbery.

Hall v. State


S97A0300.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


268 Ga. 89; 485 S.E.2d 755; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 186; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 1635



May 12, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 6, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 16-5-60; constitutional question. Muscogee State Court. Before Judge Johnston, pro hac vice.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought an interlocutory appeal from an order of the Muscogee State Court (Georgia) that denied the mother's motion to quash accusations that she violated the Georgia Reckless Conduct Statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-60 (1996).


OVERVIEW: The mother left her three youngest children in the care of an older sibling, and one of the younger children died from a head injury while under the watch of the older sibling. The court, in reversing the order that denied the mother's motion to quash, held that the Reckless Conduct Statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-5-50 (1996) was unconstitutionally vague. The court reasoned that due process required that § 16-5-50 give fair notice to the mother that leaving her children in the care of an older sibling constituted conscious disregard of a substantial or unjustifiable risk of injury to another. The court held that the statute failed to give fair notice that she could have been charged for such conduct, because the statute forbade no specific or definite act, and failed to fix an ascertainable standard of guilt. In addition, the court held the statute was unconstitutional because it allowed for law enforcement to determine that an act was forbidden based solely on the consequences of any given act, and not based upon the act itself that created a substantial and unjustifiable risk of bodily injury to another.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that denied the mother's motion to quash charges that she violated the Reckless Conduct Statute because the statute was void for vagueness in violation of the Due Process Clauses of the state and federal constitutions.

Chatham County v. Hussey


S97A0315.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 895; 485 S.E.2d 753; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 168; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 1512



May 5, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Equity. Chatham Superior Court. Before Judge Bass.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent tax assessors sued appellant county seeking a declaratory judgment that a 1994 act was unconstitutional as well as a permanent injunction enjoining the county from removing the tax assessors from office. The county appealed the decision of the Chatham Superior Court (Georgia) granting a permanent injunction and determining that the 1994 act was void because it related back to the 1965 legislation that was repealed by implication.


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined that the 1994 act was void because it related back to the 1965 legislation that was repealed by implication. The court concluded that the 1978 act failed to meet either test for a repeal by implication. First, the court held that the local act did not conflict with the general act, but instead relied on provisions in the 1933 Code that were similar to the recodified provisions of the 1978 revenue code. Second, the court held that the 1978 act contained a comprehensive list of specifically repealed acts, but did not include the 1965 local act among the laws expressly repealed. Third, the court held that the exemption of certain laws in the 1978 act showed that it was not the exclusive law on the subject matter of joint city-county boards of tax assessors. Therefore, the court concluded that the 1978 Georgia Public Revenue Code did not repeal by implication the 1965 local act providing for the Board of Tax Assessors. Because there was no implied repeal, the court concluded that the 1994 act was not void from the beginning, and the court remanded for the trial court to consider the tax assessors' constitutional challenge to the 1994 law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court granting the tax assessors a permanent injunction and declaring that the 1994 act was void. The court remanded the action for a determination as to the tax assessors' constitutional challenge to the 1994 law.

Eckles v. Atlanta Tech. Group


S96A1507.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 801; 485 S.E.2d 22; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 105; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 1239



April 4, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Equity. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Etheridge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed. Motion for reconsideration is denied. All the Justices concur.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a determination by the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) that appellee's use of a trade name that was identical to his trade name did not infringe upon appellant's use of the trade name.


OVERVIEW: The appellant filed an action seeking an injunction prohibiting the appellee from using the trade name "ATG" for trade or business purposes. The appellant had been using "ATG" for years. After conducting a hearing, the trial court held the appellee's use of "ATG" did not infringe upon the appellant's use. The appellant challenged that order. The court found the undisputed evidence established the appellee's use of "ATG" caused confusion and misunderstanding on the part of the public. On more than one occasion, customers misdirected their inquiries and legal documents were not served on the correct entity. Based on this consumer confusion, it was clear the appellant was entitled to injunctive relief under the Uniform Deceptive Trade Practices Act. In a case of first impression, the court also determined corporations could not be represented by laymen and could only be represented by attorneys. By so holding, the court overruled any previous case which authorized laymen to provide legal representation to corporations in courts of record.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and found in favor of the appellant. The court also created a rule of law that corporations must be represented in courts of record by attorneys and could not be represented by laymen.

Goldrush II v. City of Marietta


S96A1494. S96A1496. S96A1497.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 683; 482 S.E.2d 347; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 99; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 874



March 17, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 3, 1997. Certiorari Denied October 6, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 4734.


PRIOR HISTORY: Adult entertainment ordinance; constitutional question. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Bodiford.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, several establishments that provided adult entertainment in the City of Marietta, GA, appealed the decision of the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia), which affirmed the constitutionality of an adult entertainment ordinance passed by appellee city.


OVERVIEW: Several adult entertainment clubs filed suit against the city alleging that a city ordinance prohibiting the issuance of both a license to provide adult entertainment and a liquor license to the same establishment was unconstitutional. The court consolidated the appeals of three clubs. All three clubs, at the time of the passage of the ordinance, held both a license to provide adult entertainment and a liquor license. The clubs alleged that the ordinance was an unconstitutional violation of the freedom of expression guaranteed by the First Amendment of the U.S. Constitution. The ordinance was passed under the authority of the Twenty-first Amendment of the U.S. Constitution. The trial court found the ordinance to be constitutional. The appellate court found that the trial court erred in its analysis of the constitutional issues, but that the error was harmless. The appellate court found that the ordinance was constitutional and that the due process rights of the clubs was not violated because they had no vested interest in the reissuance of an annual license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court holding that the adult entertainment ordinance was constitutional.

 

92 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Sexton v. City of Jonesboro


S96A1391.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 571; 481 S.E.2d 818; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 88; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 795



March 10, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Tax ordinance; constitutional question. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Simmons.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorneys sought review of a decision by the Clayton Superior Court (Georgia), which granted summary judgment for appellee city in the attorneys' action for a declaratory judgment that the city's occupational tax ordinance, Jonesboro, Ga., Code of Ordinances § 3-2-1 to -28, operated as an unconstitutional precondition on the practice of law and, therefore, impermissibly regulated the practice of law.


OVERVIEW: The attorneys brought an action for a declaration that the city's occupational tax ordinance, Jonesboro, Ga., Code of Ordinances § 3-2-1 to -28, was an unconstitutional precondition on the practice of law and, therefore, impermissibly regulated the practice of law. The court reversed a summary judgment for the city and found that the superior court erred in finding that the ordinance was not an unconstitutional regulation of the practice of law. Regardless of its stated purpose, the ordinance did more than generate revenue because it required registration and fee payments to be made at the beginning of each year prior to the transaction of business for that year and required an occupation tax certificate to be displayed indicating compliance with the registration and fee requirement. Therefore, the court ruled that compliance with the ordinance was, in effect, a precondition on the practice of law in the city. In addition, the ordinance's imposition of criminal punishment upon the attempt by delinquent payors to conduct business supported the conclusion that the ordinance's aim and effect was to regulate the practice of the profession rather than to simply gain revenue.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment in favor of the city in the attorneys' action to declare the city's occupational tax ordinance void for operating as an impermissible regulation on the practice of law.

 

93 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



O S Adver. Co. of Ga. v. Rubin


S96A1690.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 723; 482 S.E.2d 295; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 87; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 793



March 10, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Zoning; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Jenrette.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After remand, appellant property owner challenged a decision of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which ruled that certain zoning regulations were facially unconstitutional, but upheld others. The property owner filed both an application for discretionary appeal and a direct appeal, which were denied and dismissed, respectively. On reconsideration, the court reinstated the direct appeal to consider the jurisdictional issue.


OVERVIEW: The property owner argued that the court should make an exception to the rule which required an application in all appeals involving zoning. It argued that the rule should not apply where the superior court addressed a claim challenging the constitutionality of a zoning ordinance on its face. The court noted that, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 5-6-35(a)(1) and prior case law, there was a bright-line rule such that if the underlying subject-matter was zoning, an application for discretionary appeal had to be filed. The court declined to create an exception to that bright-line rule. An exception would have created confusion as to the proper procedure to follow in appeals in zoning cases without providing property owners or zoning authorities additional review of their substantive claims; would have permitted litigants to control the appellate procedure by raising a facial challenge to every zoning ordinance; and, more problematic, would have imposed on the parties and the court the difficult task of determining whether the superior court acted in its role as a "trial court" or as a "reviewing court" in each zoning case, so parties would file both an application and a direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the property owner's direct appeal.

 

94 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Abernathy v. Abernathy


S96A1770.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 815; 482 S.E.2d 265; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 76; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 676



March 3, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 4, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Domestic relations. Muscogee Superior Court. Before Judge Pullen.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee husband filed a divorce action in the Muscogee Superior Court (Georgia). Appellant wife raised in an answer lack of personal jurisdiction. The husband filed a motion to determine jurisdiction and/or to dismiss defenses of special appearing defendant. The trial court determined there was jurisdiction over the marriage. The wife appealed, and the trial court certified said order for immediate review.


OVERVIEW: The parties were married in Florida. The wife lived in Louisiana and had never lived in Georgia. The trial court ruled that it had jurisdiction over the marriage, by virtue of the husband's residence in Georgia for at least six months, and in rem jurisdiction over the marital property located in Georgia, but was silent as to personal jurisdiction over the wife. The court held that the trial court's order was correct without regard to the trial court's lack of personal jurisdiction over the wife herself. The trial court was not required to have personal jurisdiction over the wife in order to adjudicate the husband's claim for divorce. After the husband obtained proper service by publication, the clerk of the trial court mailed a copy of the published notice to the wife, who then had actual notice of the pendency of the divorce action. The trial court had jurisdiction to grant a divorce based on service by publication. The husband did not seek division of marital property located outside of Georgia.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the interlocutory order of the trial court.

 

95 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Banks v. Ga. Power Co.


S96G0894.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 602; 481 S.E.2d 200; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 47; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 521



February 17, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 220 Ga. App. 84.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged a judgment by the trial court, which entered a judgment of taking for a portion of the landowner's property by appellee utility and upholding the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 22-3-20. The Court of Appeals of Georgia affirmed the trial court's judgment, but did not determine the constitutionality of § 22-3-20. The court granted the landowner's petition for certiorari.


OVERVIEW: A special master entered an award, which allowed a utility to condemn a portion of the landowner's property to acquire an easement to construct, operate, and maintain a high-voltage electric power line. The trial court affirmed this award. The landowner argued that § 22-3-20 was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority because there were no standards to guide utility companies in determining whether the property to be condemned was "necessary." On appeal, the court found that § 22-3-20 restricted the power of the utility company to condemn the landowner's property. The utility company could only take property that was useful, needful, and necessary for public purposes. The court determined that § 22-3-20 delegated only that authority to condemn property reasonably necessary to establish and operate an electric generating plant, and only that property that was necessary for such public purpose. Thus, the court concluded that § 22-3-20 was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which held that the condemnation statute was constitutional.

 

96 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



City of Fort Oglethorpe v. Boger


S96A1607.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 485; 480 S.E.2d 186; 1997 Ga. LEXIS 36; 97 Fulton County D. Rep. 355



February 3, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Annexation; constitutional question. Catoosa Superior Court. Before Judge Wood.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citysought review of a judgment of the Catoosa Superior Court, which hedl that the city's annexation was invalid and enjoined the city from taking any action with respect to the annexed property.


OVERVIEW: This case presented a challenge to the power of the General Assembly to annex municipal property which was not contiguous to lands owned by the municipality. The court held the General Assembly's authority to annex municipal property was limited only by the state and federal constitutions, and that, therefore, the General Assembly could annex non-contiguous property. The court held that inasmuch as the General Assembly's power to annex municipal property was plenary, its annexation of the non-contiguous property was valid. It followed that the city's annexation of property, which was contiguous to the property, was also valid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment on the annexation of municipal property.

 

97 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Bo Fancy Prods. v. Rabun County Bd. of Comm'Rs


S96A0975.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 341; 478 S.E.2d 373; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 937; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 3692



November 25, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mass Gatherings Act; constitutional question. Rabun Superior Court. Before Judge Woods.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant promoters sought review of an order entered in the Rabun Superior Court (Georgia) in favor of appellee County Board of Commissioners (Board). The promoters were held in contempt of an injunction against the conduct of a rally because it would violate county zoning provisions and the Mass Gatherings Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 31-27-1 et seq., which was held to be both applicable and constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The promoters sought to hold a rally on property that spread across two zones, one permitting agricultural use and the other permitting residential use. The court affirmed the trial court's ruling that use of the residential property as a parking lot for the vehicles of attendees would violate the zoning ordinance because such use would be for a commercial purpose. But the court found that because the zoning ordinance did not specifically provide that the uses authorized for property zoned "agricultural" could not be employed for commercial purposes, the trial court erred in concluding that the rally could not be held on agricultural property simply because it was a commercial endeavor. Despite its commercial aspect, use of the agricultural property would provide recreational opportunities to any member of the public choosing to attend. The trial court erred in upholding the constitutionality of the Mass Gatherings Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 31-27-1 et seq., as the statute delegated overly broad discretion to an agency in determining when a decision on a permit must be made and was an unconstitutional prior restraint on the exercise of First Amendment rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting injunctive relief was affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the judgment finding appellant promoters to be in contempt was affirmed.

 

98 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Brannan


S96A1635.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 315; 477 S.E.2d 575; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 919; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 3992; 25 Media L. Rep. 1222



November 12, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 16-6-23; constitutional question. Thomas State Court. Before Judge McCollum.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the decision of the lower court which ruled that a law prohibiting the publication of a rape victim's identity was overbroad and thus facially unconstitutional and dismissed the charges pending against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a reporter who published a rape victim's identity as part of his news service, but stated that she had been assaulted and robbed. On review, the court vacated and remanded. The court found that the trial court unnecessarily found Ga. Stat. Ann. § 16-6-23 to be unconstitutional because defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment against him could have been decided without reaching the constitutional question. The court determined that the article published by defendant had not stated that the victim was raped and, therefore, he could not be charged under § 16-6-23. The court concluded that the facts alleged in support of the charge against defendant for violating § 16-6-23 were insufficient and there was no need for the trial court to rule on the statute's constitutionality before dismissing the indictment.


OUTCOME: The judgment finding the law overbroad and unconstitutional was vacated and the cause was remanded with direction.

 

99 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Dean v. State


S96A1298.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 306; 477 S.E.2d 573; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 915; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 3993



November 12, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 42-8-40; constitutional question. Gwinnett State Court. Before Judge Conner.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was defendant's interlocutory appeal of a decision of the Gwinnett State Court (Georgia), which denied defendant's motion in limine to determine his right to use certain records of the county probation office as evidence at trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with driving under the influence of marijuana. At the time of his arrest, defendant was on probation. As a special condition of probation, defendant was subject to random drug tests administered by the county probation office. Such a test was administered approximately five days after defendant's DUI arrest, and his urine sample was tested for the presence of marijuana or its metabolites. Defendant subpoenaed the county probation office's records of the urine test and filed a motion in limine to determine his right to use these records as evidence at the trial on the DUI charge. The trial court denied defendant's motion. The court reversed. The court stated that defendant was entitled to the county probation office's records of the urine test. The court held that the privilege protecting the confidentiality of the probation records from unfettered public inspection under Ga. Code Ann. § 42-8-40 must yield to an accused's constitutional right to information which was material to his defense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court stated that defendant was entitled to certain records of the county probation office material to his defense on the DUI charge.

 

100 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Lillard v. Head


S97A0125.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 291; 476 S.E.2d 736; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 883; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 3626



October 15, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Dissenting Opinion Substituted November 8, 1996. Reconsideration Denied November 8, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Habeas corpus. Baldwin Superior Court. Before Judge Cline.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded for proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of a judgment from the Baldwin Superior Court (Georgia) dismissing his habeas corpus petition. The issue was whether a writ of habeas corpus was available where a prisoner was unlawfully confined beyond the term of his sentence.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus asserting that he was being detained by the state even though he had fully served his sentence. The state argued at the habeas hearing that the prisoner's claim was not cognizable in a habeas corpus proceeding. The trial court agreed and dismissed the prisoner's petition. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings. The court found no fundamental difference between confinement under a sentence longer than that permitted by state law and confinement beyond the terms of a lawful sentence. In each instance, the confinement constituted a denial of liberty without due process of law. The court found that under the circumstances, the trial court was bound to inquire into the legality of the prisoner's detention. The court held that the trial court erred in dismissing the petition and in failing to inquire into the merits of the prisoner's claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment from the trial court that had dismissed the prisoner's petition seeking a writ of habeas corpus, and remanded the case for further proceedings, in a habeas corpus action brought after the prisoner alleged that he was unlawfully confined beyond the term of his sentence.

 

101 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



City of Atlanta v. Watson


S96G0600.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 185; 475 S.E.2d 896; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 709; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 3372



September 23, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 17, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 219 Ga. App. 704.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged the judgment from the Court of Appeals of Georgia, which reversed a trial court's grant of summary judgment in appellee, owners of multi-family residences' equal protection claim against the city. The court granted the city's petition for certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Owners of multi-family residences (owners) alleged the city violated their rights to equal protection when, as part of its Airport Noise Abatement Program, the city purchased only single-family residences from their owners. The appellate court reversed summary judgment to the city and also remanded the issue of the trial court that had correctly charged the jury on a federal statute, 49 U.S.C.S. § 47506, which prohibited the recovery of damages for airport noise. The court held that the appellate court erred. The court held that the city's actions did not violate the state constitution's equal protection provisions because the classifications that were drawn by the city bore a rational relationship to the legitimate governmental purpose of reducing land use that was incompatible with airport noise in a sound and responsible fiscal matter, and the city's decision to purchase single-family residences first was reasonable and not arbitrary. The court held that it was error to remand on the issue of the jury charge because the evidence supported a giving of the charge and any factual dispute regarding the application of § 47506 was resolved by the jury, the ultimate finder of fact.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court.

 

102 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Bankers Ins. Co. v. Taylor


S96A1167.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 134; 475 S.E.2d 619; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 718; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 3371



September 23, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 33-34-3 (a) (2); constitutional question. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Wheeler, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant out of state insurer challenged a declaratory judgment by the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) holding that Ga. Code Ann. § 33-34-3(a)(2), requiring out of state insurers to provide coverage equal to Georgia's minimum requirements, was not unconstitutional under the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution. Appellees were passengers of the insurer's insured, to whom the insurer had denied coverage.


OVERVIEW: The insured, a Florida resident, was involved in an automobile accident in Georgia. The passengers sued the insured, and made a demand on the insurer for payment. The insurer denied coverage and filed a declaratory judgment action. The passengers filed a cross-motion based on Ga. Code Ann. § 33-34-3(a)(2). The trial court denied the insurer's motion for summary judgment and granted the cross-motion. The insurer appealed that decision. It claimed § 33-34-3(a)(2), requiring out of state insurers to provide Georgia's minimum coverage requirements for all accidents occurring in Georgia, was unconstitutional under the Commerce Clause. The court found the McCarran-Ferguson Act removed laws regulating insurance from Commerce Clause scrutiny. Under the plain language of § 33-34-3(a)(2), the insurer's policy of insurance was deemed to provide the minimum coverage required under Georgia law. The statute did not have a wholly extraterritorial effect because it became operative only when personal injury or property damage occurred in Georgia. The statute was not unconstitutional, so the declaratory judgment was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the declaratory judgment that rejected the insurer's Commerce Clause challenge to a state law regulating out of state insurers.

 

103 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Union


S96A0686. S96A0687.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 32; 475 S.E.2d 915; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 512; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 2617



July 15, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 40-5-67.1; constitutional question. Clarke State Court. Before Judge Lawrence.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant one and defendant two were both arrested for driving under the influence of alcohol. The State sought review of the judgments of the Clarke State Court (Georgia) that in separate trials granted defendants' motions to suppress the results of an alcohol test. The cases were consolidated by the court because the legal issue presented was the same.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were arrested for driving under the influence of alcohol. In separate trials, their motions to suppress the results of alcohol tests were granted by the trial court, upon its finding that the implied consent warnings that defendants were given did not contain the specific language required by Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-67.1(b)(2). The court consolidated the cases for review, and reversed both judgments. The court held that § 40-5-67.1(b.1), which amended § 40-5-67.1 by providing that § 40-5-67.1(b) requiring exact language only applied to offenses committed on or after April 21, 1995. The court observed a precedential case, which held that the application of § 40-5-67.1(b.1) was constitutional. Defendant's arrests occurred prior to April 21, 1995, therefore the court concluded that under the pre-amendment version of § 40-5-67.1, the implied consent warnings read to defendants by the arresting officers were sufficient and the trial court erred in holding that the State failed to demonstrate compliance with the implied consent statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgments.

 

104 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Rower v. State


S96A1068.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 46; 472 S.E.2d 297; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 496; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 2696



July 15, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Double jeopardy; constitutional question. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Kreeger.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia), which denied his plea of former jeopardy as to a count of the indictment charging him alternatively with malice or felony murder.


OVERVIEW: After a trial, a jury found defendant of kidnapping with bodily injury, armed robbery, and two counts of kidnapping in connection with the crimes perpetrated against the victim. The jury could not agree on a verdict as to the murder count. Defendant filed a motion for mistrial as to that count, which was granted. After the state announced that it intended to seek a retrial as to the murder count, defendant filed a plea of former jeopardy. The trial court denied the plea. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order. Under the facts of the case, neither the bar against multiple convictions nor the double jeopardy bar against successive prosecutions was implicated. A retrial on the murder charge, following a declaration of mistrial because of the hung jury, was not barred by double jeopardy principles notwithstanding the fact that guilty verdicts were accepted and sentences imposed with respect to the kidnapping with bodily injury and armed robbery convictions. The remaining convictions for the lesser offenses did not bar retrial of the greater offense after defendant's motion for a mistrial was granted as to the greater offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that denied his plea of former jeopardy.

 

105 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Miller v. State


S96A0167.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


266 Ga. 850; 472 S.E.2d 74; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 471; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 2468



July 1, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 35-3-16; constitutional question. Cherokee State Court. Before Judge Hilliard, pro hac vice.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with possession of marijuana and driving offenses. The Cherokee State Court (Georgia) overruled defendant's objection to the use of a certified copy of the crime lab drug analysis in lieu of the lab technician's testimony, and admitted the document into evidence pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 35-3-16. Defendant was convicted on the charges and challenged his possession conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the use of the certified copy of the crime lab drug analysis in lieu of the lab technician's testimony violated his right to confront the witnesses against him, as guaranteed him by U.S. Const. amend. VI and Ga. Const. art. I, § I, par. XIV. Defendant asserted that Ga. Code Ann. § 35-3-16 was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that because § 35-3-16 was unconstitutional because it authorized the introduction of an ex parte affidavit into evidence against defendant in contravention of his constitutional guaranty to confront the witnesses against him. Because the certificate did not fit within any statutorily recognized hearsay exception, it was error for the trial court to admit the certificate without determining that the lab technician was unavailable to testify. The court further found that § 35-3-16 impermissibly shifted the burden of proof from the state to defendant by relieving the state of its burden of proving the illicit nature of the substance found in defendant's possession and requiring defendant to prove that the substance was not illegal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of possession of marijuana because the state relied upon unconstitutional hearsay evidence.

 

106 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Crenshaw v. Crenshaw


S96A0363.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


267 Ga. 20; 471 S.E.2d 845; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 362; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 2262



June 17, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 12, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Domestic relations. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Eldridge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife sought review of a decision by the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which denied her motion to set aside the divorce judgment in favor of appellee husband.


OVERVIEW: When the wife filed for divorce, she was represented by counsel, who later withdrew with permission. The wife's counsel's notification to her stated that services of notices were to be made upon her at her last known address. The notification included the wife's correct mailing address. Notice of the trial date was made by publication but neither the trial court nor the husband's counsel informed the wife of the trial date. The trial court heard the case in the wife's absence. The court reversed and held that the trial court abused its discretion in its denial of the wife's motion to set aside the divorce judgment. The court held that the notice by publication was not reasonably designed to insure that the wife had notice of the trial date and was therefore inadequate to meet due process requirements. The court found that the trial court had the wife's current mailing address; that it knew that the wife was proceeding pro se; that it knew that she had been informed by her former counsel that services of notices were to be made at her last known address; and that a trial was required to resolve disputed issues involving the couple's minor child.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in the husband's favor.

 

107 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Ortiz v. State


S96A0585.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


266 Ga. 752; 470 S.E.2d 874; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 347; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 2083



June 3, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 17-10-7 (b); constitutional question. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Castellani.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) for rape, aggravated sodomy, and burglary, and was sentenced to life imprisonment without possibility of parole under Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-7(b) and to a consecutive sentence of 20 years' imprisonment. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress certain evidence and that § 17-10-7(b) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence obtained as a result of his arrest on an unrelated peeping tom charge. Defendant argued that the arrest was a pretext for gathering evidence to establish probable cause to arrest him for rape. The court held that under the facts of the case, the trial court did not err in admitting the evidence discovered as a consequence of the arrest. The court held that Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-7(b) was not unconstitutional. The court concluded that it did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment under the federal or state constitutions. In addition, a sentence which was not otherwise cruel and unusual did not become so simply because it was mandatory and a determination that defendant should be sentenced to life imprisonment without possibility of parole did not require a consideration of mitigating factors. The court noted that seeking to deter repeat "serious violent felonies" was a rational basis for mandatory life imprisonment without possibility of parole, therefore, the mandatory sentence required by § 17-10-7(b) did not unconstitutionally deprive defendant of due process, nor violate his right to equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for rape, aggravated sodomy, and burglary.

 

108 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Franks v. State


S96A0446.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


266 Ga. 707; 469 S.E.2d 651; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 175; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 1508



April 29, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 23, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Hall Superior Court. Before Judge Girardeau.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Hall Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of murder and denied defendant's motion for discharge and acquittal.


OVERVIEW: The State sought the death penalty against defendant on a murder conviction. Defendant initially filed a demand for a trial. More than two regular terms of court were convened and adjourned and defendant was not tried. The superior court subsequently conducted a hearing to determine whether interim appellate review would have been appropriate. In that hearing, the superior court denied defendant's motion for discharge and acquittal. The court did not agree with defendant that Ga. Code Ann. § 17-7-171(c) was inapplicable in the case. The court stated that where the superior court deemed pretrial review unwarranted, the counting of terms would not commence until the superior court entered its order obviating pretrial appellate review. The court held that because pretrial review proceedings were not yet complete in the court, the counting of terms under Ga. Code Ann. § 17-7-171(b) had not begun, and the superior's court ruling had to be affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court, which convicted defendant of murder and denied defendant's motion for discharge and acquittal.

 

109 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Childress v. State


S95P1940.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


266 Ga. 425; 467 S.E.2d 865; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 121; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 989



March 15, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Glynn Superior Court. Before Judge Williams.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Superior Court of Glynn County (Georgia) that convicted him on two counts of murder and sentenced him to death for one murder and to a consecutive life sentence for the other murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in the trial court of two counts of murder in the shooting deaths of his niece and her father. At trial, the jury found as a statutory aggravating circumstance that the murder of the niece was committed while defendant was engaged in the murder of the father. Defendant was sentenced to death for the murder of the niece and received a consecutive life sentence for the murder of the father. The court reversed defendant's convictions on two independent grounds, holding that the trial court erred in excluding testimony that the mother of the niece and widow of the niece's father violated the rule of sequestration by discussing her trial testimony with another witness. The court held that the testimony of the niece's mother was vital to the state's case, and that her impeachment was critical to the defense. The court further concluded that the trial court erred in requiring the defendant to provide the state with written reports of all experts whom he consulted, whether or not he intended to offer the reports into evidence. Such error was determined to be harmful and required reversal because it chilled the use of experts by the defense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that convicted defendant on two counts of murder and imposed a sentence of death and a consecutive life sentence.

 

110 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Greene v. State


S95P1366.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


266 Ga. 439; 469 S.E.2d 129; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 118; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 972



March 15, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 28, 1996.
Reconsideration denied by, 03/28/1996
Reversed by, Remanded by Greene v. Georgia, 519 U.S. 145, 117 S. Ct. 578, 136 L. Ed. 2d 507, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 7648 (1996)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Taylor Superior Court. Before Judge Whisnant.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Taylor Superior Court (Georgia) convicted defendant of murder, armed robbery, and aggravated assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, armed robbery, and aggravated assault. He was sentenced to death. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying his motion for funds for investigative assistance, since he failed to show that an investigator was necessary to his defense or that his trial was rendered unfair. He also failed to make a threshold showing that his mental health would be an issue in either phase of trial. The trial court, aided by its assessment of the prospective jurors' demeanors, was entitled to disqualify them. The court also held that the state articulated a valid racially-neutral basis for the employment of peremptory strike against minority prospective jurors. The court concluded that the court's admonitions of the prosecutor's two references to the sentencing phase of the trial were sufficient to address any confusion in the minds of the jurors. The court affirmed the convictions holding the death sentence was not excessive or disproportionate to penalties imposed in similar cases, considering both the crime and defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, armed robbery, and aggravated assault.

 

111 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Union City Bd. of Zoning Appeals v. Justice Outdoor Displays


S95A1976, S95X1977, S95A1978, S95X1979.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


266 Ga. 393; 467 S.E.2d 875; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 106; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 946



March 11, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Sign ordinance; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Eldridge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and zoning board, challenged a summary judgment from Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which determined that certain provisions of a municipal sign ordinance were unconstitutional and enjoined enforcement of those provisions. Appellee outdoor advertiser challenged the denial of a variance request, challenged exceptions to permitting and fee requirements, and sought attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellee outdoor advertiser challenged appellants, city and zoning board, whose municipal sign ordinance barring noncommercial messages where commercial ones were allowed was unconstitutional. The trial court enjoined appellants from limiting message content on on-premise and special signs; the court agreed. Because the ordinance prohibited vital personal expression through residential signs, without a viable alternative, the court found that the trial court did not err in declaring content restrictions on on-premise signs in residential districts unconstitutional. The court found that a 50-foot exception for quasi-public institutions had a rational relationship to a legitimate government concern and was constitutional, and the trial court erred in finding otherwise. The court found that a time limit placed on political signs did not withstand strict scrutiny and was unconstitutional. The court found that the trial court did not err in finding the prohibition of obscene, indecent, or immoral speech overbroad and vague. The court declared appellee as prevailing and remanded the case to determine a reasonable attorney fee. The judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in part and reversed in part, and the case was remanded to determine a reasonable attorney fee for appellee outdoor advertiser, the prevailing party. Appellants, city and zoning board, severed the unconstitutional provisions of the ordinance and the remainder was still enforceable.

 

112 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Christensen v. State


S95A1586.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


266 Ga. 474; 468 S.E.2d 188; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 115; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 884



March 11, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 28, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 16-6-15 (a); constitutional question. Rockdale Superior Court. Before Judge Todd.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Rockdale Superior Court (Georgia), convicting him of solicitation of sodomy, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-15 (a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of solicitation of sodomy, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-15 (a). Defendant appealed, arguing that the statute prohibiting solicitation of sodomy infringed upon the privacy rights and free expression rights of adult citizens to the extent that it criminalized discussions about engaging in private, consensual, non-commercial sodomy. The court ruled that when a privacy interest was implicated, the state was required to show that the legislation had a reasonable relation to a legitimate state purpose. Further, the court held that in the exercise of its police power the state had a right to enact laws to promote the public health, safety, morals, and welfare of its citizens. The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant, concluding that the proscription against sodomy was a legitimate and valid exercise of state police power in furtherance of the moral welfare of the public.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting defendant was affirmed.
