115 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Robert W. Woodruff Arts Ctr. v. Insardi


S96A0093. S96A0095, S96A0096.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


266 Ga. 248; 466 S.E.2d 214; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 58



February 12, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Declaratory judgment. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Eldridge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a county and a corporation, appealed judgments of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which granted plaintiff individual's motion for a temporary restraining order in two actions against each defendant separately. Plaintiff alleged the unconstitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 36-1-19, seeking both declaratory and injunctive relief in both actions. The trial court found § 36-1-19 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Section 36-1-19 was found unconstitutional as the result of a hearing that was conducted less than 20 days after the service of plaintiff's petitions. That hearing was to decide plaintiff's entitlement to injunctive relief and there was no written consent that it was to decide his entitlement to declaratory relief. On appeal, the court found that a declaratory judgment action could be tried at any time designated by the court not earlier than 20 days after the service thereof, unless the parties consented in writing to an earlier trial under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-4-5. A trial court was also not authorized to grant a complaint for declaratory judgment sua sponte, without affording the opposing party a chance to be heard. The trial court had erred in entering the orders declaring Ga. Code Ann. § 36-1-19 to be unconstitutional and the orders were reversed. That the trial court certified its orders under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-54(b) did not mandate a contrary result. Under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-4-5, the trial court was not authorized to make a ruling on any declaratory judgment issue presented and the certification did not make valid the prior premature orders.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the trial court, which granted plaintiff's motion for a temporary restraining order in two separate actions against a county and a corporation.

 

116 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Garrard v. Hicks


S95A1775.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


266 Ga. 181; 465 S.E.2d 665; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 23; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 276



January 22, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Quo warranto. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Langham.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an application for quo warranto challenging appellee judge's authority to preside over his criminal trial on the ground that the judge was ineligible to hold the office of senior judge under Ga. Code Ann. § 47-9-90. The Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) denied the application, and defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that, because the judge did not become a senior judge immediately upon ceasing to sit as a superior court judge, he was ineligible under § 47-9-60(a)(3). The court held that § 47-9-60 permitted the governor to appoint a former superior court judge who had at least 10 years of service to the office of senior judge and that the judge met such qualifications. Nothing in the statute limited the ability to become a senior judge to active judges. Rather, the statute imposed only three restrictions: that the judge have at least ten years creditable service as a superior court judge; that the judge cease holding office as a superior court judge; and that the judge be ineligible to become a senior judge under any other provision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's application for quo warranto.

 

117 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Recycle & Recover v. Ga. Bd. of Natural Res.


S95A1445, S95A1447.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


266 Ga. 253; 466 S.E.2d 197; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 27; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 365



January 22, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reconsideration Denied February 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 12-8-24 (e) (1); retroactive effect. Barrow Superior Court. Before Judge Davis.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed in Case No.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation appealed two related cases of the Barrow Superior Court (Georgia), which affirmed a decision of respondent Georgia Board of Natural Resources (board), which denied the corporation's application for a major modification, under Ga. Code Ann. § 12-8-24(e)(1), of a solid waste treatment facility (facility). The trial court also found that the board's decision did not violate the corporation's constitutional rights.


OVERVIEW: The board issued a permit to the corporation for the construction and operation of the facility. The corporation filed an application for a major modification of the facility, which was denied by the board and affirmed by the trial court, under Ga. Code Ann. § 12-8-24(e)(1), because the statute's amendment required a three-year waiting period. The corporation appealed directly in one case and appealed by a grant of an application for discretionary appeal in the other case. The court dismissed the direct appeal, solely allowing a discretionary appeal under Ga. Code Ann. § 5-6-35(a)(1). The corporation contended that the board's decision giving retroactive effect to the amendment of Ga. Code Ann. § 12-8-24(e)(1) was unconstitutional. A property owner was found to have had a vested right to consideration of his application under the existing statutory law. Where the corporation applied for modification of its permit less than three years after operation, but before the amendment to § 12-8-24(e)(1), giving retroactive effect to the amendment would have resulted in an unduly delay in deciding the pre-existing application. The court reversed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal in case one and reversed the judgment of the trial court in case two, which denied the corporation's application for major modification of a facility. Error existed in the board's decision giving a subsequent statutory amendment retroactive effect over the corporation's pre-existing application for modification.

 

118 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Jekyll Island-State Park Auth. v. Jekyll Island Citizens Ass'n


S95A1668, S95X1670.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


266 Ga. 152; 464 S.E.2d 808; 1996 Ga. LEXIS 13; 96 Fulton County D. Rep. 167



January 8, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 12-3-235 (23); constitutional question. Glynn Superior Court. Before Judge Culpepper, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed in Case No. S95A1668. Judgment affirmed in Case No. S95X1670.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 12-3-235(23), respondent state park authority (authority) increased the fee it charged petitioner citizens association (association) for operating a fire department. The association sought a declaratory judgment and mandamus against the authority. The Glynn Superior Court (Georgia) held that § 12-3-235(23) was unconstitutional. The authority sought review by direct appeal and by cross-appeal.


OVERVIEW: The authority claimed that the lower court erred in finding that the last sentence of § 12-3-235(23) was unconstitutional and that the entirety of § 12-3-235(23) was thereby also unconstitutional. The court agreed in part and reversed the judgment that held the entirety of § 12-3-235(34) unconstitutional. However, the court affirmed the judgment that the last sentence of § 12-3-235(23) was unconstitutional. The court held that to withstand an attack of vagueness, a civil statute had to provide fair notice of its intent. The court found that this last sentence failed to indicate whether the authority or the county board of commissioners (board) determined the maximum annual fee and whether the fee was to be based on the fire services provided by the authority or by the board. The court also found that this sentence did not indicate whether the fee was to be based on the county or the island's population. Thus, the court held that this sentence was unconstitutionally vague. However, the court also held that there was a presumption of severability and that the lower court erred in holding that the remainder of § 12-3-235(34) was unconstitutional based on the last sentence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that held that the entire statutory provision was unconstitutional because the last sentence of the provision was unconstitutional. However, the court affirmed the judgment that the last sentence of the statutory provision was unconstitutional.

Appalachee Enters. v. Walker


S95A1070.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


266 Ga. 35; 463 S.E.2d 896; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 954; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 3752



December 4, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] GWINNETT County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. James W. Oxendine. Date of Judgment Appealed: 01-23-95. Notice of Appeal Date: 02-22-95. Lower Ct# :94A38141.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for a declaratory judgment, quia timet, and other equitable relief, plaintiff developer appealed from an order of the Gwinnett County Superior Court (Georgia), denying the developer's motion for summary disposition against defendant property owners, mortgagors, and lienholders. The developer contended that application of Ga. Code Ann. § 44-5-60(d) constituted a retrospective application of the law.


OVERVIEW: When the developer acquired the property there was a covenant in the deed that expressly ran for 30 years; however, the law at the time stated that covenants could not run longer than 20 years. The developer intended to develop the property when the covenants expired and obtained rezoning of the property. Subsequently, Ga. Code Ann. § 44-5-60(d) was amended to permit landowners in subdivisions to extend their restrictive covenants to 30 years. The court reversed the order denying the developer summary disposition and held that Ga. Code Ann. § 44-5-60(d) amounted to an unconstitutional retrospective application of the statute because the developer relied upon the law in effect at the time the developer purchased the property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and granted the developer summary disposition of his claim that the restrictive covenant's that applied to his property expired.

McIntyre v. State


S95A1096.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


266 Ga. 7; 463 S.E.2d 476; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 879; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 3444



November 6, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] DOUGLAS County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Robert J. James. Date of Judgment Appealed: 01-05-95. Notice of Appeal Date: 01-12-95. Lower Ct # :CR88200.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Douglas County (Georgia), which convicted defendant of murder and imposed a life sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried for murder. After his arrest and return to Georgia from Louisiana, defendant made a spontaneous incriminating statement to his mother. The statement came after he had been given his Miranda warnings. During the trial, the presiding judge was temporarily substituted due to the funeral of the judge's infant grandson. The court affirmed, and held that: (1) it was error for the trial court to have refused to give a requested charge on impeachment since a witness' prior conviction for a crime of moral turpitude was proved by secondary evidence admitted without objection, but that defendant did not show harm as well as error; (2) the procedure followed by the trial court due to the temporary absence of the trial judge did not require reversal because defendant did not show that he was harmed by the temporary substitution of the trial judge; (3) defendant's spontaneous incriminating statement to his mother was correctly admitted into evidence; and (4) the trial court's error where it failed to sustain defendant's relevancy objection to the sheriff's testimony that a non-witness had asserted his Fifth Amendment rights did not warrant reversal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction and sentence.

 

121 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Bishop v. State


S95A1359.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 821; 462 S.E.2d 716; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 838; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 3233



October 16, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] DEKALB County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Daniel M. Coursey, Jr. Date of Judgment Appealed: 03-10-95. Notice of Appeal Date: 04-27-95. Lower Ct # :94CR3447.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment by the Dekalb County Superior Court (Georgia) which denied defendant's motion to dismiss and a motion to transfer his case to the juvenile court. The trial court did certify its order denying defendant's motions for immediate review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with multiple offenses, which were within the exclusive jurisdiction of the superior court pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-5(b)(2)(A). Defendant filed a motion to dismiss and a motion to transfer to the juvenile court. The trial court denied the motions and the court affirmed the trial court's judgment because no violations of the doctrine of separation of powers, due process, or equal protection were shown. The court found that after the district attorney invoked the superior court's jurisdiction, the superior court did not violate the separation of powers doctrine by exercising its discretionary authority to retain the case because Ga. Code Ann. § 15-11-5(b)(2) granted the superior court post-indictment discretion. The court held that the discretionary choice of forums afforded the district attorney was simply a consequence of the exercise by the Georgia General Assembly of the power delegated to it by the Georgia Constitution. The court further determined that defendant's due process rights were not violated because a juvenile's right to be tried in juvenile court was derived from statutory rather than constitutional law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying defendant's motion to dismiss and motion to transfer to juvenile court.

 

122 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Benton v. State


S95A0471.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 648; 461 S.E.2d 202; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 708; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 2538



July 28, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] FULTON County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Don A. Langham. Date of Judgment Appealed: 10-27-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-14-94. Lower Ct # :Z29383.

This Opinion Substituted on Motion for Reconsideration for Withdrawn Opinion of June 29, 1995, Previously Reported at: 1995 Ga. LEXIS 512.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of kidnapping, aggravated assault, and incest in the Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia). Defendant filed a motion for a new trial, which was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-22(a)(1), which criminalized sexual intercourse between a father and daughter or step-daughter, unconstitutionally infringed on the right of privacy and that testimony concerning an earlier incident of the victim's prior accusation of sexual misconduct directed against persons other than defendant should have been admitted. The court reversed the judgment and ordered a new trial. The prohibition against incest was rationally related to a legitimate governmental interest and § 16-6-22(a)(1) was an effective means of accomplishing those objectives and did not violate privacy or equal protection guarantees. The trial court erred in ruling the evidence of the victim's prior accusations of sexual misconduct was inadmissible because the offer of proof established a reasonable probability of falsity with respect to the prior allegation. Because defendant's convictions were supported largely by the testimony of the victim and it could not have been said the evidence of guilt was overwhelming or that it was highly probable the erroneous exclusion of the evidence did not contribute to the judgment, defendant had to be afforded a new trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and defendant was afforded a new trial.

McMichen v. State


S95P0209.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 598; 458 S.E.2d 833; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 533; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 2307



July 14, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by, 07/28/1995
Writ of certiorari denied McMichen v. Georgia, 516 U.S. 1095, 116 S. Ct. 819, 133 L. Ed. 2d 763, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 790 (1996)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Remanded by McMichen v. Hall, 2009 Ga. LEXIS 640 (Ga., Oct. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] DOUGLAS County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. David T. Emerson. Date of Judgment Appealed: 08-25-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 09-19-94. Lower Ct # :CR93309.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The jury convicted the defendant on two counts of malice murder and recommended the death penalty for each count, finding that each had been committed during the course of the other murder and was outrageously or wantonly vile, horrible, or inhuman in that it involved depravity of mind, and, with respect to the estranged wife's murder only, torture. The Douglas County Superior Court (Georgia) imposed two death sentences. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant claimed he killed his estranged wife's boyfriend in self-defense and his estranged wife by accident. On appeal he challenged each of the statutory aggravating circumstances and argued that the court could not choose which death sentence to uphold based upon mutually supporting aggravating circumstances. The court held that the defendant's gross disregard for the virtually certain and profound impact of walking his five-year-old child through her mother's blood and leaving her screaming in the truck overlooking the murder scene while he drank beer at a neighbor's house was sufficient to prove depravity. The court held that it was appropriate for the court, when faced with mutually supporting aggravating circumstances, to select one of the two as a basis for affirming a death sentence. The court rejected the defendant's constitutional challenges to the death penalty statute, the court's proportionality review methods, electrocution as cruel and unusual punishment, death qualification of jurors and their use in the guilt-innocence phase, as well as defendant's claim that the death penalty was unconstitutional because the district attorney had unfettered discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and both death sentences, finding that each death sentence was supported by an aggravating circumstance, in that the murder of the defendant's estranged wife involved depravity of mind and the murder of her boyfriend was committed during the course of the estranged wife's murder. The court found no reversible error in the defendant's other enumerations of error.

Massey v. State


S95A0488.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 632; 458 S.E.2d 818; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 520; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 2246



July 10, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] FULTON County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Benjamin W. Spaulding. Date of Judgment Appealed: 11-28-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-28-94. Lower Ct # :Z52863.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convicted felon challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Fulton County, which denied his pretrial motion and motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The judge who presided over the convicted felon's trial and who sentenced him after the jury returned guilty verdicts was a pro hac vice magistrate designated by the Magistrate of Fulton County pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 15-1-9.1 to assist the superior court. The convicted felon contended that the designation of persons not elected to superior court to assist the judges of the superior court violated the Georgia constitutional requirement that superior court judges be elected. The court affirmed the superior court's judgment. The court determined that the magistrate who presided over the trial was designated to do so pursuant to the terms of Ga. Code Ann. § 15-1-9.1(b)(2), (e), and (f), and as a consequence was statutorily vested with the ability to discharge all duties and exercise all powers and authority of the superior court. The court concluded that the designation of the magistrate with statutory and constitutional authority to exercise the judicial power of the superior court did not make him a superior court judge. The court held that the magistrate's designation did not violate the constitutional requirement that superior court judges be elected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court.

 

125 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Ga. Dep't of Medical Assistance v. Columbia Convalescent Ctr.


S95A0497, S95X0499.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 638; 458 S.E.2d 635; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 505; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 2220



June 30, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] COLUMBIA County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Albert Pickett. Date of Judgment Appealed: 09-08-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-14-94. Lower Ct # :C84311.

COLUMBIA County Superior. Trial Judge. Hon. Albert Pickett. Date of Judgment Appealed: 09-08-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-15-94. Lower Ct # :C84311.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed in Case No. S95A0497. Judgment affirmed in Case No. S95X0499.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Georgia Department of Medical Assistance, sought review of an order of the Columbia County Superior Court (Georgia), which held that Ga. Code Ann. § 9-2-60, the automatic dismissal statute, violated due process. Appellee convalescent center sought review of the trial court's order which held that the state notice statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 9-10-2, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the automatic dismissal statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 9-2-60, violated due process because it did not require a hearing before dismissal. The trial court held that the state notice statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 9-10-2, did not violate equal protection guarantees. The court reversed as to the dismissal statute and affirmed as to the notice statute. The automatic dismissal statute did not violate due process. Although a litigant had a property interest in her cause of action, the state could terminate a litigant's claim for failure to comply with a reasonable procedural rule. The automatic dismissal statute was a reasonable procedural rule because it afforded litigants an opportunity to litigate their claims. A litigant had five years to produce only the most minimal of activity to avoid dismissal. Moreover, in the event of dismissal, it permitted the litigant to obtain a hearing on her claims by giving her the right to renew the action within six months of dismissal. The state notice statute was a rational provision that ensured that attorneys for the state would have time to travel and to familiarize themselves with the agency involved.


OUTCOME: The court reversed as to the automatic dismissal statute and affirmed as to the state notice statute.

 

126 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Crowe v. State


S95P0108.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 582; 458 S.E.2d 799; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 383; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 2070



June 26, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied February 26, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1443.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] DOUGLAS County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Robert J. James. Date of Judgment Appealed: 11-20-89. Notice of Appeal Date: 12-08-89. Lower Ct # :CR881092.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant sought review of a decision of the Douglas County Superior Court (Georgia), which entered a judgment of conviction for malice murder and armed robbery after accepting a plea to the charges. A jury returned a verdict imposing a death sentence. The trial court denied the defendant's extraordinary motion for new trial. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence, as well as the denial of his extraordinary motion.


OVERVIEW: After arrest, the defendant gave three separate statements where he admitted killing the victim to obtain money. He pleaded guilty and a death sentence was imposed after a jury sentencing trial. On appeal, the court held: 1) even though the defendant pleaded guilty, the evidence was sufficient to prove guilt and for the jury to find aggravating circumstances; 2) the guilty pleas were voluntary where the defendant was represented by counsel both before and after the plea, and the defendant was advised that he was pleading to an aggravating circumstance; 3) the statements were not coerced and were made after a valid waiver of Miranda rights; 4) the warrantless arrest was valid, and the search was made with consent; 5) at the sentencing trial, the prosecution did not withhold Brady material where defendant was given access to the file; 6) there was no prejudicial error because of jury selection, evidentiary and jury instruction rulings, or prosecutorial comment; 7) the decision to seek the death penalty was not made with unfettered discretion, but was based upon aggravating circumstances; and 8) the sentence was not excessive or disproportionate to penalties imposed in similar cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence for murder and armed robbery. The court also affirmed the denial of defendant's extraordinary motion for new trial.

Ga. Dep't of Human Res. v. Word


S95A0411.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 461; 458 S.E.2d 110; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 372; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 1992



June 12, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ROCKDALE County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Sidney L. Nation. Date of Judgment Appealed: 09-14-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-11-94. Lower Ct # :94CV1714.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state department of human resources sought review from a Rockdale County Superior Court (Georgia) judgment denying its petition to hold appellee father in contempt and refusing to order a separate income deduction order under Ga. Code Ann. § 19-6-30(c), because Ga. Code Ann. § 19-6-32(a) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The state department of human resources filed a petition for contempt against a father based on the father's child support arrearage and sought a separate income deduction order under Ga. Code Ann. § 19-6-30(c) et seq. After the lower court declined to hold the father in contempt and held that Ga. Code Ann. § 19-6-32(a) was unconstitutional, the state department of human resources appealed. The court found that (1) the statute in question, which required the employer of the father to deduct current and past due child support from the father's income, served an obvious legislative purpose of ensuring prompt and efficient payment of child support, (2) the statute did not violate the separation of powers because it merely stated a procedural requirement that once a court had determined and ordered child support, that court had to issue an income deduction order, (3) the statute required that such deduction orders become effective immediately unless certain requirements had been met, and (4) because the court reversed the lower court's determination on constitutionality, it remanded for a determination of whether the effective date of the order should be delayed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment against the state department of human resources and remanded with directions to determine whether the father had shown good cause for the delaying of the effective date of the income deduction order.

 

129 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Hca Health Servs. v. Roach


S95A0089. S95A0126.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 501; 458 S.E.2d 118; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 382; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 1995



June 12, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] FULTON County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Thelma Wyatt-Cummings Moore. Date of Judgment Appealed: 09-20-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 09-22-94. Lower Ct # :E12013.

FULTON County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Thelma Wyatt-Cummings Moore. Date of Judgment Appealed: 09-20-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 09-22-94. Lower Ct # :E29377.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part in Case Number S95A0089. Judgment reversed in Case Number S95A0126.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In challenges to defendant agency's approval of a competitor's certificate of need, plaintiff health services provider sought review of two separate decisions from the Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia), which rendered judgments in favor of the agency.


OVERVIEW: The agency, the state health planning department, interpreted Ga. Code Ann. § 31-6-47(c) as authority to allow it to exempt certain projects from the full certificate of need (CON) process and promulgated a new rule that dealt with relocation of existing facilities. Under its new rule, the agency granted CONs to a competitor of the health services provider. The health services provider challenged the issuance of the certificates, and the trial court granted judgment in favor of the agency. The provider sought review. The court reversed in part. It found that the rule constituted an unlawful delegation of legislative authority because the rule would have allowed the agency to do far more than merely administer and effectuate an existing enactment. Under the rule, the agency would have complete and unbridled authority to determine what health care facilities were subject to Ga. Code. Ann. § 31-6-47(c).


OUTCOME: The court found that the agency's rule that dealt with relocation was an invalid delegation of legislative authority, and reversed in part the judgments in favor of the agency.

 

130 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Club S. Burlesque v. City of Carrollton


S95A0432.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 528; 457 S.E.2d 816; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 366; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 1909



June 5, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CARROLL County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Allen B. Keeble. Date of Judgment Appealed: 10-03-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 10-28-94. Lower Ct # :93V01289.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult entertainment club (club) sought review of the decision of the Carroll County Superior Court (Georgia), which entered an order upholding the constitutionality of a new ordinance and denied the club an injunction against its enforcement.


OVERVIEW: The club brought an action against appellee city and alleged that a new adult entertainment ordinance was unconstitutional and sought declaratory and injunctive relief. The lower court upheld the constitutionality of the ordinance and the court affirmed. The court rejected the club's argument that an ordinance regulating adult entertainment was not content-neutral. The court found that the club agreed to accept the city's responses to interrogatories as the equivalent of sworn testimony and therefore waived its right to cross-examination. The court concluded that there was sufficient unrebutted evidence in those answers to authorize the lower court to find that the city relied on specific studies that it reasonably believed to be relevant to the problems addressed by the ordinance. The court found that the ordinance was not an unconstitutional prior restraint and that the club lacked standing to challenge the different requirements provided for the entertainers. The court determined that the ordinance's provision denying licenses to owners or managers who had been convicted of a felony within the last five years was not overbroad or unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding the constitutionality of the ordinance concerning adult entertainment.

 

131 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Connally v. State


S95A0511.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 563; 458 S.E.2d 336; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 367; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 1925



June 5, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] DOUGLAS County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. David T. Emerson. Date of Judgment Appealed: 10-10-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-04-94. Lower Ct # :CR911367.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Douglas County Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of eight counts of theft by conversion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a trustee of several trusts and took money from those trusts for his personal use. He was convicted of theft by conversion. The court affirmed the convictions. Defendant contended that the sums he took were authorized loans, that he was unable to repay all the money, and that he was being imprisoned for a debt in violation of the constitutional prohibition against imprisonment for debt. The court held that the theft by conversion statute required more than proof of a failure to comply with any contractual obligation. It required proof of criminal intent -- the knowing appropriation of funds or property belonging to another. The court held that because the statute required proof of a criminal intent, it did not violate the constitutional prohibition against imprisonment for debt. The court held further that the evidence supported the convictions and that a rational trier of fact could have found that defendant knowingly converted trust funds to his own use. Finally, the court held that the theft by conversion statute was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of eight counts of theft by conversion.

 

132 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Woodard v. Laurens County


S95A0462.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 404; 456 S.E.2d 581; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 277; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 1763



May 15, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] LAURENS County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. William M. Towson. Date of Judgment Appealed: 10-25-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-22-94. Lower Ct # :931029.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, who were injured in a motor vehicle accident, challenged the decision of the Laurens County Superior Court (Georgia), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, county, county commissioners in their official capacities, and county employees in their official and individual capacities, in the injured parties' action predicated upon allegations of negligent inspection and maintenance of a stop sign at an intersection.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the trial court correctly granted summary judgment in favor of the county and individuals in their official capacities, because sovereign immunity regarding counties was waived only to the extent of the amount of liability insurance purchased for the negligence of county officers and employees arising from the use of a motor vehicle, Ga. Code Ann. § 33-24-51(b), and their liability was not predicated upon their alleged negligent use of an insured motor vehicle. The court held that although the statutory scheme afforded a county broader sovereign immunity from tort liability than it afforded the state, resulting in unequal treatment of plaintiffs, it was not unconstitutional. The court held that the trial court correctly granted summary judgment in favor of the county employees in their individual capacities because they were alleged to have been negligent in their performance of a discretionary act (the establishment of procedures for discovering and removing tree limbs that were obstructing stop signs) and subsection (d) of the 1991 amendment to Ga. Const. art. I, § II, para. IX provided immunity for the negligent performance of discretionary acts.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment in favor of the county, county commissioners, and county employees was affirmed.

 

133 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Stephens v. State


S95A1854.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 356; 456 S.E.2d 560; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 161; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 1144



March 30, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


PRIOR HISTORY: This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of March 17, 1995, Previously Reported at: 1995 Ga. LEXIS 160.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of a trial court (Georgia), which denied defendant's constitutional challenge on racial discrimination grounds of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(d), which provided for life imprisonment on the second conviction of the sale or possession with intent to distribute a controlled substance. The trial court sentenced defendant to two life sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a second time controlled substances offender and the trial court imposed two life sentences upon him pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(d). Defendant argued that the statute as applied discriminated on the basis of race, that the court should infer discriminatory intent from statewide and countywide statistical data on sentences for drug offenders. Defendant conceded that he could not prove any discriminatory intent by the Georgia General Assembly in enacting the law or by the county district attorney in choosing to seek life imprisonment in this case. The court stated that those concessions precluded the court from finding an equal protection violation under the federal and state constitutions. The court affirmed the sentence and held that the statute as applied was constitutional. Defendant failed to present the critical evidence by race concerning the number of persons eligible for life sentences under the statute in the county, but against whom the district attorney did not seek the aggravated sentence. Also, other factors beside race possibly explained the disparity shown by the statistical evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentences imposed on defendant, holding that the challenged sentencing statute did not violate the due process or equal protection clauses of the federal or state constitutions based on the statistical evidence presented by defendant.

Brooks v. Parkerson

DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent parents appealed from an order of the Douglas County Superior Court (Georgia), which denied respondents' motion to dismiss on constitutional grounds petitioner grandparent's request for visitation of respondents' child under the Georgia Grandparent Visitation Statute, O.C.G.A. § 19-7-3.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner grandparent submitted a petition for visitation of her grandchild under Georgia's Grandparent Visitation Statute, O.C.G.A. § 19-7-3. Both respondent parents opposed the petition and filed a motion to dismiss the petition on constitutional grounds. The trial court denied respondents' motion and respondents submitted an application to appeal. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the statute was unconstitutional under the United States and Georgia Constitutions. The court held that the statute impermissibly interfered with respondents liberty and privacy interests to raise their child without state interference because the statute did not clearly promote the health or welfare of the child and did not require a showing of harm before state interference was authorized.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order that denied respondent parents' motion to dismiss petitioner grandparent's petition for visitation of her grandchild under Georgia's Grandparent Visitation Statute. The court held that the statute was unconstitutional under the Georgia and United States Constitutions.

City of Atlanta v. McKinney


S94A1610. S94X1612.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 161; 454 S.E.2d 517; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 151; 19 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 1065; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 905; 67 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 646



March 14, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] FULTON County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Isaac Jenrette. Date of Judgment Appealed: 04-28-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 06-06-94. Lower Ct # :E16763.

FULTON County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Isaac Jenrette. Date of Judgment Appealed: 04-28-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 05-23-94. Lower Ct # :E16763.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part in Case No. S94A1610.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, representative, city council member, city taxpayer and city employees, filed an action against defendants, city and city officials, seeking to have certain city ordinances declared unconstitutional and seeking damages. The Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia) granted partial judgment on the pleadings in favor of the plaintiffs and dismissed plaintiffs' remaining claims. All parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The contested ordinances prohibited discrimination on the basis of sexual orientation in city employment, artist selection, festival admission, licensed alcohol beverage establishments, and vehicles for hire, established a domestic partnership registry for jail visitation, and extended insurance and other employee benefits to domestic partners of city employees. The court found that the trial court erred in declaring the registry ordinance unconstitutional because the law created no legal rights and was a reasonable ordinance related to the city's affairs. The court affirmed the trial court's ruling invalidating the benefits ordinance because the city exceeded it's authority when it defined dependents for benefit purposes to include domestic partners. The city's definition of dependants was inconsistent with state law. The court found that the trial court did not err in dismissing the claim with respect to the anti-discrimination ordinances because the ordinances only affected city employees and property and those businesses that state law allowed the city to regulate and thus the city did not exceed its authority. The court affirmed the dismissal of all damage claims.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's ruling that declared the city's registry ordinance unconstitutional and affirmed the trial court's decisions invalidating the city's benefit ordinance, dismissing the claim with respect to the anti-discrimination ordinances, and dismissing the claims for damages.

Worley v. State


S94A1553.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 251; 454 S.E.2d 461; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 131; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 1311



March 6, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] WHITFIELD County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Charles A. Pannell, Jr., Date of Judgment Appealed: 03-01-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 03-10-94. Lower Ct # :570342.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Whitfield County Superior Court (Georgia), which denied his petition to have his conviction of armed robbery and sentence to life imprisonment declared void.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the sentence provision of the armed robbery statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 16-8-41(b) was unconstitutional on due process grounds. The statute permitted the trial court to sentence a defendant, including a sentence to life imprisonment, upon the judge's discretion. Defendant argued that he should have been given a determinate sentence because he was not a recidivist and, therefore, the trial court was not required to impose a life sentence. The court found that the trial court had the option to oppose a life sentence, even though he was not a recidivist, according to Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-1. Defendant argued that Ga. Code Ann. § 16-8-41(b) was void for vagueness due to the discretionary language. The court found that the language of the sentencing statute was unambiguous and the statute was not invalid because the term of the sentence was made discretionary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence of life imprisonment.

Kevinezz v. State


S94A1583.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 78; 454 S.E.2d 441; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 109; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 763



February 27, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CLAYTON County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Kenneth Kilpatrick. Date of Judgment Appealed: 03-10-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 12-01-93. Lower Ct # :91CR017644.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Clayton County Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted her of vehicular homicide and following too closely.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of vehicular homicide and following too closely, and she appealed. The court held that Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(5) was not unconstitutionally vague and provided adequate notice that a person who ingested marijuana or any other specified drug and then drove a motor vehicle did so at his or her own peril of violating the statute. The court held that the indictment only put defendant on notice that she could be convicted of vehicular homicide if the marijuana or cocaine had made her a less safe driver and did not put her on notice that she could be convicted solely on the physical act of driving with any amount of marijuana or cocaine in her blood or urine under § 40-6-391(a)(5). The court held that defendant did not waive her right to raise the sufficiency of the vehicular homicide indictment by not filing a special demurrer to the indictment. The court held that the evidence supported the conviction for following too closely. The judgment was reversed in part and affirmed in part.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for vehicular homicide and affirmed her conviction for following too closely.

Miller v. Ga. Dep't of Pub. Safety


S94A1230.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 62; 453 S.E.2d 725; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 110; 95 Fulton County D. Rep. 741



February 27, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] FULTON County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Frank M. Eldridge. Date of Judgment Appealed: 03-03-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 03-28-94. Lower Ct # :E16644.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the Georgia Department of Public Safety (DPS), filed a motion to dismiss a direct appeal on the ground that appellant driver was required to file an application to appeal under Ga. Code Ann. § 5-6-35(a) in the driver's action that alleged the DPS mandatory breath test rule was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The driver contended that both Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-67.1(f)(1) and a DPS rule enacted pursuant to it were unconstitutional. As a result of the alleged unconstitutionality of the statute and rule, the driver sought to have the administrative suspension of his driver's license set aside. The trial court dismissed the declaratory judgment action and, in the administrative appeal, the trial court ruled that § 40-5-67.1(f)(1) was constitutional and affirmed the suspension of driver's license. The court affirmed and held that a direct appeal from a ruling on a Ga. Code Ann. § 50-13-10 claim for a declaratory judgment could not be characterized, for the purposes of Ga. Code Ann. § 5-6-35, as essentially an appeal from an agency decision. Thus, a direct appeal was not allowed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court because the court could not review a matter that was not an agency decision.

N. Fulton Medical Ctr. v. Roach


S94A1864.


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


265 Ga. 125; 453 S.E.2d 463; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 92



February 20, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] FULTON County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Frank M. Eldridge. Date of Judgment Appealed: 05-19-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 06-07-94. Lower Ct # :E16116.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant medical center challenged the judgment of the Fulton County Superior Court (Georgia), which, upon remand, denied the medical center's petition for a writ of mandamus against appellee director of a state health planning agency and dismissed the medical center's petition for judicial review of the director's decision that competing hospitals were not required to obtain a certificate of need (CON) to relocate.


OVERVIEW: The medical center argued that the director acted without authority to exempt the hospitals from the CON requirements. The trial court dismissed the medical center's complaint, and on appeal, the court remanded to determine whether judicial review or mandamus was the appropriate remedy. On the morning of the trial, the agency announced that it had adopted Ga. Comp. R. & Regs. r. 272-2-.07(1)(u) (1994), which exempted relocations from CON reviews and validated relocations permitted prior to the adoption of the new rule. The trial court ruled that the medical center's remedy was a declaratory judgment action, denied the medical center's petition for judicial review, and dismissed the petition for mandamus relief. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal of the claim for judicial review. The director's act did not constitute a declaratory ruling because she did not issue the letter pursuant to any rule consistent with Ga. Code Ann. § 50-13-11; thus, judicial review was not available. The court reversed the denial of mandamus relief. Because the medical center did not have an adequate legal remedy at the time it initiated its action, it could raise all challenged to the new rule.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the medical center's petition for judicial review and reversed the denial of mandamus relief and remanded the case to permit the trial court to consider the merits of the medical center's challenged to the new rule.

 

140 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Stevenson v. State


No. S94A1174


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 892; 453 S.E.2d 18; 1995 Ga. LEXIS 62



February 13, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 40-6-391 (a) (5); constitutional question. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Anne Workman. Date of Judgement Appealed: 10-25-93. Notice of Appeal Date: 10-29-93. Lower Ct # :93C114893.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded nolo contendere to being in actual physical control of a moving vehicle at a time when marijuana was present in his urine in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-391(a)(5). Prior to entering the plea, the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) denied defendant's motion to suppress statements and test results. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the statement he made to police should have been suppressed because Miranda warnings were not given. The court rejected defendant's contention, holding that the statement was voluntary and was not made in response to police interrogation or while in police custody. Accordingly, the court held that Miranda warnings were not required. Additionally, the court rejected defendant's challenge to chemical test results. The court held that because the traffic accident in which defendant was involved resulted in serious injury, defendant was deemed by operation of law, pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-55, to have given consent to the chemical test of his bodily substances for the presence of alcohol or drugs. Finally, the court rejected defendant's argument that Ga. Code Ann. § 40-6-3919(a)(5) was unconstitutional because it created an impermissible irrebutable presumption that a person with a trace, no matter how minuscule, of marijuana in his or her system is an unsafe driver. The court held that § 40-6-3919(a)(5) required the state to prove the elements of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt and that those elements did not include impaired driving ability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for being in actual physical control of a moving vehicle at a time when marijuana was present in his urine.

 

141 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Burgess v. State


No. S94P1047


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 777; 450 S.E.2d 680; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 914; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 3985



December 5, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 20, 1994. As Corrected. Second Correction February 2, 1995.
Reconsideration denied by, 12/20/1994
Writ of certiorari denied Burgess v. Georgia, 515 U.S. 1133, 115 S. Ct. 2559, 132 L. Ed. 2d 813, 1995 U.S. LEXIS 3970 (1995)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Burgess v. Terry, 2012 U.S. App. LEXIS 10653 (11th Cir. Ga., May 25, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Douglas Superior Court. Before Judge Robert J. James. Date of Judgment Appealed: 01-31-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 03-07-94. Lower Ct # :CR901002.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for murder and his death sentence in the Douglas Superior Court (Georgia). Defendant argued that the trial erred in not striking certain jurors for cause, and that the trial court erred during the sentencing phase by refusing to instruct the jury that it could not return a death sentence if it found by a preponderance of the evidence that defendant was mentally retarded.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. Defendant sought review of the conviction and death sentence, arguing that inquiry into the issue of his parole eligibility was erroneously restricted on voir dire, that the trial court erred in refusing to strike potential jurors based upon their alleged bias concerning race, that the trial court erred in refusing to strike potential jurors concerning alleged bias in favor of the death penalty, and that the trial court erred by refusing to instruct at the sentencing phase that the jury could not return a death sentence if it found by a preponderance of the evidence that defendant was mentally retarded. The court affirmed defendants' conviction for murder and his death sentence, holding that under Ga. Code Ann. § 17-7-131(3), the factfinder was required to decide at the guilt-innocence phase whether to return a verdict of "guilty but mentally ill." Ga. Code Ann. § 17-7-131(c) required that the defendant prove his mental retardation beyond a reasonable doubt in order to be found "guilty but mentally retarded." Thus, defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction at the sentencing phase concerning mental retardation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and his death sentence. In order for a defendant to receive a verdict of "guilty but mentally retarded," a defendant was required to prove his mental retardation beyond a reasonable doubt. Thus, because the issue of whether defendant was mentally retarded would have been decided in the guilt-innocence phase, he was not entitled to have the jury charged on retardation in the sentencing phase.

 

142 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Quetgles v. City of Columbus


Nos. S94A0918, S94A0927


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 708; 450 S.E.2d 677; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 915; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 3975



December 5, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] City ordinance violation; constitutional question. Appling Superior Court. Before Judge Whisnant from Chattahoochee Circuit. Date of Judgment Appealed: 02-01-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 02-25-94. Lower Ct # :SU93CV3588.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the decision of the Appling Superior Court (Georgia), which dismissed their suit against defendant city challenging as unconstitutional a city ordinance prohibiting private modeling sessions or other sexual displays in one-on-one sessions and close mingling between customers and employees of adult entertainment establishments.


OVERVIEW: Defendant moved to dismiss plaintiffs' freedom of speech case for failure to state a claim on which relief could be granted. On a motion to dismiss under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-12 (b) (6), the pleadings must be construed most favorably for plaintiffs and all doubt resolved in their favor. Plaintiffs' pleadings raised a justiciable issue as to whether defendant's ordinance furthered an important governmental interest unrelated to free speech. In support of its motion to dismiss, the city produced no evidence showing that the ordinance furthered such an interest. Thus it was error to dismiss for failure to state a claim. The grant of the city's motion was reversed and the case remanded.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing plaintiff's case for failure to state a claim was reversed and the case remanded, because it was error to grant summary judgment upholding the constitutionality of an ordinance regulating adult entertainment in the absence of evidence that the ordinance served a governmental interest.

Parking Ass'n v. City of Atlanta


No. S94A0975


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 764; 450 S.E.2d 200; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 899; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 3891



November 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Zoning ordinance; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Elizabeth E. Long. Date of Judgment Appealed: 03-03-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 03-04-94. Lower Ct # :E21249.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, property owners and corporations, appealed from a judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which found in favor of defendant city in a suit seeking a declaration that a zoning ordinance enacted by the city was invalid.


OVERVIEW: The city passed a zoning ordinance that established barrier and landscaping requirements for certain parking lots. However, the property owners and corporations managing the affected parking lots argued that the ordinance exceeded the city's police power and violated constitutional equal protections provisions. On review, the court concluded that the property owners and corporations failed to prove that the ordinance presented a significant detriment to them. In reaching its conclusion, the court held that the loss of, at most, three percent of the spaces on the affected parking lots did not constitute a significant deprivation of property. Additionally, the court held that the property owners and corporations failed to prove that the ordinance was not substantially related to the public health, safety, and welfare. The court held that the ordinance did not violate equal protection rights because it bore a fair and substantial relation to the object of the ordinance and furnished a legitimate ground of differentiation between affected and non-affected parking lots.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that upheld the validity of a zoning ordinance passed by the city.

N. Ga. Elec. Mbrshp. Corp. v. City of Calhoun


No. S94A1009


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 769; 450 S.E.2d 410; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 902; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 3897



November 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Franchise fee; constitutional question. Gordon Superior Court. Before Judge Tom Pope. Date of Judgment Appealed: 01-12-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 02-08-94. Lower Ct. # :27616.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility challenged an order of the Gordon Superior Court (Georgia), which granted summary judgment to appellee city on the utility's action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief against the city's collection of a business tax.


OVERVIEW: A city ordinance imposed a gross receipts tax on the revenues of each secondary supplier of electric power within the city. The utility refused to pay the tax, claiming that as a franchise of the Tennessee Valley Authority (TVA) it was exempt under 16 U.S.C.S. § 831(1). The court affirmed summary judgment for the city, holding that although the Tennessee Valley Act authorized TVA to enter into contracts with states, counties, municipalities, corporations, partnerships, or individuals for the sale of its surplus electric power, it did not authorize TVA to grant franchises. Thus cooperatives, such as the utility, were never intended to be exempted from state and local taxation. The court held that the utility's contractual relationship with the TVA to distribute electric power purchased by it from TVA did not render it a instrumentality of the United States government that was exempted from taxation by state and local authorities by the Supremacy Clause. The city's ordinance did not violate the uniformity requirements of Ga. Const. art. VII, § 1, cl. 3 (1983) because the classification of businesses based upon the payment of another tax or franchise fee was not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment for the city in the utility's action for declaratory and injunctive relief from the collection of a business tax.

 

145 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



In the Interest of B. L. S.


No. S94A1035


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 643; 449 S.E.2d 823; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 888; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 3737



November 21, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Statutory rape. Rockdale Superior Court. Before Judge Lavigno, pro hac vice. Date of Judgment Appealed: 09-03-93. Notice of Appeal Date:10-01-93. Lower Ct # :12293121B



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Rockdale Superior Court (Georgia), which found him delinquent by reason of his commission of an act of statutory rape in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-3.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a motion to recuse the juvenile court judge because the judge was engaged in the private practice of criminal law in other courts. Another juvenile court judge denied the motion. Thereafter, the juvenile court found appellant delinquent. On appeal, the court affirmed. It found that § 16-6-3 did not deprive appellant of equal protection of the law, and thus it was not invalid because a female "child" under the age of 17 who engaged in sexual intercourse with a male under the age of 14 was subject to the same delinquency adjudication as appellant. It also found that there was sufficient evidence to authorize the juvenile court, as the trier of fact, to find proof beyond a reasonable doubt that, in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-6-3, appellant had engaged in sexual intercourse with an under-age female who was not his spouse because the female's testimony showed that an act of sexual intercourse occurred. Further, it found that appellant's motion was properly denied because the motion stated no viable grounds for the recusal or disqualification of the judge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the juvenile court's judgment that found appellant delinquent by reason of his commission of an act of statutory rape.

 

146 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Gilbert v. Richardson


No. S94G0735


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 744; 452 S.E.2d 476; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 892; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 3818



November 21, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 211 Ga. App. 795. WALKER County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Jon B. Wood. Date of Judgment Appealed: 02-02-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 02-10-94. Lower Ct # :A93A2221.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff accident victims brought an action against defendants, county sheriff and his deputy sheriff, seeking damages for injuries sustained in an automobile collision with the deputy sheriff while she was responding to an emergency call. The Court of Appeals of Georgia affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the county sheriff and the deputy sheriff. The accident victims sought a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Victims of an automobile collision claimed that sovereign immunity was waived as to both the county sheriff and the deputy sheriff. The court found that official immunity banned the accident victims' claims against the deputy sheriff because she was performing an official discretionary function when the accident occurred and was immune from personal liability under Ga. Const. art. I, § II, para. IX (a), (e) (amended 1991). The court reasoned that the county's purchase of liability coverage constituted the purchase of insurance as contemplated by O.C.G.A. § 33-24-51(b). The court held that sovereign immunity was waived to the extent of liability insurance coverage provided by the county's participation in the Georgia Interlocal Risk Management Agency. The court held that because the county sheriff was being sued in his official capacity, he was entitled to the benefit of the county's sovereign immunity defense. Because, however, the county had waived sovereign immunity to the extent of its liability insurance coverage, the county sheriff's sovereign immunity defense was likewise waived to that extent.


OUTCOME: The affirmance of the entry of summary judgment in favor of the deputy sheriff was affirmed, but the affirmance of summary judgment in favor of the county sheriff was reversed because the sheriff's sovereign immunity defense had been waived.

Lee v. City of Villa Rica


No. S94A0885


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 606; 449 S.E.2d 295; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 871; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 3573



November 7, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Election qualification; constitutional question. Carroll Superior Court. Before Judge Smith. Date of Judgment Appealed: 01-27-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 02-07-94. Lower Ct #:A93A2098



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mayor appealed a judgment from the Carroll Superior Court (Georgia), which ruled that local legislation passed by defendant city that rendered the mayor ineligible to continue in office was constitutional and ordered the mayor to vacate his position.


OVERVIEW: The mayor was qualified for his office when he was elected. During his term the city de-annexed the area where the mayor resided, which rendered him ineligible for his office because he no longer resided in the city. The city called for his removal from office. The mayor filed a petition for declaratory judgment and sought an injunction against the effort to remove him from office. The trial court ruled in favor of the city. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that: (1) the de-annexation statute was not an unconstitutional bill of attainder because it neither singled out the mayor nor punished him as an officeholder; (2) Ga. Code Ann. § 1-3-11 and its requirement of a local referendum was not applicable because the de-annexation act neither abolished the office of mayor nor shortened or lengthened the term of office; and (3) the mayor's failure to raise an objection to the procedure before the trial court and his acquiescence in the procedure used, precluded him from asserting on appeal that improper procedure was followed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that the city's de-annexation legislation was constitutional and the order for the mayor to vacate his position.

Love v. Whirlpool Corp.


Nos. S94A0781, S94A0783, S94A0784, S94A0830


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 701; 449 S.E.2d 602; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 877; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P14,083



November 7, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Langham. Date of Judgment Appealed: 11-03-93. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-30-93. Lower Ct # :D8099.

FULTON County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Don A. Langham. Date of Judgment Appealed: 11-03-93. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-30-93. Lower Ct # :E8100.

FULTON County Superior. Trial Judge: Hon. Don A. Langham. Date of Judgment Appealed: 11-03-93. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-30-93. Lower Ct # :E8098



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant consumer sought review of a judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), granting summary judgment to appellee manufacturers, upholding the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 51-1-11, a statute of repose for strict products liability actions, and ruling that the statute barred the consumer's actions notwithstanding the provisions of the renewal statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 9-2-61(a).


OVERVIEW: The consumer filed four actions seeking to recover for his injuries and for the wrongful deaths of his wife and two sons and for their respective pain and suffering from a fire allegedly caused either by a defective electric clothes dryer or by a defect in the power cord or both. The manufacturers filed motions for summary judgment contending that the actions, filed more than 10 years after the stipulated sale date of the dryer and cord, were barred by the statute of repose, Ga. Code Ann. § 51-1-11. The consumer filed a motion to declare § 51-1-11 unconstitutional. In an order made applicable to all four cases, the trial court upheld the constitutionality of the statute and ruled that the statute barred the actions. The court affirmed. The court found that the consumer was not a member of a suspect class and applied the "rational basis" test. The court held that the consumer did not sustain his burden of showing that the 10-year limitation was arbitrary and that it did not further a legitimate state interest. The court held that the trial court did not err in ruling that the consumer lacked standing to challenge "disease " exceptions to the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment, which was entered in favor of the manufacturers and upheld the constitutionality of the statute of repose for strict products liability actions.

Thornton v. State

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with malice murder, three counts of felony murder, cruelty to children, and aggravated battery, and the jury found him guilty. The Douglas Superior Court (Georgia) imposed four death sentences and a prison term, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lived with his girlfriend and her children. The state claimed that the videotaped testimony was admissible under the Child Hearsay Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 24-3-16. Defendant claimed that the videotaped testimony was improperly admitted. The court held that the admission of the videotaped testimony was reversible error. The court ruled that the evidence was inadmissible because the requirement of § 24-3-16 that the statement describe abuse inflicted upon the declarant himself was not satisfied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court.

E. W. Express v. Collins


Nos. S94A1040, S94X1041


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 774; 449 S.E.2d 599; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 864; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 3581



October 31, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsiderations Denied December 2, 1994 and December 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  O.C.G.A. § 48-5-442 et seq. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Isaac Jenrette. Date of Judgment Appealed: 01-14-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 02-09-94. Lower Ct # :D96743.

Trial Judge: Hon. Isaac Jenrette. Date of Judgment Appealed: 01-14-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 02-11-94. Lower Ct # :D96743.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. S94A1040 and reversed in Case No. S94X1041.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff carrier's action against defendant State Revenue Commissioner, seeking a declaratory judgment holding Ga. Code Ann. §§ 48-5-442 to 48-5-445, 48-5-471 unconstitutional because they did not provide for apportionment of ad valorem taxes on motor vehicles engaged in interstate commerce, the carrier challenged the judgment of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which awarded summary judgment to the commissioner.


OVERVIEW: The carrier, which provided interstate trucking services with vehicles registered and titled in Georgia, sought a declaratory judgment that §§ 48-5-442 to 48-5-445, 48-5-471 were unconstitutional. The trial court granted the commissioner's motion for summary judgment. Both parties appealed, with the commissioner arguing that the trial court erred in finding that the power to apportion those taxes was vested in the commissioner. The court affirmed the judgment as to the carrier's appeal, holding that the carrier, as owner of motor vehicles used in interstate commerce could have obtained apportionment of ad valorem taxes on such a motor vehicle by demonstrating to the local taxing authority, in an appeal under Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-311 challenging the assessed value of the vehicles, that the vehicles had acquired a tax situs in one or more other states. The court reversed the trial court's ruling as to the commissioner's appeal, holding that it was the local taxing authority to whom motor vehicle owners had to demonstrate the acquisition of a foreign tax situs and the degree to which the valuation of the vehicle was to have been adjusted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's ruling that the ad valorem tax scheme challenged by the carrier was not unconstitutional, but reversed on the trial court's ruling that the commissioner was vested with the power to apportion those taxes.

 

151 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. S94A1319


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 590; 449 S.E.2d 94; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 870; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 3502



October 31, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. §§ 16-5-90, 16-5-91; constitutional question. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Robinson. Date of Judgment Appealed: 04-18-94. Notice of Appeal Date: 02-22-94. Lower Ct #:939327505



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted defendant of misdemeanor stalking and burglary, the intended felony being aggravated stalking.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with misdemeanor stalking and burglary. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the indictments, alleging that Ga. Code Ann. §§ 16-5-90, 16-5-91 were unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The motions were denied, and defendant was convicted. On appeal, the court affirmed and determined that that §§ 16-5-90, 16-5-91 were not vague because they gave a person of ordinary intelligence notice of the conduct that was prohibited. Moreover, §§ 16-5-90, 16-5-91 were not overbroad because they did not reach a substantial amount of constitutionally protected conduct. Sections 16-5-90, 16-5-91 did not prohibit the act of merely communicating with another person, but prohibited such contact if it was done for a "harassing and intimidating" purpose. The restrict on communication was limited to "harassing and intimidating" contact that was "knowing and willful." This action was not protected by the First Amendment. Moreover, the legislature was permitted to define "harassing and intimidating" conduct more broadly than the making of "an overt threat of death or bodily harm" or the causing of substantial "emotional distress."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for misdemeanor stalking and burglary.

Reed v. State


No. S94A0862


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 466; 448 S.E.2d 189; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 770



September 21, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 16-12-100; constitutional question. Hall Superior Court. Before Judge Girardeau. Date of Judgment Appealed: 10-27-93. Notice of Appeal Date: 01-31-94. Lower Court #:93CR405C



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Hall Superior Court (Georgia), which denied defendant's motion to dismiss an indictment for unconstitutionality charging him with attempted sexual exploitation of a child, in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-12-100(b)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with attempted sexual exploitation of a child, in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-12-100(b)(1) for conduct involving a 17-year-old married female. Defendant filed a motion to dismissed the indictment on constitutional grounds, which was denied. The superior court certified its order for immediate review and an application for interlocutory appeal was granted to consider whether the statute violated the equal protection clause of the Georgia Constitution and the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that Ga. Code Ann. § 16-12-100 did not violate defendant's right to equal protection because defendant was not similarly situated to other defendants charged with crimes under other statutes with different age limits. The court determined that because the statute applied equally to all those accused under it, there were no disparate classifications among similarly situated persons. Because defendant failed to satisfy a threshold obligation to show disparate treatment, the court did not consider whether the statute was rationally related to a legitimate state interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment.

Daniels v. State


No. S94G0362


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 460; 448 S.E.2d 185; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 772



September 21, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 211 Ga. App. 23. CLARKE County. Trial Judge: Honorable N. Kent Lawrence. Date of Judgment Appealed: 11-19-93. Notice of Appeal Date: 11-29-93. Lower Ct #:A93A1017, ST92M1154



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals of Georgia, which affirmed his conviction and sentence for violation of the Anti-Mask Act (Act), Ga. Code Ann. § 16-11-38.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after being stopped by a police officer for wearing a mask. Prior to being stopped, defendant was entertaining children in the area with his mask. On appeal, the court reversed defendant's conviction and found that the evidence at trial was not sufficient to prove that defendant had the requisite culpability or intent for conviction. The court found that defendant was attempting to playfully "scare" the children, as opposed to attempting to frighten or intimidate the children. The court noted that defendant's actions were tantamount to the actions of a person on Halloween and the Act excepted this type of conduct. The court further found that defendant's intention to entertain was beyond the purview of the Act. The court stated that the standard "reasonably should know" regarding the accused's state of mind in relation to the Act was inapplicable and the standard should encompass the requirements of intention or criminal negligence. The court applied this standard and found that defendant did not act with reckless disregard of consequences or heedless indifference to the rights and safety of the children as would have been required for conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for violation of the Anti Mask Act.
