Livingston v. State


Nos. S94A0277, S94A0279, S94A0280


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 402; 444 S.E.2d 748; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 476; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 2234



June 27, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsiderations Denied July 21, 1994.
Subsequent appeal at Waldrip v. State, 266 Ga. 874, 471 S.E.2d 857, 1996 Ga. LEXIS 477 (1996)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Waldrip v. Humphrey, 2013 U.S. App. LEXIS 17492 (11th Cir. Ga., Aug. 21, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Interim appellate review. Dawson Superior Court. Before Judge Girardeau. Date of Judgment Appealed: 10-28-93. Lower Ct # :91CR300C



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a death penalty case, defendants contested orders of the Dawson County Superior Court (Georgia), which denied the first defendant's challenges regarding the admission of victim impact evidence under Ga. Code Ann. § 17-101.2 and his motion for a separate trial, denied the second defendant's motion to enjoin the victim's family from showing emotion at trial, and denied the third defendant's motion to suppress the discovery of the victims body.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the Eighth Amendment prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment did not bar the introduction of all victim impact evidence, and that such evidence could be admissible if it was not inflammatory or unduly prejudicial. The court ruled that Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-1.2 was not unconstitutional because it contained sufficient safeguards against the admission of evidence that would "unduly prejudice" a jury. The court instituted procedures for trial courts to follow to ensure that victim impact evidence did not result in the arbitrary imposition of the death penalty. The denial of a separate trial for the first defendant was not error because the jury in a capital trial determined a whether a defendant was mentally retarded in the guilt phase of the trial. The trial court appropriately instructed the victim's family to avoid any visible or audible display of emotion in the courtroom. The third defendant's statement to the agents was admissible because it was voluntary when there was no evidence of coercive police activity. The discovery of the victim's body did not need to be suppressed because it was the "fruit" of the third defendant's voluntary statement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders denying defendants' motions.

Franklin v. Hill


No. S94A0235


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 302; 444 S.E.2d 778; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 478; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 2225



June 27, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended June 27, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 51-1-16; constitutional question. Gwinnett Superior Court. Before Judge Winegarden. Date of Judgment Appealed: 07-01-93. Notice of Appeal Date:07-30-93. Lower Ct # :88A36965



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Gwinnett Superior Court (Georgia) granted summary judgment to defendant teacher in plaintiff mother's action against him for violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 51-1-16 on the ground that § 51-1-16 violated the equal protection clauses of the Georgia and United States Constitution. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother filed an action against the teacher, alleging that he had violated the seduction statute, § 51-1-16, by seducing her teenage daughter. Because only men could have been liable under § 51-1-16 for seducing unwed daughters, the teacher claimed that § 51-1-16 violated the equal protection clauses of the Georgia and United States Constitutions. The trial court agreed and granted the teacher summary judgment. On appeal, the court found that § 51-1-16 was unconstitutional because it contained gender-based classifications which violated the equal protection clauses of the Georgia and United States Constitutions. The court found that the gender-based classification was not justified by an important governmental purpose because § 51-1-16 was not substantially related to such a purpose. The court found that although the prevention of unwanted pregnancies was an important governmental purpose, § 51-1-16 was not substantially related to that goal because it had no age limitation, such as restricting the claim to parents of minor children, it did not give a cause of action to the affected woman, only her parents, and it covered seductions whether or not they resulted in pregnancy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment to the teacher.

Bd. of Tax Assessors v. Tom's Foods


No. S94A0602


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 309; 444 S.E.2d 771; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 467; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 2137



June 27, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 48-5-18; constitutional question. Muscogee Superior Court. Before Judge Followill. Date of Judgment Appealed: 11-24-93. Notice of Appeal Date: 12-14-93.Lower Ct # :88C45183



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Tax Assessors (Board) found that appellee taxpayer's return was untimely and denied a tax exemption to the taxpayer. The board of equalization affirmed the board's decision. The Muscogee Superior Court (Georgia) reversed the board of equalization, and the taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The governing authority for the consolidated city and county government established March 1 as the closing date for tax returns. The Board established a policy that any return postmarked after March 1 would be considered untimely. The Board found that the taxpayer's return, postmarked on March 3, was untimely. On appeal, the court ruled in favor of the taxpayer. The court held that pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-18(a), the Board was unauthorized to close its books earlier than April 1. Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-18(a) provided that, subject to certain exceptions, each tax commissioner and tax receiver shall close his books on April 1 of each year. The court held that the exception relied on by the Board, Ga. Code Ann. § 48-5-18(e), was not applicable because the county was not a county within the scope of that subsection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court entered in favor of the taxpayer.

Rower v. State


No. S94A0612


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 323; 443 S.E.2d 839; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 446; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 1892



June 6, 1994, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Kreeger. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 01-10-94. LOWER CT # :939062418



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was to be tried in the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia) for murder. The court granted defendant's application for interim appeal pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-35.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in denying his motion to bar the state from seeking the death penalty against him and in granting the state's demand for the names, addresses, and written reports of his expert witnesses. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment with direction. Furthermore, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to bar the death penalty on the basis of the district attorney's alleged abuse of prosecutorial discretion in the use of plea bargaining because absent a showing that the district attorney acted in an unconstitutional manner with respect to his case, defendant could not inquire into the prosecutor's exercise of discretion in seeking the death penalty against him. The court concluded that, with regard to scientific reports, the state was entitled to only those discovery rights specifically granted to defendant by Ga. Code Ann. § 17-7-211.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment with respect to defendant's murder trial with direction.

State v. Burch


No. S94A0547


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 231; 443 S.E.2d 483; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 434; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 1817



May 31, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 16-11-36; constitutional question. DeKalb State Court. Before Judge Johnson, pro hac vice. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 09-29-93. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 10-07-93. LOWER CT # :93C145802



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment of the DeKalb State Court (Georgia), which dismissed an accusation charging defendant with violating Ga. Code Ann. § 16-11-36, on the ground that the statute was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with loitering or prowling in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-11-36 after he was seen scaling a fence around an automobile dealership. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the charge, arguing that § 16-11-36 was unconstitutionally vague and gave too much discretion to the arresting officer. The court reiterated that § 16-11-36 made clear to persons of ordinary intelligence the conduct sought to be prohibited, and contained sufficient safeguards to prevent unwarranted arrests and convictions. The court therefore reaffirmed its holding that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague and reversed the trial court's dismissal of the charge against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment dismissing the accusation charging defendant with loitering or prowling.

 

159 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



U. S. Anchor Mfg. v. Rule Indus.


No. S94Q0409


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 295; 443 S.E.2d 833; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 426; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 1682; 1994-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P70,664



May 16, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 24, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certified question from the United States Court of Appeals for the Eleventh Circuit. JUDICIAL INQUIRY. LOWER CT # :918854



DISPOSITION: Certified questions answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Court of Appeals for the Eleventh Circuit certified questions of law regarding plaintiff's state law claims for conspiracy in restraint of trade and intentional interference with business relations and the effect of a general release on liability for injury caused by subsequent acts.


OVERVIEW: Defendant brought suit against plaintiff alleging infringement of trademarks and copyrights. Parties executed a settlement, including a release. Later, plaintiff brought suit, alleging federal law violations by conspiracy to monopolize the U.S. market for light weight fluke-style anchors for small boats by below-cost pricing intended to drive out competition, and state law claims. The lower court granted judgment to defendant on the federal claims; as to the state law claims, questions of law were certified regarding conspiracy in restraint of trade and intentional interference with business relations. The court held that: (1) a release did not discharge liability for an injury caused by a subsequent acts; (2) in order to discharge liability for already committed but unknown tortious conduct, a general release had to so specify; and (3) below-cost pricing by a single defendant was not improper in the absence of an unlawful element and, thus, was not encompassed by the tort of intentional interference with business relations.


OUTCOME: The court held that: (1) a release did not discharge liability for subsequent acts; (2) to discharge liability for unknown tortious conduct, a general release had to so specify; and (3) defendant's below-cost pricing was not improper without an unlawful element and was not encompassed by the intentional interference with business relations tort.

 

160 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Nagel v. State


No. S94A0203


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 150; 442 S.E.2d 446; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 399; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 1520



May 2, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Troup Superior Court. Before Judge Keeble. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 08-19-93. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 09-01-93. LOWER CT # :893179



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant murderer sought review of the decision of the Troup Superior Court (Georgia) which, on remand, denied the murderer's application for release from civil commitment under Ga. Code Ann. § 17-7-131(f), after he was acquitted by reason of insanity of the murder of his grandparents.


OVERVIEW: The murderer was tried before a jury for the murder of his grandparents, but he was acquitted by reason of his insanity. The trial court, finding that he met the criteria for civil commitment set forth in Ga. Code Ann. § 37-3-1(9.1) placed him in the custody of the Department of Human Resources. Pursuant to Ga. Code Ann. § 17-7-131(f), he filed an application for his release from civil commitment which was, initially and on remand, denied. The court affirmed and held that the murders of his grandparents were not the only violent acts which he had ever committed and that the evidence supported the finding that he exhibited a steady pattern of violent behavior which culminated in his murder, while insane, of the only people who were willing to love him and give him a home. Further, neither of the murderer's experts held the opinion that he had recovered from being mentally ill. Rather, both were of the opinion that he had never been mentally ill. However, the jury's verdict acquitting him by reason of insanity was res judicata and thus, the murderer failed to prove by a preponderance of evidence that he was no longer insane and should be released from civil commitment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the murderer's application for release.

 

161 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Brophy v. McCranie


No. S94A0603


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 187; 442 S.E.2d 230; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 289; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 1323



April 18, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended May 16, 1994. Reconsideration Denied May 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Quo warranto. Dodge Superior Court. Before Judge Lawson. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 12-21-93. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 12-21-93. LOWER CT # :93V3158



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a hospital authority and trustees challenged a decision of the Dodge Superior Court (Georgia), which ruled in favor of appellee county commissioner on his quo warranto action seeking a declaration that seven of the nine trustees of a hospital authority were holding office illegally, and challenging the constitutionality of a local act.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that the trustees held office illegally because each had been appointed to succeed himself in violation of a 1969 county resolution prohibiting succession without a break of 12 months. In reversing the trial court's decision concerning whether the trustees legally held office, the court held that the 1969 resolution was an invalid attempt to alter by "home rule" the provisions of the Hospital Authorities Law. Under Ga. Code Ann. § 31-7-72(c), appointments to fill vacancies on boards of hospital authorities were governed by the terms of a resolution adopted prescribing the manner by which vacancies were filled, unless changed by local legislation or constitutional amendment. The commissioner asserted that the "resolution" referred to in § 31-7-72 was the resolution of the county commissioner, but the court held that the "resolution" referred to was that of the hospital authority's board. The General Assembly had not changed the law to grant the local governing authority power to change the method of appointments to fill vacancies on hospital authority boards.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order insofar as it held that the trustees were not legal holders of their offices, and affirmed the trial court's order regarding the unconstitutionality of the local act.

Freeman v. State


No. S93A1574


Supreme Court of Georgia


264 Ga. 27; 440 S.E.2d 181; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 108; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 752



February 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 18, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Interim appellate review. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Stoddard. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 07-16-93. LOWER CT # :929395624



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought interim appellate review in his death penalty case of orders of the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia). Defendant was to be tried for an indictment for murder and armed robbery. The principal issues on appeal involved the state's proposed use of similar transaction evidence, the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-16 that provided for a sentence of life without parole, and the propriety of a change of venue.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was to be tried for murder and the armed robbery of a store. Defendant had been convicted of murder and armed robbery of another store and the armed robbery of a restaurant, and was indicted for the murder and armed robbery of another restaurant. The court affirmed the trial court's ruling permitting the state to present evidence of such convictions and of the pending indictment for murder and armed robbery of the restaurant, holding that there was sufficient evidence that defendant committed each of the independent crimes, and sufficient similarity between the independent crimes and the crime for which defendant was currently to be tried. The court affirmed the ruling that Ga. OUTCOME: In defendant's interim appeal from rulings in his death penalty case for murder and armed robbery, the court affirmed the trial court's ruling approving the state's use of similar transaction evidence and declaring the constitutionality of the life-without-parole statute. The court reversed the trial court's ruling granting defendant a change of venue for defendant's trial on other indictments.

Crowe v. Humana, Inc.


No. S93A1371


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 833; 439 S.E.2d 654; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 75; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 400



February 7, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 25, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Bonner, pro hac vice. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 03-10-93. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 03-18-93. LOWER CT # :92VS0053029C



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents sought review of an order of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia) that dismissed their medical malpractice complaint against defendants, hospital and health care providers. The parents brought the action on their own behalf and on behalf of their daughter (child). The trial court found that the cause of action was time barred by Ga. Code Ann. § 9-3-73(b).


OVERVIEW: When she was one year old, the child suffered fever, seizures, and respiratory distress. She was taken to the hospital and treated by the health care workers. An oxygen deficiency caused permanent brain damage, and more than six years after the child was treated, the parents filed this medical malpractice action. The complaint alleged that the parents did not discover that the hospital and health care workers had been negligent until one month prior to filing of the complaint. Ga. Code Ann. § 9-3-71(b) (statute) provided that if a minor was less than five years old when a cause of action for medical malpractice "arose," the minor had two years from her fifth birthday to bring a medical malpractice action. The parents argued that their cause of action "arose," and that the period of limitation commenced, when they discovered that negligence caused the child's injuries. In affirming the trial court, the appellate court held that initiating the period of limitation when the alleged negligence was first discovered was contrary to the plain language of the statute. The court also held that the statute, as construed, was rational and constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing the medical malpractice complaint brought by the parents against the hospital and health care providers.

Davis v. Shavers


Nos. S93A1616, S93X1734, S93A1617, S93X1735, S93A1618, S93X1736


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 785; 439 S.E.2d 650; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 78; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 482



February 7, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Election contest. Catoosa Superior Court. Before Judge Pannell from Conasauga Circuit.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged a decision of the Catoosa Superior Court (Georgia), which ruled that their recall application in an election contest action against appellee city officials was legally insufficient to support a recall. The city officials filed a cross appeal, claiming that Ga. Code Ann. § 21-4-3, which allowed for a recall for malfeasance while they were in office, was unconstitutionally overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Appellants sought the recall as a result of alleged acts of misconduct and malfeasance by the city officials while they were in office. After the election superintendent issued applications for recall petitions, appellees sought review with the trial court, which determined that the recall applications filed by appellants were legally insufficient to justify a recall. On appeal, the court affirmed the ruling of the trial court and held that appellants' application failed to clearly state the facts supporting the grounds for a recall. The court noted that there was nothing within the recall application to allow the public to determine that the facts alleged by appellants, even if true, actually amounted to acts of malfeasance by the city officials. However, the court rejected the city officials' cross appeal alleging that the statute allowing for a recall denied them due process by prohibiting a hearing to determine the truth of the allegations made in the recall application. The court also rejected the city officials' claim that Ga. Code Ann. § 21-4-3(7)(b)(i), which allowed a recall on the grounds of an "act of malfeasance while in office," was unconstitutionally overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court ruling that appellants' recall application against the city officials was legally insufficient. The court rejected the city officials' cross-appeal that the law allowing for a recall based on malfeasance, while in office, was unconstitutionally overbroad.

O S Adver. Co. v. Rubin


No. S93A1973


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 761; 438 S.E.2d 907; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 53; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 323



January 31, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Zoning; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Jenrette. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 07-15-93. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 09-02-93. LOWER CT # :D93176



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant advertising company challenged the ruling of the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which upheld the decision of appellee board of zoning appeals to deny a building permit to the advertising company, after the board determined that its outdoor sign exceeded the limits imposed by Atlanta, Ga., City Code §§ 16-14.010(d) and 16-28.019(7).


OVERVIEW: An advertising company put up a sign that exceeded the limits imposed by Atlanta, Ga., City Code §§ 16-14.010(d) and 16-28.019(7). The board of zoning appeals found that the sign exceeded the Code's limits and denied the advertising company's application, filed after the fact, for a building permit to erect the sign. The advertising company challenged the board's denial in superior court; it alleged that the board misapplied the Code and that the Code violated the advertising company's constitutional rights. The superior court affirmed the board's denial; it held that the Code was correctly applied and that the constitutional claims were premature because the advertising company had not exhausted its administrative remedies. On the advertising company's appeal, the court affirmed on the merits but reversed on the constitutional issues. Clearly, the superior court correctly found that the board did not act arbitrarily or capriciously in enforcing the Code. But only when a constitutional challenge arose about features unique to the challenger's property did the exhaustion rule apply. In this case, fair notice to the board was adequate to sustain the constitutional challenge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the superior court's ruling that supported the zoning board's decision on the merits and held that the board did not act arbitrarily or capriciously when it denied the building permit. The court reversed the part of the superior court's ruling that dismissed the advertising company's constitutional challenge to the city's sign code.

Douglas v. State


No. S93A1553


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 748; 438 S.E.2d 361; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 51; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 238



January 24, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 19-8-24; constitutional question. Crisp Superior Court. Before Judge Forrester from Cordele Circuit. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 05-28-93. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 06-22-93. LOWER CT # :90R504



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Crisp Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted her, following her conditional plea of guilty, of inducing a mother to part with her child in violation of Ga. Code Ann. § 19-8-24(a)(2) by purchasing a used car for the mother of the child in exchange for physical custody or control of the child. The trial court had denied a motion to dismiss based on the alleged unconstitutional vagueness of § 19-8-24(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted that she purchased a car for the mother of the child and that the mother subsequently gave her the child. Defendant was charged under § 19-8-24(a)(2). The mother filed a motion to dismiss based upon constitutional vagueness grounds. The trial court denied the motion and permitted defendant to enter a conditional guilty plea. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. The court rejected the constitutional challenge because § 19-8-24(a)(2) was sufficiently clear to advise an ordinary person of the conduct proscribed. Defendant's claim that the failure to define "inducement" or "parting with their children" in § 19-8-24(a)(2) created vagueness was without merit because vagueness had to apply to defendant's circumstances and was not tested in the abstract. The term "inducement" was sufficiently defined by § 19-8-24(a) as any financial assistance other than payment of the pregnancy and birth medical expenses. The court found that the language was sufficient to warn defendant that offering an automobile in exchange for the child was proscribed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which convicted defendant of inducing a mother to part with her child.

Collins v. Morris


Nos. S93A1311, S93A1341


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 734; 438 S.E.2d 896; 1994 Ga. LEXIS 52; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 319



January 24, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 21-4-6; constitutional question. Polk Superior Court. Before Judge Matthews from Rome Circuit. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 04-15-93. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 04-29-93. LOWER CT # :93CV107



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant elected city council members challenged the decision of the Polk Superior Court (Georgia), which, in two cases, ruled that the revised recall application of appellee electorate was legally sufficient and determined that the Recall Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 21-4-1 et seq., was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The first petition of the electorate for recall of the city council members was deemed legally insufficient by the trial court. A revised application was found to be legally sufficient. Subsequent to the rulings, the city council members brought a separate declaratory action attacking the constitutionality of the Act. On appeal, the court affirmed the decisions. The court recognized that an elected city official had a property interest in his office that could only be taken by procedures meeting due process requirements. However, the electorate's right of recall was a substantial right. The court held that because judicial review was limited solely to a review of the legal sufficiency of the recall grounds, the Act was constitutional because it afforded adequate due process protection to the public official. If one or more of the statutory grounds for recall set forth in Ga. Code Ann. § 21-4-3(7)(B) were alleged in the recall application, then the grounds for recall were legally sufficient. Also, the trial court correctly held that its mere determination of the legal insufficiency of the first recall petition did not bar the revised application under res judicata.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the constitutionality of the Act and the determination of the legal sufficiency of the revised application for a recall petition.

Riley v. H & H Operations


No. S93A1164


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 652; 436 S.E.2d 659; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 1177; 94 Fulton County D. Rep. 95



December 3, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 16, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Action for damages; constitutional question. Clayton Superior Court. Before Judge Benefield.
Riley v. H & H Operations, 1993 Ga. LEXIS 816 (Ga., Dec. 3, 1993)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorist sought review of a summary judgment entered by the Clayton Superior Court (Georgia) in favor of appellee corporation in the motorist's personal injury action based on the corporation's sale of liquor to a minor.


OVERVIEW: A motorist filed a personal injury claim against a corporation after he was involved in an automobile accident caused by a minor who purchased alcohol at one of the corporation's convenience stores. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the corporation. On appeal, the court found constitutional Ga. Code Ann. § 51-1-40, which insulated purveyors of alcoholic beverages from liability to third persons, but reversed summary judgment. In an exception for sale to minors who would soon be driving, the statute gave sufficient notice that the corporation could be held liable for injuries occurring four and one-half hours after the sale of alcohol to a minor. A construction of the statute requiring actual knowledge that a minor would soon be driving would render it an ineffective sanction, because only when a defendant admitted its own knowledge could a plaintiff prevail. Because the corporation's evidence reflected only that its employee did not remember selling alcohol to the minor, the corporation failed to show that no genuine issue of material fact remained as to its constructive knowledge of the sale of alcohol or its knowledge that the minor would soon be driving.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment in favor of a corporation in a motorist's personal injury action based on the corporation's sale of liquor to a minor.

172 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State v. Moseley


S93A1129


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


263 Ga. 680; 436 S.E.2d 632; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 799; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 4131; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,844



November 22, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] FULTON County State. TRIAL JUDGE: Honorable A. L. Thompson. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 03-08-93. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 03-16-93. LOWER CT # :90V6276



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellees were awarded $ 101 million dollars in punitive damages in a products liability action against an automotive corporation, the state relied on Ga. Code Ann. § 51-12-5.1(e)(2) to request 75 percent of such award. Based upon a motion filed by appellees, the trial court (Georgia) found § 51-12-5.1(e)(2) to be unconstitutional. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellees brought a products liability action against an automotive corporation. When the jury awarded appellees $ 101 million dollars in punitive damages, the state sought 75 percent of the award pursuant to § 51-12-5.1(e)(2). The trial court refused to apply the statute. The court reversed, holding that § 51-12-5.1(e)(2) was applicable and constitutional. The statute did not violate equal protection or the "Takings" clauses of the United States and Georgia Constitutions. Because it was not a revenue raising measure, § 51-12-5.1(e)(2) also did not violate Ga. Const. art. 3, § 5, para. 3. Nor did § 51-12-5.1(e)(2) violate the right to a jury trial guaranteed by Ga. Const. art. 1, § 1, para. 11. In short, appellees received a jury trial on the amount of punitive damages to which they were entitled, 25 percent of the amount that the jury believed would serve to punish the corporation and to deter its future conduct. Finally, § 51-12-5.1(e)(2) did not violate Ga. Const. art. 1, § 1, para. 12, which was never intended to provide an expansive right of "access to the courts" but was only intended to provide a "right of choice" between self-representation and representation by counsel.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

Mack Trucks v. Conkle


Nos. S93A0725, S93A0726


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 539; 436 S.E.2d 635; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 800; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 4126; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,723



November 22, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Action for damages; constitutional question. Spalding Superior Court. Before Judge Cramer. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 10-16-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 11-10-92. LOWER CT # :90SV268



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant truck manufacturer sought review of an award of punitive damages made to appellee truck driver following the trial of a products liability action in the Spalding Superior Court (Georgia). Appellant state sought review of the trial court's determination that Ga. Code Ann. § 51-12-5.1(e)(2), which required that 75 percent of appellee's punitive damages award be paid to the state, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee truck driver brought an action against appellant truck manufacturer and others on a products liability theory. The jury found that appellant truck manufacturer was negligent and awarded appellee compensatory and punitive damages. On appellee's motion, the trial court held unconstitutional Ga. Code Ann. § 51-12-5.1(e)(2), which required 75 percent of the punitive damages to have been paid to appellant state. Appellants sought review of both rulings, and the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that this was a products liability action sounding in negligence and that Ga. Code Ann. § 51-12-5.1(g), which capped the amount of punitive damages in strict liability actions, did not apply. The court also held that § 51-12-5.1(e)(2) was constitutional. The court said that Ga. Code Ann. § 51-12-5.1 set forth a comprehensive scheme that regulated punitive damages. The court found that § 51-12-5.1(e)(2) was not arbitrary and did not violate equal protection because, although the statute treated the defendants in various tort actions differently, it treated all similarly situated parties equally. The court held that the statute was not an unconstitutional taking.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an award of punitive damages to appellee truck driver after the trial of a products liability action against appellant truck manufacturer. The court reversed a decision that held unconstitutional a statute requiring that 75 percent of appellee's punitive damages be paid to appellant state. The court held that, although the statute treated various tort plaintiffs differently, it treated all similarly situated parties equally.

Keenan v. State


S93A1467


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


263 Ga. 569; 436 S.E.2d 475; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 801; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 4133



November 22, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ROCKDALE County State. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. William F. Todd, Jr. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 05-27-93. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 06-03-93. LOWER CT # :93SR1227



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment by the trial court (Georgia) which convicted and sentenced him of driving under the influence. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence of his post-arrest refusal to take the state-administered breath tests, contending the Implied Consent Law was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed finding defendant did not have standing to have challenged the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-67.1(g)(2) which limited the scope under Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-67.1(g) for hearings requested when one's driver's license was suspended by the department of public safety. The court held defendant's case was not one involving an administrative hearing but rather a criminal trial that determined defendant's guilt of driving under the influence. Thus, the court declined to address the constitutionality of a statute when a party whose rights were not affected by it challenged it. The court held under the Georgia Constitution a blood sample could have been lawfully taken from defendant without his consent as the Implied Consent Statute granted him an opportunity not afforded by the Georgia Constitution to refuse to take the test. Therefore, since defendant was given a right he otherwise did not have, such refusal was admissible. The court also held Miranda warnings were no required prior to the request to undergo the alco-sensor test, as he was not in custody and that the evidence was admissible and did not violate his Fifth Amendment right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for driving under the influence.

 

175 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Ga. Mental Health Inst. v. Brady


Nos. S93A0976, S93A0977


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 591; 436 S.E.2d 219; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 792; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 3957



November 8, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 2, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Equity. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Seeliger. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 03-04-93. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 03-04-93. LOWER CT # :9329805



DISPOSITION: Case No. S93A0976. Judgment affirmed. Case No. S93A0977. Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia) entered judgments for the appellee individual in the appellant state's appeal of a probate court decision denying the state's petition to involuntarily commit the individual to a psychiatric facility, and in the individual's petition for habeas corpus seeking release from the facility. The superior court also awarded the individual attorney fees. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state petitioned in the probate court for the involuntary commitment of the individual to a psychiatric treatment facility. The probate court denied the petition and ordered the state to immediately release the individual from the facility. The state appealed the probate court decision to the superior court and refused to release the individual on the grounds that it could continue to confine her while its appeal was pending. In response, the individual filed a petition for habeas corpus in the superior court. On the state's appeal from the superior court's judgment for the individual in the state's appeal, and in the habeas proceeding, the court affirmed. The court held that under Ga. Code Ann. § 37-2-150, the state had no right to appeal from a decision denying its petition for involuntary commitment, and that the state had no right to continue to restrain the individual after the probate court's decision. The court held that restraining the individual while the state's appeal was pending was a massive curtailment of liberty in violation of the individual's right to due process. The court reversed the superior court's award of attorney fees to the individual.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgments for the individual in the state's appeal from a probate court decision denying the state's petition to involuntarily commit the individual to a psychiatric facility, and on the individual's petition for habeas corpus. The court reversed an award of attorney fees to the individual.

 

176 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



State Bd. of Educ. v. Drury


Nos. S93A1226, S93X1227, S93A1228, S93X1230


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 429; 437 S.E.2d 290; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 698; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 3624



October 12, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 19, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 20-2-240 (a); constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Eldridge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed in Case Nos. S93A1226 and S93A1228. Judgment affirmed in Case Nos. S93X1227 and S93X1230.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs teachers filed suit against defendants, board of education (board), and board members individually, alleging violations of federal and state constitutional rights when they were denied renewable teaching certificates. The Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), granted summary judgment against the board but in favor of the board members. The teachers and the board challenged that judgment.


OVERVIEW: The board enacted a rule whereby teachers initially would be issued non-renewable teacher certificates, and in order to receive renewable teaching certificates they would be required to pass a performance assessment test. The teachers commenced the instant action after they failed the test and were denied renewable teaching certificates. The teachers argued that they had a property interest in their ability to engage in the teaching profession and that property interest was taken from them. The court found that the teachers had no property interest in the renewable teaching certificates because they were never issued to them. Therefore, the teachers received all the relief that they were entitled to when the board's rules which implemented the assessment test were held to be invalid and the teachers' eligibility to engage in the teaching profession was restored. Thus, they could not recover further damages from the board. As to the board members, the trial court correctly found that they had governmental immunity in their individual capacities for actions within the scope of their discretionary authority.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court against the board and affirmed the judgment in favor of the board members.

 

177 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Amalgamated Transit Union Local 1324 v. Roberts


Nos. S93G0081, S93G0132


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 405; 434 S.E.2d 450; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 622; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 3304



September 13, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 8, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: CHATHAM County SUPERIOR. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. James W. Head. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 09-28-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 10-02-92. LOWER CT # :X870424H.

Certiorari to the Court of Appeals of Georgia -- 205 Ga. App. 594.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, former employer and union, challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals of Georgia, which reversed a judgment for appellants and found in favor of appellee former employee in his breach of contract action that he filed after he was injured on the job and discharged. The appellate court held that the collateral source rule barred the admission of collateral source evidence in both tort and contract actions.


OVERVIEW: Appellee former employee was injured when an automobile struck the bus that he was operating. After appellant former employer discharged appellee, appellee requested that appellant union pursue a grievance. Appellant union refused to do so. In appellee's breach of contract action against appellants, the trial court found in favor of appellants. The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and found in favor of appellee. On appeal, the court reversed the appellate court's judgment. The court held that evidence of collateral payments was not absolutely barred by the collateral source rule in contract actions because the measure of damages would be a plaintiff's injury rather than a defendant's culpability. Thus, a jury was permitted to consider all facts when assessing breach of contract damages. Although the collateral evidence was not barred in appellee's action, the court did not determine whether it was or was not admissible as relevant to demonstrate that appellee's recovery would be limited to the amount of lost wages incurred as a result of the breach. The court found that appellee's sole contention that such evidence was absolutely barred was unavailing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and found in favor of appellants, former employer and union. Evidence of collateral payments was not absolutely barred by the collateral source rule in contract actions as it was in tort actions. The court did not determine whether the collateral evidence was admissible as relevant in appellee former employee's action because his sole contention that such evidence was absolutely barred was unavailing.

 

178 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Cline v. McMullan


No. S93A0140


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 321; 431 S.E.2d 368; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 520; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 2431



July 12, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 30, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Condemnation of land; constitutional question. Newton Superior Court. Before Judge Ott. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 08-10-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 10-20-92.LOWER CT # :9120110



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee landowner successfully petitioned to condemn a private right of way over the lands of appellant landowner. The board of assessors awarded damages to appellant for the value of the property. Appellee sought review in the Newton Superior Court (Georgia) but did not tender the amount of the award. Appellant filed a motion to dismiss the appeal, which the trial court denied. Appellant sought review of the denial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that appellee was required to tender the assessors' award as a condition precedent to filing the appeal. The court affirmed the denial and discussed the differences between eminent domain proceedings for public purposes and procedures to obtain a private way. The condemnor in a public purpose exercise of eminent domain obtained the right to enter use the property because the fact that a condemnor obtained title to the subject property would not change on appeal. In the private way action, appellant did not have the right to enter the land and put it to use before all appeals were exhausted and a final judgment was entered. The public purpose exercise, therefore, required tender of just compensation prior to filing an appeal, but the requirement was unnecessary in private way proceedings because the title did not pass until the trial court made a grant by final judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's motion to dismiss.

Bowman v. Knight


S93A0838


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


263 Ga. 222; 430 S.E.2d 582; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 493; 2 Am. Disabilities Cas. (BNA) 945; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 2190



June 21, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] WALTON County SUPERIOR. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Marvin W. Sorrells. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 12-03-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 02-01-93. LOWER CT # :911688S



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tractor trailer driver sought review of a judgment of the Walton County Superior Court (Georgia), which held that Department of Public Safety Regulation ch. 570-17-.02 was unconstitutional. The superior court ordered respondent, the commissioner of the Department of Public Safety, to return the driver's commercial driver's license.


OVERVIEW: The driver, an epileptic for 10 years, suffered an epileptic seizure, which was reported to the department by his employer. Pursuant to his medical history, the department suspended the driver's regular and commercial licenses to drive. The driver filed a de novo appeal that challenged the constitutionality of Department of Public Safety Regulation Ch. 570-17-.02, which provided for the review of individuals who suffered alterations of consciousness. The trial court found the regulation unconstitutional, and the department appealed. On review, the court reversed and held that the state had a legitimate interest in protecting the traveling public from accidents caused by individuals who suffered from epileptic seizures while driving. The difference in the treatment of Class C drivers and commercial drivers was based on the much greater potential for harm involved in the operation of commercial vehicles among other safety concerns. The court held that the difference in treatment was not arbitrary and bore a rational relationship to the legislative objective of protecting the public.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment, which held that the regulation was unconstitutional and ordered the return to the driver of his commercial license.

 

180 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Vlass v. Sec. Pac. Nat'l Bank


No. S93A0875


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 296; 430 S.E.2d 732; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 501; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 2270



June 21, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Foreclosure; constitutional question. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Hill. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 12-29-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 01-21-93. LOWER CT # :E7555



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor sought review of an order of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which confirmed appellee creditor's non-judicial foreclosure sale of the debtor's real property. The trial court rejected the debtor's challenge to the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 44-14-161 regarding service in confirmation proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The Civil Practice Act, Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-4, required service of a complaint filed in any civil action. Ga. Code Ann. § 44-14-161 did not expressly provide for service on the debtor of the creditor's application for confirmation, but required only that the debtor be given five days notice of the hearing. The trial court gave the debtor three weeks notice and entered judgment in favor of the creditor. On appeal, the debtor asserted that service of the creditor's application under Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-4 was a prerequisite to the initiation of confirmation under § 44-14-161 and that the denial of service violated equal protection. The court disagreed and affirmed. An application for confirmation was not a complaint, which initiated a civil action. Even though an application to confirm a foreclosure sale was a special statutory proceeding, it was not a "civil suit" because it did not result in a personal judgment or adjudicate the title of the property sold. Also, the debtor in a confirmation proceeding was not a defendant in a civil action. The debtor in a confirmation proceeding was in an entirely different class from a defendant in a civil action in which § 9-11-4 applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the confirmation of the creditor's non-judicial foreclosure sale of the debtor's real property.

 

181 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Fleet Fin. v. Jones


S93A0185


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


263 Ga. 228; 430 S.E.2d 352; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 487; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 2194



June 14, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] RICHMOND County SUPERIOR. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. William W. Fleming, Jr. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 09-04-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 10-16-92. LOWER CT # :92RCCV519



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lender sought review of an order by the Richmond County Superior Court (Georgia), which enjoined the lender from proceeding with any foreclosures against appellee debtors and granted the debtors' motion for class certification.


OVERVIEW: The debtors contended that the lender was charging usurious interest rates under Ga. Code Ann. § 7-4-18. Accordingly, the trial court enjoined the lender from proceeding with any foreclosures against the debtors and granted debtors' motion for class certification. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court on the issue of usurious rates because under the statutory scheme the lender's interpretation and calculation of interest rates was reasonable. The court found no rate of interest higher than 5 percent per month could have been charged. The lender contended that the calculation of the rate of interest must be made upon the ratio of total interest paid to the total number of months in the loan. The court concluded that this statute was subject to multiple interpretations, and § 7-4-18 was a criminal statute, therefore the court was required to adopt the interpretation most favorable to the lender. Lastly, the court found that the structure of the loans did not violate the statute as the debtors had fixed monthly payments, faced no threat of default at closing by the deduction of the points and origination fees, or through high interest charges in a given month.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment enjoining the lender from proceeding with any foreclosures against the debtors due to the possibility of the lender charging usurious interest rates on its loans.

S. J. T. v. Richmond County


S93A0496


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


263 Ga. 267; 430 S.E.2d 726; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 490; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 2191



June 14, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] RICHMOND County SUPERIOR. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. William W. Fleming, Jr. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 12-04-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 12-04-92. LOWER CT # :92RCCV910



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of a decision of the Richmond County Superior Court (Georgia) in favor of appellee county, refusing to enjoin enforcement of an ordinance prohibiting certain types of entertainment, attire, and conduct on premises licensed to sell, serve, or dispense alcohol beverages for consumption on the premises.


OVERVIEW: The county enacted an ordinance prohibiting nude dancing upon any premises licensed to sell alcohol. The trial court refused to enjoin enforcement of the ordinance and the court affirmed. The court noted that laws regulating nude dancing had have furthered an important government interest, been unrelated to the suppression of speech, and incidental restrictions on speech had to have been no greater than was essential to further the government interest. The court held that descriptions of prohibited attire in the ordinance were sufficiently narrow to pass constitutional muster. The court held that the ordinance was not vague because it permitted the corporation to conduct itself so as to avoid that which was forbidden. The court found that the restriction against alcohol had a rational relation to the proper legislative purpose of limiting the effects of combining public nudity with alcohol consumption. The court found that the ordinance did not violate equal protection because the effect of the ordinance was to classify adult entertainment establishments, which experience had shown to produce undesired secondary effects, differently than mainstream entertainment establishments.


OUTCOME: The court held for the county and against the corporation, affirming the judgment of the trial court which refused to enjoin enforcement of the ordinance.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of selling cocaine and sentenced to life in prison under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-13-30(d). OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and life sentence.

Barge-Wagener Constr. Co. v. Morales


S93A0252


SUPREME COURT OF GEORGIA


263 Ga. 190; 429 S.E.2d 671; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 456; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 1958



May 24, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] FULTON County SUPERIOR. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. Don A. Langham. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 08-28-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 10-09-92. LOWER CT # :E03875



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an employer and insurer, sought review of a judgment entered in the Superior Court of Fulton County (Georgia), which ruled in favor of appellees, decedent's dependents, who were nonresident aliens, and reversed the $ 1,000 benefit award made by the State Board of Workers' Compensation (Georgia) under Ga. Code Ann. § 34-9-265(b)(5). The superior court held that § 34-9-265(b)(5) violated the Equal Protection Clause.


OVERVIEW: The employer and insurer contended that the Board's benefit award was proper and that the superior court erred in finding § 34-9-265(b) unconstitutional. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court found that the legislature intended the rights to death benefits to vest in the dependents while making the burial expenses recoverable by the decedent's estate. The court concluded that the dependents were required to assert their own rights to the benefits and could not rely on the constitutional status of the decedent. Thus, the court held that the Equal Protection Clause did not extend to the dependents, who were nonresident aliens, and that Board correctly awarded death benefits under Ga. Stat. Ann. § 34-9-265(b)(5). However, the court held that the right to reasonable burial expenses under Ga. Stat. Ann. § 34-9-265(b) belonged to decedent's estate. Thus, the denial of burial expenses to decedent because of his alienage or the alienage of his family was an arbitrary exercise of the law in violation of the Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: The court found that the limitations on death benefits did not violate the equal protection clause of the Georgia Constitution. The denial of burial expenses to the estate of decedent worker, however, was reversed.

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor sought review of an order of the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia), which granted partial summary judgment to appellees, injured mother and child, and precluded seat belt usage evidence under Ga. Philmore v. State


No. S93A0020


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 67; 428 S.E.2d 329; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 376; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 1682



April 19, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Glynn Superior Court. Before Judge Tuten. DATE OF JUDGEMENT APPEALED: 08-05-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 08-10-92. LOWER CT#:9100894



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Glynn Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of felony murder, aggravated assault with a deadly weapon, aggravated assault with intent to rob, and attempted possession of marijuana with intent to distribute, and sentenced him to life imprisonment as a recidivist.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of felony murder, aggravated assault with a deadly weapon, aggravated assault with intent to rob, and attempted possession of marijuana with intent to distribute, and was sentenced to life imprisonment as a recidivist. Upon review the court affirmed the convictions and the sentence. The court held that substantial evidence supported the verdict and thus the jury was authorized to find beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was guilty of the charged crimes. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion for mistrial based upon remarks made during the state's closing argument. The court held that it was not improper for the prosecutor to appeal to the jury send a message to others that criminal activities would not go unpunished. The court held that defendant was properly sentenced as a recidivist under Ga. Code Ann. § 17-10-7 (b). The court held that all of the convictions were the result of separate indictments and a separate order of sentence was entered on each indictment. Thus, the prior convictions had not been "consolidated for trial" within the meaning of § 17-10-7(c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence for felony murder, aggravated assault with a deadly weapon, aggravated assault with intent to rob, and attempted possession of marijuana with intent to distribute.

Allen v. State


No. S93A0436


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 60; 428 S.E.2d 73; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 359; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 1602



April 12, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] COBB County SUPERIOR. TRIAL JUDGE: Hon. James G. Bodiford. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 07-15-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 07-23-92. LOWER CT #: 919128704



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Cobb County Superior Court (Georgia) convicting him of child molestation, aggravated child molestation, and cruelty to children.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged: (1.) the child hearsay statute, Ga. Code Ann. § 24-3-16, was unconstitutional; (2.) the trial court erred in admitting portions of an audio tape of his statements to the police because they were prejudicial; and (3.) he received ineffective assistance of counsel. In affirming defendant's convictions, the court found that the child hearsay statute was repeatedly upheld as constitutional. The portions of the audio tape were properly admitted. During one portion of the tape, a questioning detective told defendant that the victim described the molestation in detail. During the molestation, defendant told the victim that he had done it to his daughter and she enjoyed it. This portion was admissible as evidence of motive, scheme, design, or method of operation of defendant. In another portion of the tape, defendant claimed that his wife was accusing him of doing drugs in order to gain custody of their daughter. The statement was not an admission that defendant used drugs, and he volunteered the information. Defendant did not prove that defense counsel was so ineffective to deny him a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant businesses sought an injunction against enforcement of a nude dancing ordinance enacted by appellee city. The Superior Court (Georgia) denied the injunction and the businesses appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an ordinance that restricted "nude" dancing and imposed licensing restrictions on nude dancers and the establishments they worked in. The trial court denied the injunctive relief sought by the businesses.
