OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment holding the city's nude dancing ordinance constitutional was reversed.

 

190 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Fisch v. Randall Mill Corp.


No. S92A1223


Supreme Court of Georgia


262 Ga. 861; 426 S.E.2d 883; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 316; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 1158



March 15, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Mineral rights. Fulton Superior Court. Before Judge Alverson. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 01-29-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 02-26-92. LOWER CT#:D73545



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant appealed a decision of the Fulton Superior Court (Georgia), which denied his motion for summary judgment and granted summary judgment to defendant corporation in an action over mineral rights.


OVERVIEW: The corporation filed a petition for declaratory judgment that it had absolute title to all mineral rights on its property because no one had attempted to work the mineral rights or paid taxes on them for seven years. The claimant, a descendant of the owner of the property, contended that he had attempted to work the minerals by walking the property and collecting rock samples for analysis. He also contended that he made several trips to the courthouse to try to pay the taxes but the commissioner would not assess taxes. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment. The trial court granted summary judgment to the corporation, and the claimant appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the claimant's acts did not constitute working or attempting to work his mineral rights and the owner of a mineral interest had to do more than conduct genealogical research and pick up rock samples to meet the statutory requirement of working or attempting to work the mineral rights. The court also held that if the tax commissioner failed to assess taxes on his interest, the claimant should have filed a writ of mandamus to compel the commissioner to act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the corporation in an action it filed for declaratory judgment as to its absolute rights to mineral interests that were disputed by the claimant.

 

191 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Gwinn v. State Ethics Com


No. S92A1177


Supreme Court of Georgia


262 Ga. 855; 426 S.E.2d 890; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 318; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 1260



March 15, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 21-5-30.1; constitutional question. Cobb Superior Court. Before Judge Brantley. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 02-11-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 05-08-92. LOWER CT#:911347906



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an insurer and its president, sought review of the judgment of the Cobb Superior Court (Georgia), which upheld the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 21-5-30.1(b) against the insurer's and its president's contentions that it violated their constitutionally-protected freedom of speech and was a denial of due process and equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Appellee State Ethics Commission determined that the insurer and its president violated § 21-5-30.1 by placing a full-page newspaper ad supporting the candidacy of the incumbent insurance commissioner who was seeking re-election. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of the statute. The court affirmed, holding that § 21-5-30.1(b) was not an unconstitutional infringement upon the freedom of speech as guaranteed by the constitutions of the United States and Georgia because the prohibition against making a campaign contribution to the commissioner of insurance or a candidate for that office did burden expressive activity, but the state justified the burden by establishing that the prevention of corruption or the appearance of corruption through campaign contributions was a legitimate and compelling governmental interest that permitted the absolute prohibition of campaign contributions from a regulated entity to the regulator or a candidate for the office of regulator. Additionally, the legislative infringement on freedom of speech was narrowly tailored to achieve the compelling state interest because the regulated entity was free to contribute to all other political campaigns.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment which upheld the constitutionality of the statute which prohibited the insurer from making a campaign contribution to the commissioner of insurance or a candidate for that office.

 

192 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Hill v. State


No. S92P1336


Supreme Court of Georgia


263 Ga. 37; 427 S.E.2d 770; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 315; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 1172



March 15, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 30, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Lee Superior Court. Before Judge Blanks. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 06-11-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 07-10-92. LOWER CT # :91R14



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Lee Superior Court (Georgia), which entered a judgment convicting him of murder and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant bludgeoned a fellow prison inmate to death. He contended on appeal that the trial court erred in the handling of motions to recuse and to adjourn, that the death penalty laws were unconstitutional, that the trial court erred by excusing two prospective jurors, that there was racial discrimination in the prosecutor's exercise of peremptory challenges, and that the prosecutor argued improperly during sentencing. The court affirmed the judgment. The court determined that the trial was not unfairly expedited through long sessions or truncated arguments and examinations. The court stated that the death penalty laws were not unconstitutional for any reason alleged. The court found no error in excusing the jurors because of their beliefs on the death penalty. The court determined that the trial court was authorized to conclude that the prosecutor had overcome the accusation of discrimination in the use of peremptory challenges. The court did not find the prosecutor's religious references sufficiently prejudicial to overcome failure to raise the issue at trial. The court found the death sentence neither excessive nor disproportionate to sentences imposed in similar cases.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant and sentencing him to death.

 

193 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Lutz v. Foran


Nos. S92A1068, S92X1069


Supreme Court of Georgia


262 Ga. 819; 427 S.E.2d 248; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 283; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 863



March 8, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended March 9, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 9-11-9.1; constitutional question. Chatham State Court. Before Judge Mikell, pro hac vice. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 04-08-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 04-20-92. LOWER CT # :912459M



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in Case No. S92A1068; reversed in Case No. S92X1069 and remanded with direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a shrimp boat owner and a salvage equipment owner, sought review of the judgment of the State Court of Chatham County (Georgia), which granted defendant harbor pilot's motion to dismiss their complaint for property damage because of the failure to attach a professional malpractice affidavit required by Ga. Code Ann. § 9-11-9.1.


OVERVIEW: The harbor pilot operated a ship, which struck and damaged a sunken shrimp boat beyond repair. The shrimp boat had been raised to within five feet of the river's surface as part of a salvage operation. The shrimp boat owner and the salvage equipment owner sued the harbor pilot for negligence based upon his failure to control his vessel and his causing the collision. The harbor pilot filed a motion to dismiss because an expert affidavit was not attached to the complaint in compliance with § 9-11-9.1. The trial court ordered the dismissal of the complaint. The court held that the shrimp boat owner was required to file an expert affidavit with the complaint because conducting an ocean-going ship in the river called for the professional skills of the harbor pilot. The court held that the shrimp boat owner was entitled to a reasonable time to file the appropriate affidavit because he did not have the benefit of the court's earlier decision, which delineated the professionals against whom an expert affidavit had to be filed in accordance with § 9-11-9.1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of one action by the trial court, and reversed and remanded the dismissal of the second action with directions that the trial court give the shrimp boat owner a reasonable time to file the appropriate affidavit.

 

194 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Land v. State


No. S92A1307


Supreme Court of Georgia


262 Ga. 898; 426 S.E.2d 370; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 257; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 766



February 25, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 18, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: O.C.G.A. § 16-11-31 (a); constitutional question. Hall State Court. Before Judge Gosselin. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: December 11, 1991. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: December 12, 1991. LOWER CT#:91SR3178D



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Hall State Court (Georgia) of inciting a riot under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-11-31(a). Defendant challenged the constitutionality of § 16-11-31(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of incitement to riot under Ga. Code Ann. § 16-11-31 for standing in a public street in front of an apartment building full of Hispanics, dressed in the ceremonial garb of the Ku Klux Klan, and pointing his finger and yelling. When officers arrived, the situation was very tense. The court affirmed, first, because § 16-11-31 met defendant's vagueness challenge. It provided fair warning to persons of ordinary intelligence as to what it prohibited. Second, the statute was not overbroad. Third, the state presented sufficient evidence to authorize the jury to have found defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. Fourth, defendant's right to free speech was not infringed. Because his conduct constituted inciting to riot, his speech was not afforded any constitutional protection. Fifth, the admission of hearsay was harmless error. Sixth, the condition of his probation forbidding him from participating in Klan activities did not violate his First Amendment right to freedom of association because it was tied to the rehabilitative purpose of his probationary sentence, and his loss of rights was rationally related to the purpose underlying the sentencing objective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for incitement to riot.

 

195 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Brantley v. State


No. S92P1127


Supreme Court of Georgia


262 Ga. 786; 427 S.E.2d 758; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 263; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 770



February 25, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Murder. Burke Superior Court. Before Judge Fleming. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED June 3, 1992. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: June 8, 1992. LOWER CT#: 89R43



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Burke Superior Court (Georgia), which convicted him of two murders and aggravated assault, burglary, and a firearms possession charge, and sentenced him to death on one of the two murders.


OVERVIEW: After defendant learned of an extra-marital affair his wife was having, he went to her mother's house where he shot his wife, her sister, and her mother. The wife and sister were killed, and the mother was injured. Thereafter, defendant was convicted of the murders, aggravated assault, burglary, and a firearm possession charge, and sentenced to death on one of the two murders. He appealed. The court affirmed the convictions but reversed the death sentence imposed for the murder of the sister-in-law and remanded for resentencing. Defendant alleged numerous errors none of which the court found reversible. The court concluded that although the trial court did not explicitly impose a unanimity requirement on the jury's mitigation findings, its instructions contained numerous reminders to the jury that its findings needed to be unanimous. The court found that requiring a written finding on mitigating circumstances, signed by the foreperson, implicitly imposed a unanimity requirement on mitigating circumstances. The court concluded that a unanimity requirement on mitigating circumstances was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions but reversed the death sentenced imposed for the murder of defendant's sister-in-law and remanded for resentencing.

 

196 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Poole v. State


No. S92A1218


Supreme Court of Georgia


262 Ga. 718; 425 S.E.2d 655; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 189; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 490



February 8, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] O.C.G.A. § 16-10-1; constitutional question. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Mallis. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 05-21-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 05-21-92. LOWER CT#:92CR111



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, upon a jury verdict, for violating his oath as a public officer from the DeKalb Superior Court (Georgia), challenging, for vagueness, the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 16-10-1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a police officer, was convicted of the felony of violating his oath as a public officer by pawning a handgun that had been confiscated during an automobile stop. On appeal, defendant argued that Ga. Code Ann. §16-10-1, as applied to him and read in conjunction with his oath as a police officer, was unconstitutionally void for vagueness. The court rejected the argument and affirmed defendant's conviction. Although the language of the oath that required defendant to demean himself as a police officer and to act for the best interest of the city was arguably vague, defendant could not reasonably have been surprised that his conduct violated his sworn duty as a police officer. The court concluded that defendant's conduct was so far outside the realm of acceptable police behavior that he had adequate notice that he could have been prosecuted for the conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for violating his oath as a public officer.

 

197 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Van Dyck v. Van Dyck


No. S92A1279


Supreme Court of Georgia


262 Ga. 720; 425 S.E.2d 853; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 198; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 405



February 8, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Granted interlocutory application. DeKalb Superior Court. Before Judge Hunter. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 05-04-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 06-18-92. LOWER CT#:91119048



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-wife sought review of an order from the DeKalb County Superior Court (Georgia), which, in an action brought by appellee ex-husband to modify his alimony obligation under Ga. Code Ann. § 19-6-19 on the ground that his ex-wife was cohabiting with a person of the same sex in which she was engaged in a meretricious relationship, denied the ex-wife's motion to dismiss the ex-husband's complaint for modification.


OVERVIEW: The ex-husband filed his motion for modification because the ex-wife was cohabiting with a person of the same sex as the ex-wife in a meretricious relationship. The ex-wife filed a motion to dismiss the complaint and the trial court denied the motion. On review the court found that Ga. Code Ann. § 19-6-19(b) provided that such a relationship was grounds to modify the payment of alimony in the event of cohabitation with a third party in a meretricious relationship. The court held that the word cohabitation meant dwelling together continuously and openly in a meretricious relationship with a person of the opposite sex. The court held that the plain language of the statute did not apply when the former spouse was involved in a homosexual relationship. In light of the clear and unambiguous language of the statute, the trial court was not authorized to construe the language of the statute otherwise. The court held that if the legislature intended the statute to allow modification in such a circumstance, it was the duty of the legislature rather than the courts to amend the statute. The court finally held that the statute did not violate the Fourteenth Amendment of the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of the ex-wife's motion to dismiss the complaint to modify alimony because the plain language of the statute indicated that it did not apply to meretricious cohabitation by members of the same sex.

 

198 of 1995 DOCUMENTS



Griggs v. State


No. S92A1091


Supreme Court of Georgia


262 Ga. 766; 425 S.E.2d 644; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 184; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 500



February 5, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 24, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Murder. Early Superior Court. Before Judge Crosby from Tifton Circuit. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 10-16-91. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 11-12-91. LOWER CT # :199



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for murder from Early Superior Court (Georgia). Defendant had been granted the right to appeal out of time due to a writ of habeas corpus issued by a circuit court.


OVERVIEW: When defendant was tried for murder, his counsel was also his codefendant's counsel. Defendant was convicted of murder. Later, the superior court granted defendant a writ of habeas corpus and reinstated his right to appeal. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that the trial court did not err based on the law as it then existed in not instructing the jury on voluntary manslaughter even though defendant did not request such a charge. The trial court also did not err in excluding evidence of the victim's propensity for violence. When the evidence was tendered, there had been no prima facie showing of the victim's reputation and propensity for violence. Neither did Ga. Code Ann. § 38-416 as it then existed preclude his getting a fair trial even though the statute was later declared unconstitutional. Section 38-416, which precluded defendant from testifying under oath in his own behalf, did not preclude a fair trial, given the other evidence. Defendant failed to show a conflict of interest in his being represented by his codefendant's attorney. There was no error in not granting a new trial on newly discovered evidence because the affidavits failed to meet requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder.

 

199 of 1995 DOCUMENTS


Quiller v. Bowman


No. S92A1427


Supreme Court of Georgia


262 Ga. 769; 425 S.E.2d 641; 1993 Ga. LEXIS 188; 93 Fulton County D. Rep. 489; 18 A.L.R.5th 1051



February 5, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 24, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Granted discretionary application. Upson Superior Court. Before Judge English. DATE OF JUDGMENT APPEALED: 06-03-92. NOTICE OF APPEAL DATE: 08-03-92. LOWER CT # :92V199



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted petitioner driver's discretionary application for review of a judgment of the Upson Superior Court (Georgia), which upheld the constitutionality of Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-75, requiring the suspension of the driver's license of any person convicted of the possession of a controlled substance or marijuana. The driver contended that the statute violated his constitutional rights to due process and equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The driver was convicted and sentenced for possessing controlled substances on facts not involving a motor vehicle. The state notified him that his driver's license was suspended indefinitely, but could be reinstated if he completed an approved drug use risk reduction program. The license suspension was upheld based on Ga. Code Ann. § 40-5-75, which the superior court found constitutional. On discretionary review, the driver argued that the statute violated substantive due process and equal protection by requiring driver's license suspensions even for drug offenses not involving motor vehicles. The court affirmed, holding that the state's desire to ensure safe driving and discourage illegal drug use was reasonably related to mandatory suspension of driver's licenses and attendance at a drug reduction program, even if the offense did not involve a motor vehicle. The driver argued that the statute impermissibly distinguished between persons convicted of drug possession and those convicted of other crimes. The court disagreed and held that the distinction bore a reasonable relationship to the purpose of deterring drug use, curtailing drug distribution, and protecting motorists.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding the constitutionality of the Georgia statute that required the suspension of any person's driver's license if convicted of possession of a controlled substance or marijuana.
